Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
12 min
Hajj: Definition, Historical Obligation, and Required Permissions
Opening of Kitab al-Hajj defining Hajj and discussing obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of Hajj, identify the year it became obligatory (6 AH), and explain the rules of seeking permission from parents, creditors, and istikhara before undertaking Hajj.

Core Idea
Hajj is fard ayn only on this Ummah, made obligatory in 6 AH; requires permission from parents if they need you and a father may prevent a handsome-faced son from travel.

This lesson opens the Book of Hajj in Hashiyat al-Tahtawi. It defines the pilgrimage linguistically and legally, settles the historical debate on when it became obligatory, and then discusses important social conditions for fulfilling this obligation, including parental permission and the special case of a handsome young man. Understanding these rules ensures that the act of worship is performed correctly and in a manner that avoids harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and legal nature of Hajj
Read the Arabic definition: 'ziyaratu biqa'in makhsusatin bif'lin makhsusin fi ashhurihi'. Note that linguistically it means 'intending a great thing' and legally it is a visit to specific places with specific actions in specific months (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and ten of Dhu al-Hijjah).
This definition sets the scope of the act.
2
Recognize the Hanafi view on obligation for previous nations
The text states that the correct view is that Hajj was not obligatory on previous nations, only on this Ummah. This is a critical refinement against those who thought it was always obligatory.
This is a point of legal history (usul).
3
Review the differing opinions on the year of obligation
The author lists several opinions: year 5, 6, 9, 10 AH; also before Hijrah. The famous and correct view according to the text is year 6 AH. This is supported by hadith from Bukhari and Darqutni.
The dalil from Zaid ibn Arqam and Jabir is used to argue for after Hijrah.
4
Apply the rules of permission from parents, creditors, and istikhara
The text discusses that one intending Hajj should seek permission from parents if they need his service; otherwise he sins. Grandparents take their place. A father may prevent a handsome-faced son even if not needed for service, to avoid fitna. Permission from debt-holder and guarantor is also advised. Istikhara is recommended for travel decisions but not for obligatory, disliked, or forbidden acts.
These are conditions for undertaking the journey, not conditions of the obligation itself.
5
Note the exception and the duty of repentance
The passage ends with advising to begin with repentance, indicating that purity of intention is essential before embarking on Hajj.
Repentance is a spiritual condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج هو زيارة بقاع مخصوصة بفعل مخصوص في أشهره وهي شوال وذو القعدة، وعشر الحاء كتاب الحج وكسرها لغة القصد إلى معظم لا مطلق القصد كما ظنه بعضهم در واختلف بفتح هل كان في شريعة من قبلنا واجباً أم لا، والصحيح أنه لم يجب إلا على هذه الأمة، وفي حاشية العلامة نوح اختلف العلماء في السنة التي فرض فيها الحج والمشهور أنها سنة ست، وهو الصحيح وقيل : سنة خمس وقيل سنة تسع وصححه القاضي عياض، وقيل: فرض قبل الهجرة وهو بعيد وأبعد منه قول بعضهم أنه فرض سنة عشر أخرج البخاري عن زيد بن أرقم : أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حج بعدما هاجر حجة واحدة، وأخرج الدارقطني عن جابر بن عبد الله قال : حج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثلاث حجج حجتين قبل أن يهاجر وحجة قرن بها عمرة، وكانت حجته بعدما هاجر سنة عشر، وحج أبو بكر الصديق في السنة التي قبلها سنة تسع، وأما سنة ثمان، وهي عام الفتح فحج بالناس قبلها عتاب بن أسيد ا هـ، وهو الذي ولاه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أميراً بمكة بعد الفتح، وذكر مثلا علي أنه لا حج قبل أن يهاجر حججاً لا يعلم عددها، وقال ابن الأثير : كل سنة قبل أن يهاجر يعني إلا أن يمنع منه مانع وينبغي لمريد الحج، أو الغزو أن يستأذن أبويه فإن خرج بدون أذن . الاحتياج إليه للخدمة أثم وقيل : يكره والأجداد، والجدات كالأبوين عند فقدهما، وللأب منعه إذا كان صبيح الوجه حتى يلتحي وإن استغنى عن خدمته كذا يستفاد من النوازل وفي الفتاوى الغلام إذا كان صبيح الوجه لا يخرجه الأب من بيته، وإن كان بالغاً كما لا يخرج بنته لأن البنت يشتهيها الرجال فقط، والأمرد إن كان صبيح الوجه يشتهيه الرجال والنساء معاً فالفتنة فيه من الجانبين، وينبغي أن يستأذن رب الدين، والكفيل ويستخير في هل يشتري أو يكتري، وهل يسافر براً، أو بحراً، وهل يرافق فلاناً أو فلاناً لأن الاستخارة في الواجب والمكروه والحرام لا محل لها نهر، ويبدأ بالتوبة مراعياً
Book of Hajj. It is visiting specific places with specific actions in its months, which are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and ten of Dhu al-Hijjah. The letter Ha, Book of Hajj, with kasr means linguistically intending a great thing, not absolute intending as some thought. There is disagreement about whether it was obligatory in the law of those before us, and the correct view is that it was not made obligatory except upon this Ummah. In the footnote of Allamah Nuh, scholars differed about the year in which Hajj was made obligatory. The famous view is the year six, and that is the correct one. It is said: year five, and it is said: year nine, and Qadi Iyad corrected it. It is said: made obligatory before Hijrah, which is far-fetched, and further from that is some saying it was made obligatory in year ten. Al-Bukhari narrated from Zaid ibn Arqam that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed Hajj once after he emigrated. Al-Daraqutni narrated from Jabir ibn Abdullah who said: The Messenger of Allah performed three Hajjs, two before Hijrah and one with an Umrah, and his Hajj after Hijrah was in year ten. Abu Bakr al-Siddiq performed Hajj in the year before that, year nine. As for year eight, which is the year of the Conquest, the people were led in Hajj before that by 'Attab ibn Asid, may Allah be pleased with him, whom the Prophet appointed governor of Mecca after the Conquest. And the example mentioned from 'Ali that he did not perform Hajj before Hijrah, Hajjs whose number is not known. And Ibn al-Athir said: every year before Hijrah he meant, unless prevented. One who intends Hajj or military expedition should seek permission from his parents, for if he goes out without permission while they need his service, he sins, and it is said: it is disliked. Grandfathers and grandmothers are like parents in their absence. The father may prevent him if he is handsome-faced until he grows a beard, even if he does not need his service. This is understood from al-Nawazil. And in al-Fatawa: if a boy is handsome-faced, the father should not let him out of his house, even if he is adult, just as he does not let out his daughter because men desire the daughter only, but the beardless boy is desired by both men and women, so the trial is from both sides. He should also seek permission from the debt-holder and the guarantor, and he should perform istikhara about whether to buy or rent, whether to travel by land or sea, whether to accompany so-and-so or so-and-so, because istikhara has no place in obligatory, disliked, or forbidden acts. He should begin with repentance, being careful.
Source pages p. 726

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Hajj in Hashiyat al-Tahtawi. It defines Hajj linguistically and legally, stating its months. A key discussion is whether Hajj was obligatory upon previous nations; the correct Hanafi view is that it was made obligatory only for this Ummah. The text then details scholarly opinions on the year Hajj was made obligatory: the famous view is 6 AH, supported by hadith from Bukhari and Darqutni. The passage also covers the permissibility of delaying Hajj, and importantly, the requirement to seek permission from parents before undertaking Hajj (or jihad) if they need one's service. Special attention is given to the case of a handsome-faced boy or young man, where the father may prevent him even from Hajj to avoid fitna. Permission from creditors and guarantors is also advised. Istikhara is recommended for travel decisions, but not for actions that are inherently obligatory, disliked, or forbidden. The passage concludes with the reminder to begin with repentance.

Key Terms
حج (hajj): Visiting specific places (Makkah, Arafat, etc.) with specific actions in specific months.
صبيح الوجه (sabih al-wajh): A person (male) with a handsome, attractive face, considered a source of fitna.
استخارة (istikharah): Seeking guidance from Allah through prayer when choosing between permissible options.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many Hajjs did the Prophet (peace be upon him) perform after the Hijrah?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Hajj is fard ayn only on this Ummah, made obligatory in 6 AH; it requires fulfilling conditions including parental permission and absence of fitna for a handsome-faced son.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Definition and Obligation of Hajj: Fawr vs Tarakhi
Matn plus hashya: definition and obligation with internal Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of hajj and explain why the obligation is immediate (fawr) according to the preferred view.

Core Idea
Hajj is a defined ritual with an immediate obligation: delaying without reason incurs sin, yet the act remains ada.

This lesson opens Kitab al-Hajj with the classical Hanafi definition: hajj is the visitation of specific places with specific actions in specific months. The text then declares hajj obligatory once in a lifetime, immediately upon ability. We will examine the internal Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf (fawr) and Muhammad (tarakhi) and understand the unique usuli concept of time as both a measure and a container.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of hajj
Locate the phrase 'زيارة بقاع مخصوصة بفعل مخصوص في أشهره' and note the three elements: specific places (Kaaba and Arafat), specific actions (ihram, tawaf, wuquf), and specific months (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah).
The definition establishes the legal reality of hajj.
2
State the ruling and its timing
Find the statement 'فرض مرة على الفور في الأصح' and parse its components: fard (obligatory), marratan (once in a lifetime), ala al-fawr (immediately), fi al-ashah (according to the most correct view).
The phrase 'fi al-ashah' signals a preferred view within the school.
3
Analyze the fawr-tarakhi dispute
Read the commentary: Abu Yusuf holds fawr (immediate), Muhammad holds tarakhi (within lifetime). Note the consequences: under fawr, delay without excuse makes one a sinner and rejects testimony, but eventual hajj is ada; under tarakhi, no sin for delay but sin if death occurs without performing.
The dispute is practical: when does sin attach? Both agree hajj must be performed before death.
4
Understand time as 'mushkil'
Review the usuli explanation: the time of hajj has two aspects – as a measure (mi'yar) and as a container (zarf). The fawr view emphasizes measure; tarakhi emphasizes container. This clarifies why ada/qada classification differs.
This is a unique Hanafi usul analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
هو زيارة بقاع مخصوصة بفعل مخصوص في أشهره وهي شوال وذو القعدة، وعشر ذي الحجة فرض مرة على الفور في الأصح، وشروط فرضيته ثمانية على الأصح الإسلام، والعقل والبلوغ، والحرية والوقت والقدرة على الزاد ولو بمكة بنفقة وسط والقدرة على راحلة مختصة به، أو على شق محمل بالملك، أو الإجارة لا الإباحة، والإعارة لغير أهل نفسه
قوله: (بقاع مخصوصة) هي الكعبة وعرفات قوله : (بفعل مخصوص بأن يكون محرماً بنية الحج سابقاً، وطائفاً في زمن من ابتداء طلوع فجر النحر، ويمتد إلى آخر العمر واقفاً في زمن من زوال يوم عرفة إلى طلوع فجر النحر قوله : (وهي شوال الخ) فائدة التوقيت بها أنه لو فعل شيئاً من أفعال الحج خارجها لا يجزيه، وأنه يكره الإحرام قبلها، وإن أمن على من المحظور لشبهه بالركن وإطلاقها يفيد التحريم .در قوله : (وذو القعدة) بفتح وكسرها درر. قوله : (فرض مرة على الفور) عند أبي يوسف وفي العمر عند محمد اعلم أن وقت الحج في اصطلاح الأصوليين يسمى مشكلاً لأنّ فيه جهة المعيارية والظرفية، فمن قال : بالفور لا يقول : بأن من أخره عن العام الأول يكون فعله قضاء، ومن قال بالتراخي لا يقول بأن من أخره لا يأثم أصلاً كما إذا أخر الصلاة عن الوقت الأول ، بل جهة المعيارية راجحة عند القائل بالفور حتى أن من أخر يفسق، وترد شهادته لكن إذا حج بالأخرة كان أداء لا قضاء وجهة الظرفية راجحة عند القائل بخلافه حتى إذا أداه بعد العام الأول، لا يأثم بالتأخير، لكن لو مات، ولم يحج أثم أيضاً عنده .در قوله : (الإسلام) فلا يجب على الكافر حتى لو ملك ما به الاستطاعة، ثم أسلم بعد ما افتقر لا يجب عليه شيء بتلك الاستطاعة بخلاف ما لو ملكه مسلماً، فلم يحج حتى افتقر حيث يتقرر وجوبه ديناً في ذمته ذكره العلامة نوح عن الفتح، وهذا على أن الكفار غير مخاطبين بفروع الشريعة وقال العراقيون، بخاطبهم: فيكون على قولهم من شرائط الصحة قوله : (والعقل والبلوغ والحرية إنما اشترطت هذه لما روي عن ابن عباس قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : أيما صبي حج ثم بلغ الحنث فعليه أن يحج حجة أخرى وأيما أعرابي حج ، ثم هاجر فعليه أن يحج حجة أخرى وأيما عبد حج، ثم أعتق فعليه أن يحج حجة أخرى، واعلم أنه لا يجب عليه وأن أذن له مولاه فلو حج بإذن مولاه، أو بغيره لا يقع عن حجة الإسلام، أفاده العلامة نوح قوله : (والوقت) أي وقت الطواف، والوقوف ويحتمل أن المراد الوقت الذي يحصل فيه الحج، وهو يختلف باختلاف البلدان. قوله: (والقدرة على الزاد الذي يصح به بدنه فالمعتاد للحلو ونحوه إذا قدر على خبز وجبن يعد قادراً در . قوله : (بنفقة وسط) أي من غير إسراف ولا تقتير قوله : على راحلة مخصة به) فإن لم يقدر على ركوب المقتب اشترط القدرة على المحارة قال صاحب البحر عند ذكر الراحلة أنه لو قدر على غير الراحلة من بغل أو حمار لم يجب، ولم أره وإنما صرحوا بالكراهة قال أبو السعود
The Book of Hajj. It is the visitation of specific places with specific actions in its months, which are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the ten (days) of Dhu al-Hijjah. It is obligatory once immediately (ala al-fawr) according to the most correct view. The conditions of its obligation are eight according to the most correct view: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, time, and the ability for provisions even if in Makkah with moderate expenditure, and the ability for a mount specific to him, or (to sit) on the side of a howdah (shiqq mahmil) by ownership or hire, not by permission, and (the ability for) a loan for other than the person himself.

His saying: “Specific places” – they are the Kaaba and Arafat. His saying: “by specific action” – that one be in ihram with the intention of hajj beforehand, a circumambulating one in a time from the beginning of the dawn of the Day of Sacrifice, extending to the end of one’s life, a standing one in a time from the decline of the sun on the Day of Arafah to the dawn of the Day of Sacrifice. His saying: “and they are Shawwal, etc.” – the benefit of specifying them is that if one performs any act of hajj outside them, it does not suffice; and that it is disliked to enter ihram before them, even if one is safe from prohibitions, due to its resemblance to the pillar; and its unrestricted (mention) indicates prohibition. Durr. His saying: “and Dhu al-Qa'dah” – with fatḥ and kasr (of the letter). Durar. His saying: “obligatory once immediately (fard marratan ala al-fawr)” – according to Abu Yusuf, and during the lifetime according to Muhammad. Know that the time of Hajj in the terminology of the usuliyyun is called “mushkil” because it has the aspect of measure (mi‘yariyyah) and circumstance (zarfiyyah). Whoever says it is immediate does not say that delaying it past the first year makes it a qada; and whoever says it is lax (tarakhi) does not say that delaying it entails no sin at all, as if one delays prayer beyond its first time; rather, the aspect of measure is preponderant for those who say immediate, so much so that one who delays becomes a transgressor and his testimony is rejected, yet if he eventually performs hajj, it is ada, not qada; and the aspect of circumstance is preponderant for those who differ, so that if he performs it after the first year, he does not sin for the delay, but if he dies without having performed hajj, he sins according to him as well. Durr. His saying: “Islam” – it is not obligatory upon the disbeliever; even if he possesses means, then becomes Muslim after having lost wealth, nothing is due upon him from that means, unlike if he possessed it as a Muslim and did not perform hajj until he became poor, the obligation becomes established as a debt in his liability. This is mentioned by Allamah Nuh from al-Fath. And this is on the view that the disbelievers are not addressed with the branches of Shari'a; but the Iraqis say they are addressed, so according to them it is a condition of validity. His saying: “and sanity, puberty, freedom” – these are only stipulated due to what is related from Ibn Abbas: he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: “Any child who performs hajj then reaches the age of obligation, he must perform another hajj; and any Bedouin who performs hajj then migrates (hajara), he must perform another hajj; and any slave who performs hajj then is freed, he must perform another hajj.” And know that it is not obligatory upon him even if his master permits; so if he performs hajj with his master’s permission or otherwise, it does not count as the hajj of Islam (hajjat al-Islam). This is stated by Allamah Nuh. His saying: “and time” – i.e., the time of tawaf and wuquf; and it is possible that it means the time in which hajj takes place, and it varies by country. His saying: “and ability for provisions that sustain his body” – so one accustomed to sweets and the like, if he is able to have bread and cheese, he is considered able. Durr. His saying: “with moderate expenditure” – i.e., without extravagance nor miserliness. His saying: “on a mount specific to him” – if he is unable to ride the miqtab (small camel saddle), the ability to ride the mahara (large camel saddle) is required. The author of al-Bahr said regarding the mention of the mount: if he is able to ride other than a mount, such as a mule or donkey, it is not obligatory; I have not seen (this), and they only declared it disliked. Abu al-Sa'ud said.
Source pages p. 726

Commentary
This passage is the opening of Kitab al-Hajj from the matn of Maraqi al-Falah along with the hashya commentary of al-Tahtawi. It begins by defining hajj as the visitation of specific locations (the Kaaba and Arafat) with specific rituals (ihram, tawaf, wuquf) within the designated months: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. The matn then states that hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime immediately (ala al-fawr) according to the most correct view. This immediate obligation means that one must perform hajj as soon as one is able, without delay. The commentary discusses the dispute between Abu Yusuf (who holds fawr) and Muhammad (who holds it can be delayed within one's lifetime). Al-Tahtawi explains the usuli concept that the time of hajj has dual aspects: as a measure (mi'yar) and as a container (zarf), and how each view impacts sin and the classification of performance as ada or qada.

The matn then lists eight conditions for the obligation of hajj: Islam, sanity (aql), puberty (bulugh), freedom, time (the designated months), ability for provisions (zad) with moderate expenditure, ability for a mount (rahilah) specifically for the traveler (or alternatively the ability to afford a share in a howdah), and that the ability be by ownership or hire, not by mere permission or loan (except for non-relatives). Each condition is expounded in the hashya.

For Islam: Hajj is not obligatory upon a disbeliever. If a disbeliever becomes Muslim after losing wealth, no hajj is due from that former wealth. But if a Muslim had the means and lost it, the obligation remains as a debt. There is also a dispute between the Hanafis (majority) and the Iraqis on whether disbelievers are addressed with furu'.

For sanity, puberty, and freedom: The proof is a hadith from Ibn Abbas that a child, a Bedouin, and a slave who perform hajj must repeat it after becoming obligated. Thus their hajj does not fulfill the Islamic obligation.

Time: Refers to the time of tawaf and wuquf, or the general time of hajj.

Ability for provisions: Means having enough food for the journey. The commentary gives an analogy: one accustomed to sweets is considered able if he has bread and cheese.

Mount: If one cannot ride a normal camel saddle, he must afford a mahara (large camel). The author of al-Bahr notes that riding a mule or donkey does not obligate hajj; only a camel is considered. This is an exclusively Hanafi position; other schools may allow other means.

The overall tone is instructive, presenting the Hanafi school's standard rulings on the obligation of hajj. The hashya clarifies technical terms and intra-madhhab differences.

Key Terms
الحج (al-hajj): Visitation of specific places (Kaaba and Arafat) with specific actions (ihram, tawaf, wuquf) in specific months (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah).
الفور (al-fawr): Immediate obligation: one must perform hajj as soon as possible after fulfilling conditions.
المشكل (al-mushkil): A term in usul al-fiqh meaning a text or concept that is ambiguous because it has two aspects; here, the time of hajj has both a measure (mi'yar) and container (zarf) aspect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view regarding the timing of hajj obligation in the Hanafi school?
A) Hajj is obligatory immediately (fawr).
B) Hajj is obligatory within one's entire lifetime (tarakhi).
C) Hajj is obligatory every year for those who are able.
D) Hajj is obligatory only once, but can be delayed indefinitely without sin.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is an immediate obligation (fard 'ayn) once in a lifetime, and delaying without valid reason is sinful according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Conditions for Hajj Obligation: Islam, Sanity, Puberty, and Freedom
Matn lists conditions; hashya provides hadith and commentary on Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight conditions for hajj obligation, state the proof for the four personal conditions from the hadith of Ibn Abbas, and explain the dispute regarding disbelievers being addressed with furu'.

Core Idea
Hajj is not obligatory on children, the insane, slaves, or disbelievers; their hajj does not fulfill the Islamic obligation.

This lesson focuses on the eight conditions for the obligation of hajj as listed in the matn, with particular attention to the first four: Islam, sanity, puberty, and freedom. The hashya provides a key hadith from Ibn Abbas proving these conditions. We will also examine the usuli dispute about whether disbelievers are addressed with the branches of Shari'a.

Guided Path
1
List the eight conditions
From the matn: 'وشروط فرضيته ثمانية على الأصح الإسلام، والعقل والبلوغ، والحرية والوقت والقدرة على الزاد والقدرة على راحلة'. Identify each.
These are conditions for obligation, not validity, though some overlap.
2
Analyze the hadith for the first four
Read the hadith: 'أيما صبي حج ثم بلغ الحنث فعليه أن يحج حجة أخرى...' Note that it explicitly requires puberty (from child), settlement/maturity (from Bedouin?), and freedom (from slave). Explain how each word indicates the condition.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalalah).
3
Examine the condition of Islam
The hashya states: 'لا يجب على الكافر'. It discusses whether a disbeliever's subsequent Islam after losing wealth waives the obligation. Contrast: if a Muslim had ability and lost it, obligation remains as debt.
This leads to the usuli dispute on whether kuffar are mukhattabun bi furu'.
4
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Take a case: a wealthy child performs hajj, then reaches puberty. According to the hadith, he must perform another hajj. Similarly, a slave who is freed must repeat hajj.
This shows that previous hajj does not count for fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
هو زيارة بقاع مخصوصة بفعل مخصوص في أشهره وهي شوال وذو القعدة، وعشر ذي الحجة فرض مرة على الفور في الأصح، وشروط فرضيته ثمانية على الأصح الإسلام، والعقل والبلوغ، والحرية والوقت والقدرة على الزاد ولو بمكة بنفقة وسط والقدرة على راحلة مختصة به، أو على شق محمل بالملك، أو الإجارة لا الإباحة، والإعارة لغير أهل نفسه
قوله: (بقاع مخصوصة) هي الكعبة وعرفات قوله : (بفعل مخصوص بأن يكون محرماً بنية الحج سابقاً، وطائفاً في زمن من ابتداء طلوع فجر النحر، ويمتد إلى آخر العمر واقفاً في زمن من زوال يوم عرفة إلى طلوع فجر النحر قوله : (وهي شوال الخ) فائدة التوقيت بها أنه لو فعل شيئاً من أفعال الحج خارجها لا يجزيه، وأنه يكره الإحرام قبلها، وإن أمن على من المحظور لشبهه بالركن وإطلاقها يفيد التحريم .در قوله : (وذو القعدة) بفتح وكسرها درر. قوله : (فرض مرة على الفور) عند أبي يوسف وفي العمر عند محمد اعلم أن وقت الحج في اصطلاح الأصوليين يسمى مشكلاً لأنّ فيه جهة المعيارية والظرفية، فمن قال : بالفور لا يقول : بأن من أخره عن العام الأول يكون فعله قضاء، ومن قال بالتراخي لا يقول بأن من أخره لا يأثم أصلاً كما إذا أخر الصلاة عن الوقت الأول ، بل جهة المعيارية راجحة عند القائل بالفور حتى أن من أخر يفسق، وترد شهادته لكن إذا حج بالأخرة كان أداء لا قضاء وجهة الظرفية راجحة عند القائل بخلافه حتى إذا أداه بعد العام الأول، لا يأثم بالتأخير، لكن لو مات، ولم يحج أثم أيضاً عنده .در قوله : (الإسلام) فلا يجب على الكافر حتى لو ملك ما به الاستطاعة، ثم أسلم بعد ما افتقر لا يجب عليه شيء بتلك الاستطاعة بخلاف ما لو ملكه مسلماً، فلم يحج حتى افتقر حيث يتقرر وجوبه ديناً في ذمته ذكره العلامة نوح عن الفتح، وهذا على أن الكفار غير مخاطبين بفروع الشريعة وقال العراقيون، بخاطبهم: فيكون على قولهم من شرائط الصحة قوله : (والعقل والبلوغ والحرية إنما اشترطت هذه لما روي عن ابن عباس قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : أيما صبي حج ثم بلغ الحنث فعليه أن يحج حجة أخرى وأيما أعرابي حج ، ثم هاجر فعليه أن يحج حجة أخرى وأيما عبد حج، ثم أعتق فعليه أن يحج حجة أخرى، واعلم أنه لا يجب عليه وأن أذن له مولاه فلو حج بإذن مولاه، أو بغيره لا يقع عن حجة الإسلام، أفاده العلامة نوح قوله : (والوقت) أي وقت الطواف، والوقوف ويحتمل أن المراد الوقت الذي يحصل فيه الحج، وهو يختلف باختلاف البلدان. قوله: (والقدرة على الزاد الذي يصح به بدنه فالمعتاد للحلو ونحوه إذا قدر على خبز وجبن يعد قادراً در . قوله : (بنفقة وسط) أي من غير إسراف ولا تقتير قوله : على راحلة مخصة به) فإن لم يقدر على ركوب المقتب اشترط القدرة على المحارة قال صاحب البحر عند ذكر الراحلة أنه لو قدر على غير الراحلة من بغل أو حمار لم يجب، ولم أره وإنما صرحوا بالكراهة قال أبو السعود
The Book of Hajj. It is the visitation of specific places with specific actions in its months, which are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the ten (days) of Dhu al-Hijjah. It is obligatory once immediately (ala al-fawr) according to the most correct view. The conditions of its obligation are eight according to the most correct view: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, time, and the ability for provisions even if in Makkah with moderate expenditure, and the ability for a mount specific to him, or (to sit) on the side of a howdah (shiqq mahmil) by ownership or hire, not by permission, and (the ability for) a loan for other than the person himself.

His saying: “Specific places” – they are the Kaaba and Arafat. His saying: “by specific action” – that one be in ihram with the intention of hajj beforehand, a circumambulating one in a time from the beginning of the dawn of the Day of Sacrifice, extending to the end of one’s life, a standing one in a time from the decline of the sun on the Day of Arafah to the dawn of the Day of Sacrifice. His saying: “and they are Shawwal, etc.” – the benefit of specifying them is that if one performs any act of hajj outside them, it does not suffice; and that it is disliked to enter ihram before them, even if one is safe from prohibitions, due to its resemblance to the pillar; and its unrestricted (mention) indicates prohibition. Durr. His saying: “and Dhu al-Qa'dah” – with fatḥ and kasr (of the letter). Durar. His saying: “obligatory once immediately (fard marratan ala al-fawr)” – according to Abu Yusuf, and during the lifetime according to Muhammad. Know that the time of Hajj in the terminology of the usuliyyun is called “mushkil” because it has the aspect of measure (mi‘yariyyah) and circumstance (zarfiyyah). Whoever says it is immediate does not say that delaying it past the first year makes it a qada; and whoever says it is lax (tarakhi) does not say that delaying it entails no sin at all, as if one delays prayer beyond its first time; rather, the aspect of measure is preponderant for those who say immediate, so much so that one who delays becomes a transgressor and his testimony is rejected, yet if he eventually performs hajj, it is ada, not qada; and the aspect of circumstance is preponderant for those who differ, so that if he performs it after the first year, he does not sin for the delay, but if he dies without having performed hajj, he sins according to him as well. Durr. His saying: “Islam” – it is not obligatory upon the disbeliever; even if he possesses means, then becomes Muslim after having lost wealth, nothing is due upon him from that means, unlike if he possessed it as a Muslim and did not perform hajj until he became poor, the obligation becomes established as a debt in his liability. This is mentioned by Allamah Nuh from al-Fath. And this is on the view that the disbelievers are not addressed with the branches of Shari'a; but the Iraqis say they are addressed, so according to them it is a condition of validity. His saying: “and sanity, puberty, freedom” – these are only stipulated due to what is related from Ibn Abbas: he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: “Any child who performs hajj then reaches the age of obligation, he must perform another hajj; and any Bedouin who performs hajj then migrates (hajara), he must perform another hajj; and any slave who performs hajj then is freed, he must perform another hajj.” And know that it is not obligatory upon him even if his master permits; so if he performs hajj with his master’s permission or otherwise, it does not count as the hajj of Islam (hajjat al-Islam). This is stated by Allamah Nuh. His saying: “and time” – i.e., the time of tawaf and wuquf; and it is possible that it means the time in which hajj takes place, and it varies by country. His saying: “and ability for provisions that sustain his body” – so one accustomed to sweets and the like, if he is able to have bread and cheese, he is considered able. Durr. His saying: “with moderate expenditure” – i.e., without extravagance nor miserliness. His saying: “on a mount specific to him” – if he is unable to ride the miqtab (small camel saddle), the ability to ride the mahara (large camel saddle) is required. The author of al-Bahr said regarding the mention of the mount: if he is able to ride other than a mount, such as a mule or donkey, it is not obligatory; I have not seen (this), and they only declared it disliked. Abu al-Sa'ud said.
Source pages p. 726

Commentary
This passage is the opening of Kitab al-Hajj from the matn of Maraqi al-Falah along with the hashya commentary of al-Tahtawi. It begins by defining hajj as the visitation of specific locations (the Kaaba and Arafat) with specific rituals (ihram, tawaf, wuquf) within the designated months: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. The matn then states that hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime immediately (ala al-fawr) according to the most correct view. This immediate obligation means that one must perform hajj as soon as one is able, without delay. The commentary discusses the dispute between Abu Yusuf (who holds fawr) and Muhammad (who holds it can be delayed within one's lifetime). Al-Tahtawi explains the usuli concept that the time of hajj has dual aspects: as a measure (mi'yar) and as a container (zarf), and how each view impacts sin and the classification of performance as ada or qada.

The matn then lists eight conditions for the obligation of hajj: Islam, sanity (aql), puberty (bulugh), freedom, time (the designated months), ability for provisions (zad) with moderate expenditure, ability for a mount (rahilah) specifically for the traveler (or alternatively the ability to afford a share in a howdah), and that the ability be by ownership or hire, not by mere permission or loan (except for non-relatives). Each condition is expounded in the hashya.

For Islam: Hajj is not obligatory upon a disbeliever. If a disbeliever becomes Muslim after losing wealth, no hajj is due from that former wealth. But if a Muslim had the means and lost it, the obligation remains as a debt. There is also a dispute between the Hanafis (majority) and the Iraqis on whether disbelievers are addressed with furu'.

For sanity, puberty, and freedom: The proof is a hadith from Ibn Abbas that a child, a Bedouin, and a slave who perform hajj must repeat it after becoming obligated. Thus their hajj does not fulfill the Islamic obligation.

Time: Refers to the time of tawaf and wuquf, or the general time of hajj.

Ability for provisions: Means having enough food for the journey. The commentary gives an analogy: one accustomed to sweets is considered able if he has bread and cheese.

Mount: If one cannot ride a normal camel saddle, he must afford a mahara (large camel). The author of al-Bahr notes that riding a mule or donkey does not obligate hajj; only a camel is considered. This is an exclusively Hanafi position; other schools may allow other means.

The overall tone is instructive, presenting the Hanafi school's standard rulings on the obligation of hajj. The hashya clarifies technical terms and intra-madhhab differences.

Key Terms
شروط الوجوب (shurūṭ al-wujūb): Conditions that must be present for an act to be obligatory.
الحنث (al-hanath): The age of legal responsibility (puberty) or sin; in the hadith, 'balagha al-hanath' means reaching puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What proof does the Hanafi school use for requiring puberty, sanity, and freedom as conditions for hajj obligation?
A) Quranic verse: 'And perform hajj for Allah'
B) Hadith of Ibn Abbas about the child, Bedouin, and slave
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogical reasoning from prayer

Key Takeaway
Hajj is obligatory only upon Muslims who are sane, pubert, free, and have the means; the hadith of Ibn Abbas is the primary proof for the personal conditions.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Conditions of Ability: Provisions and Mount for Hajj
Hashya explanation of the last two conditions for obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define istita'ah for hajj in terms of provisions and mount, and explain why the Hanafi school specifically requires a camel mount.

Core Idea
Ability for hajj means having sufficient provisions and a mount (camel) by ownership or hire, not mere permission or a loan.

This lesson delves into the last two conditions for hajj obligation: ability for provisions (zad) and ability for a mount (rahilah). The hashya clarifies that the mount must be specific to the person, acquired by ownership or hire, and that a mule or donkey is not sufficient according to the Hanafi school. We will also examine the concept of moderate expenditure.

Guided Path
1
Define ability for provisions (zad)
Find the condition 'القدرة على الزاد' and note that the hashya says it is for sustaining the body. Even if one is in Makkah, provisions are needed for moderate expenditure. The example shows that one accustomed to sweets is considered able if he has bread and cheese.
Moderation means neither extravagance nor miserliness.
2
Define ability for a mount (rahilah)
Read the condition: 'القدرة على راحلة مختصة به، أو على شق محمل بالملك، أو الإجارة لا الإباحة، والإعارة لغير أهل نفسه'. Parse: the mount must be specific to him; alternatively, a share in a howdah (shiqq mahmil) by ownership or hire. Mere permission (ibahah) or loan (i'arah) to a non-relative does not suffice.
The mount is typically a camel; the school specifies this.
3
Understand the exclusive camel requirement
The hashya from al-Bahr notes that if one can afford a mule or donkey, it is not obligatory. The Hanafi school specifically requires a camel (rahilah). If one cannot ride a miqtab (small saddle), he must afford a mahara (larger saddle).
This is a uniquely Hanafi position; other schools are more flexible.
4
Apply to a real scenario
Consider a person who can afford a donkey and provisions but not a camel. According to the Hanafi school, hajj is not obligatory upon him. This shows the strictness of the condition.
If he can hire a camel, that is sufficient.

Each condition is expounded in the hashya.

For Islam: Hajj is not obligatory upon a disbeliever. If a disbeliever becomes Muslim after losing wealth, no hajj is due from that former wealth. But if a Muslim had the means and lost it, the obligation remains as a debt. There is also a dispute between the Hanafis (majority) and the Iraqis on whether disbelievers are addressed with furu'.

For sanity, puberty, and freedom: The proof is a hadith from Ibn Abbas that a child, a Bedouin, and a slave who perform hajj must repeat it after becoming obligated. Thus their hajj does not fulfill the Islamic obligation.

Time: Refers to the time of tawaf and wuquf, or the general time of hajj.

Ability for provisions: Means having enough food for the journey. The commentary gives an analogy: one accustomed to sweets is considered able if he has bread and cheese.

Mount: If one cannot ride a normal camel saddle, he must afford a mahara (large camel). The author of al-Bahr notes that riding a mule or donkey does not obligate hajj; only a camel is considered. This is an exclusively Hanafi position; other schools may allow other means.

The overall tone is instructive, presenting the Hanafi school's standard rulings on the obligation of hajj. The hashya clarifies technical terms and intra-madhhab differences.

Key Terms
الزاد (al-zād): Provisions for the journey, sufficient for moderate expenditure to sustain the body.
الراحلة (al-rāḥilah): A riding camel (mount) that is specifically used for traveling.
المقتب (al-miqtāb): A small camel saddle used for riding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what type of mount is required for the obligation of hajj?
A) Any vehicle that can carry the person
B) A camel (rahilah)
C) A horse or mule
D) A donkey

Key Takeaway
Istita'ah for hajj requires not only provisions but specifically a camel mount (rahilah) by ownership or hire; other animals do not suffice.

Conditions of Hajj Obligation and the Ruling of Immediacy
Explains Hajj conditions and immediacy ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight conditions of Hajj obligation and explain why the Hanafi school holds it is obligatory immediately (fawr), evaluating the intra-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory once immediately — delaying without excuse makes one sinful.

Hajj is a foundational pillar of Islam, but its obligation is not unconditional. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi delineates the precise eight conditions that must be met for Hajj to become obligatory (fard), and clarifies the critical ruling of immediacy (fawr) — that once the conditions are fulfilled, one may not delay without sin. We will walk through these conditions, examine the hadith proof, and understand the disagreement within the Hanafi school about whether the obligation is immediate or can be delayed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
State the ruling: Hajj is fard 'ayn once in a lifetime. Note the textual phrase 'fi al-ashah' (most correct) indicating the preferred view.
The ruling is proven by qat'i evidence (Quran and Sunnah), making it fard, not wajib.
2
List the eight conditions of obligation
Work through each condition: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, time (months of Hajj), ability for provisions, ability for a mount (or walking), and knowledge of obligation for new Muslims.
The first four are general; the last four are specific to Hajj.
3
Examine the hadith proof
Analyze the hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'Any child who performs Hajj then reaches puberty must perform another Hajj...' Identify how it proves that Hajj before puberty does not fulfill the obligation.
The imperative 'فعليه أن يحج' indicates obligation. The hadith implies that once conditions are met, a new Hajj is required.
4
Understand the dispute: fawr vs tarakhi
Compare Abu Yusuf's immediate view (fawr) with Muhammad al-Shaybani's view that only 'umrah is immediate; and the opposing school (Shafi'i) holding tarakhi. Note the usul concept of time having a criterion (mi'yari) and container (zarf) aspect.
The Hanafi relied-upon position is fawr, as stated 'fi al-ashah'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Apply the difference: under fawr, delaying without excuse makes one sinful (fasiq) and testimony rejected, but the Hajj performed later is ada', not qada. Under tarakhi, no sin until death approaches.
This practical difference affects one's religious and legal status.

الكافر حتى لو ملك ما به الاستطاعة، ثم أسلم بعد ما افتقر لا يجب عليه شيء بتلك الاستطاعة بخلاف ما لو ملكه مسلماً، فلم يحج حتى افتقر حيث يتقرر وجوبه ديناً في ذمته ذكره العلامة نوح عن الفتح، وهذا على أن بغيره لا يقع عن حجة الإسلام، أفاده العلامة نوح قوله : (والوقت) أي وقت الطواف، والوقوف ويحتمل أن المراد الوقت الذي يحصل فيه الحج، وهو يختلف باختلاف البلدان. قوله: (والقدرة على الزاد الذي يصح به بدنه Book of Hajj: Dhul-Hijjah is obligatory once immediately according to the most correct view. Its conditions of obligation are eight according to the most correct: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, time, ability for provisions even if in Mecca with moderate expenditure, and ability for a mount specific to him, or on a camel litter by ownership or hire, not by permission, and lending for other than himself... His statement: (specific places) are the Kaaba and Arafat. His statement: (by a specific action) being in ihram with intention of Hajj previously, and performing tawaf in a time from the beginning of dawn of the day of sacrifice extending to the end of one's life, and standing in a time from noon of Arafah to dawn of the day of sacrifice. His statement: (They are Shawwal etc.) The benefit of specifying these times is that if one performs any Hajj actions outside them, it does not suffice, and it is disliked to enter ihram before them even if safe from prohibitions due to resemblance to the pillar, and its absolute wording indicates prohibition. His statement: (and Dhu al-Qa'dah) with fatha and kasra. His statement: (obligatory once immediately) according to Abu Yusuf, and in 'umrah according to Muhammad. Know that the time of Hajj in the terminology of usuliyyun is called mushkil because it has both a criterion aspect and a container aspect. So the one who says it is immediate does not say that delaying past the first year makes it qada', and the one who says it is permissive does not say that the delayer is not sinful at all, as if delaying prayer beyond the initial time. Rather, the criterion aspect is preponderant according to the one who says immediacy, so that the delayer becomes sinful and his testimony is rejected, but if he performs Hajj later, it is ada' not qada'. The container aspect is preponderant according to the one who says otherwise, so that if he performs after the first year, he is not sinful for delay, but if he dies without performing Hajj, he is also sinful according to him. His statement: (Islam) so it is not obligatory upon a disbeliever; even if he possessed the means of capability, then he accepts Islam after becoming poor, nothing is obligatory upon him due to that capability. Unlike if he possessed it as a Muslim and did not perform Hajj until he became poor, then the obligation is established as a debt in his liability, as mentioned by Allamah Nuh from al-Fath. This is based on the view that disbelievers are not addressed with the branches of Sharia. The Iraqis say they are addressed, so according to them it is a condition of validity. His statement: (and sanity, puberty, and freedom) These are required due to what is narrated from Ibn Abbas who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Any child who performs Hajj and then reaches the age of responsibility must perform another Hajj; any Bedouin who performs Hajj and then migrates must perform another Hajj; any slave who performs Hajj and then is freed must perform another Hajj.' Know that he is not obligated even if his master gives him permission; if he performs Hajj with his master's permission or otherwise, it does not count as the Hajj of Islam, as Allamah Nuh stated. His statement: (and time) meaning the time of tawaf and standing, and it is possible that what is meant is the time in which Hajj occurs, which varies by country. His statement: (and ability for provisions that sustain his body; for one accustomed to sweets and the like, if he has bread and cheese he is considered capable. His statement: (with moderate expenditure) meaning without extravagance or stinginess. His statement: (a mount specific to him) if he cannot ride a litter, then ability for a riding animal is required. The author of al-Bahr said regarding the mount: if he can ride other than a mount, such as a mule or donkey, it is not obligatory, but they explicitly stated it is disliked. Abu al-Sa'ud said: and those around them if they can walk on foot with strength without hardship, otherwise a mount is absolutely necessary. And that ability must be surplus to his own expenses and his family's expenses until his return, and to what is indispensable such as housing, furniture, tools of professionals, and repayment of debt. Knowledge of the obligation of Hajj is required for one who accepts Islam in dar al-harb or resides in dar al-Islam.
Source pages p. 727

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditions of Hajj obligation. It begins by defining Hajj as visiting specific places (Kaaba and Arafat) with specific actions at specific times (Shawwal to Dhu al-Hijjah). The ruling that Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime immediately (fawr) is presented, with an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds immediate obligation for Hajj, while Muhammad applies it to 'umrah. The commentator explains the usul concept of 'time' having both a criterion (mi'yari) and container (zarf) aspect, leading to nuanced views on sin for delay. The eight conditions of obligation (shurut al-fardiyyah) are: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, time (the months of Hajj), ability for provisions, ability for a mount (or walking if possible), and knowledge of the obligation for those new to Islam. A hadith from Ibn Abbas is cited to prove that Hajj performed before puberty, freedom, or residence in Mecca does not fulfill the Islamic obligation. The ability condition includes having sufficient provisions for the journey and for dependents, and a mount—or walking if feasible without hardship. Lending or permission-based rides do not constitute ability. The passage also clarifies that ability must be surplus to essential needs like housing and debts.

Key Terms
فرضية (fardiyyah): The state of being obligatory (fard).
فور (fawr): Immediate performance of an obligatory act at the earliest possible time.
استطاعة (istita'ah): The ability or capacity to perform Hajj, including provisions and mount.
تراخي (tarakhi): The view that an obligation can be delayed as long as it is performed before death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is TRUE regarding a person who has the means to perform Hajj but delays it for two years without a valid excuse?
A) He is not sinful because he intends to perform it eventually.
B) He becomes sinful (fasiq) and his testimony is rejected.
C) He must perform Hajj as qada' when he eventually does it.
D) His obligation is lifted after the first year.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is obligatory immediately upon fulfillment of eight conditions; delaying without excuse is sinful in the Hanafi school.

Conditions for Valid Performance of Hajj and the Mahram Dispute
Ruling with proof and critical refinement on Hajj conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for valid performance of Hajj and explain the Hanafi dispute on whether the mahram is a condition of obligation or performance.

Core Idea
Five conditions validate Hajj performance; the mahram requirement sparks debate: obligation or performance?

The Hanafi school specifies five conditions (shurut al-ada) that must be fulfilled for Hajj to be validly performed. Among these, the requirement of a mahram for women has generated intra-madhhab discussion: is it a condition for the obligation to arise (wujub) or for the act's performance (ada)? This lesson unpacks the five conditions and resolves the ikhtilaf using Hanafi usul and textual proofs.

Guided Path
1
List the five conditions
Identify and memorize the five conditions: physical health, removal of physical obstacles, road safety, being free from iddah, and presence of a mahram (for women). Note the proof for the iddah condition from Quran 65:1.
These are shurut al-ada, not shurut al-wujub.
2
Understand the mahram requirement in detail
Read the commentary on the mahram: who qualifies (Muslim, trustworthy, adult, sane) and exceptions (dhimmi does not suffice, fasiq excluded). Note that a husband also qualifies.
The mahram must be reliable for the journey.
3
Identify the ikhtilaf
The text reports a difference of opinion: is the mahram a condition of obligation (wujub) or performance (ada)? Recognize that this affects whether a woman must actively procure a mahram.
Al-Bada'i's view that it is a condition of obligation is cited as corroborated.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
Work through the practical consequences: if mahram is a condition of obligation, she is not required to marry to obtain one; if of performance, she would be obliged to seek one. The text sides with the former.
The Hanafi principle: conditions of obligation need not be procured.
5
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Consider a woman in iddah who has a mahram. The iddah condition overrides? Actually, both must be absent. If she is in iddah, Hajj is not valid even with a mahram. So conditions are cumulative.
All five conditions must be met for valid performance.

And the conditions for obligation of performance are five according to the most correct: physical health, removal of physical obstacle for going to Hajj, safety of the road, being free from waiting period, and exit of a mahram—even through breastfeeding or in-law relationship—a trustworthy, sane, mature Muslim man, or a husband for a woman traveling. The criterion is predominant safety by land and sea... His statement: (other than the people of Mecca) connected to his statement: (and ability for a mount). His statement: (if they can walk) then it is obligatory for them by analogy to the Friday prayer. His statement: (until his return) and it was said a day after, and it was said a month after. His statement: (such as the house) meaning its maintenance; he is not obliged to sell part of his house that he is not using to perform Hajj, though it is better. They said: if he could borrow and perform Hajj even if unable to repay, hoping, he should not perform Hajj so that Allah does not hold him accountable—meaning if he intends to repay when able, as restricted by al-Zahiriyya. His statement: (physical health) meaning including eyesight. His statement: (removal of physical obstacle for going) such as imprisonment; similarly, it is required that he not be afraid of it. His statement: (safety of the road) such that the predominant state is safety, even through bribery; killing of some pilgrims is an excuse. His statement: (being free from the waiting period) due to irrevocable or revocable divorce or death, as per the verse: 'Do not expel them from their houses' [65:1]. Hajj can be performed at another time, as per the clarification. His statement: (exit of a mahram) even if a slave or a dhimmi, not a woman even if elderly. The mahram's expenses are obligatory on her because he is confined due to her. Her husband cannot prevent her from the Hajj of Islam. If she performs Hajj without a mahram, it is permissible with dislike. His statement: (Muslim) it is better to say 'non-Muslim' as in al-Tanwir because a dhimmi does not suffice. His statement: (trustworthy) excludes a sinful person (fasiq) for he is not protective like a Zoroastrian. His statement: (mature) a near-pubescent is like an adult. His statement: (or a husband for a woman in travel) There is a difference of opinion whether the husband or mahram is a condition of obligation or a condition of performance, analogous to their difference regarding safety of the road. The effect of the difference appears in the obligation of making a will, the obligation of the mahram's expenses and mount, and the obligation for her to marry to perform Hajj if she cannot find a mahram. One who said it is a condition of obligation, as corroborated in al-Bada'i, said: No, because conditions of obligation are things that are obligatory to procure, so if he is given wealth, he may refuse acceptance until Hajj becomes obligatory on him.
Source pages p. 728

Commentary
This passage discusses the five conditions for the valid performance of Hajj (shurut al-ada): 1) physical health (including eyesight), 2) removal of physical obstacles like imprisonment or fear, 3) safety of the road (predominant safety, even via bribery), 4) not being in a waiting period (iddah) from divorce or death, based on Quran 65:1, and 5) for women, the presence of a mahram or husband. The commentary clarifies that the mahram must be a trustworthy, sane, adult Muslim; a slave or dhimmi is acceptable for a non-Muslim woman? The text corrects that a dhimmi does not suffice. A fasiq is not trustworthy. The near-pubescent is treated as adult. The dispute over whether the mahram is a condition of obligation (wujub) or performance (ada) has practical consequences: if it is a condition of obligation, a woman is not required to seek a mahram actively (e.g., by marrying), whereas if it is a condition of performance, she must try to obtain one. The text mentions the view of al-Bada'i that it is a condition of obligation, so she is not obliged to marry to perform Hajj. The passage also discusses ability in terms of surplus wealth: one is not forced to sell essential housing or borrow money to perform Hajj, though it is virtuous to do so.

Key Terms
شرط الأداء (shart al-ada): A condition that must exist at the time of performing the act for it to be valid.
محرم (mahram): A male relative whom a woman is permanently forbidden to marry (e.g., father, brother).
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death before remarrying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the correct classification of the mahram requirement for a woman's Hajj?
A) It is a condition of obligation (shart al-wujub) according to al-Bada'i
B) It is a condition of performance (shart al-ada) according to all Hanafis
C) It is not required if the woman is elderly
D) It is required only for the first Hajj

Key Takeaway
The mahram requirement for a woman's Hajj is correctly understood as a condition of obligation (wujub) in the Hanafi school, relieving her of the duty to procure one through marriage.

Shurut al-Wujub: The Five Conditions for the Obligation of Hajj
Ruling with proof and critical refinement on conditions of Hajj obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for Hajj being obligatory and explain why the mahram condition is a condition of performance rather than obligation according to the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Hajj becomes obligatory only when five conditions are met; the mahram for women is a condition of performance, not of obligation.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi details the five conditions that must be present for Hajj to be obligatory (shurut al-wujub). It also clarifies a key intra-Hanafi dispute: whether the requirement of a mahram for women is a condition of obligation (shart al-wujub) or a condition of performance (shart al-ada). The commentary resolves this, guiding the mufti on the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five conditions
List the five conditions explicitly mentioned: sound body, removal of physical impediment, safe route, not in 'iddah, and mahram for women.
The text says 'on the most correct opinion' indicating some ikhtilaf.
2
Understand the distinction between shart al-wujub and shart al-ada
A condition of obligation must be present for the duty to arise; a condition of performance must be present at the time of acting. The latter can be acquired.
This distinction is central to the mahram dispute.
3
Note the dalil for the 'iddah condition
The prohibition in Quran 65:6 (do not expel them from their homes) implies Hajj is not obligatory during 'iddah.
This is a clear proof for one of the conditions.
4
Analyze the dispute regarding the mahram
Some Hanafi scholars held mahram is a condition of obligation (shart al-wujub); others held it is a condition of performance (shart al-ada). The text adopts the latter as mufta bihi.
The practical difference is whether she must seek a mahram and pay his expenses.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
If mahram is a condition of performance, she must endeavor to find one; if obligation, she does not have to. The mufta bihi is the former, based on al-Kasani's tarjih.
This affects the obligation to bequeath for Hajj and the cost of the mahram's travel.

في حاشية الأشباه: تصريحهم بالكراهة يدل على عدم الوجوب إذ لو كان واجباً لما كره لأن الواجب لا يتصف بالكراهة، وتمامه فيه قوله: (لا) (الإباحة فلو وهب له ابنه ما لا يحج به لم يجب قبوله لأن شرائط الوجوب لا يجب تحصيلها قوله: الغير أهل مكة مرتبط بقوله: والقدرة على راحلة قوله: إذا أمكنهم المشي فيجب عليهم لشبهه بالسعي إلى الجمعة. قوله: (إلى حين عوده وقيل بعده بيوم وقيل بشهر در. قوله: (كالمنزل) أي ومرمته ولا يلزم بيع ما استغنى عنه من بعض منزله ليحج به نعم هو الأفضل، وكذا لا يلزمه لوكان عنده ما لو اشترى به مسكناً وخادماً لا يبقى بعده ما يكفي للحج كما في الخلاصة، وقالوا لو أن يستقرض ويحج ولو غير قادر على وفائه، ويرجو لم يحج حتى لا يؤاخذه الله بذلك أي لو ناوياً وفاءه إذا قدر كما قيده به في الظهيرية. قوله: (أو الكون بدار الإسلام وإن لم يعلم فيكون وجوده في دار الإسلام علماً وحكماً سواء نشأ على الإسلام، أو لا ذكره السيد. قوله: (صحة البدن) أي مع البصر. قوله: (وزوال المانع الحسي عن الذهاب) كالحبس، وكذا يشترط أن لا يكون خائفاً منه قوله: (وأمن الطريق) بأن لا يكون سلطان يمنع، ويكون الغالب السلامة، ولو بالرشوة، وقتل بعض الحجاج عذر قوله: (وعدم قيام العدة) من طلاق بائن، أو رجعي أو وفاة لقوله تعالى: (لا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن) [الطلاق: 65] والحج يمكن أداؤه في وقت آخر غاية البيان قوله: (وخروج محرم) ولو عبداً أو ذمياً لا امرأة، ولو عجوزاً، وتجب نفقة المحرم عليها لأنه محبوس عليها، وليس لزوجها منعها عن حجة الإسلام، ولو حجت بلا محرم جاز مع الكراهة. در قوله: (مسلم) الأولى أن يقول غير أنه كما في التنوير لما يكفي الذمي. قوله: (مأمون) خرج الفاسق فإنه لا يحفظ كالمجوسي قوله: (بالغ) المراهق كالبالغ جوهرة قوله: (أو زوج لامرأة في سفر) اختلف في أن الزوج أو المحرم شرط الوجوب، أو شرط الأداء على حسب اختلافهم في أمن الطريق، وتظهر ثمرة الخلاف في وجوب الوصية وفي وجوب نفقة المحرم، وراحلته إذا أبى أن يخرج معها لا بالزاد منها والراحلة وفي وجوب التزوج عليها ليحج بها إن لم تجد محرماً فمن قال هو شرط الوجوب وصححه في البدائع قال: لا لأن شروط الوجوب لا يجب تحصيلها، ولذا لو أبيح له المال كان له الامتناع من القبول حتى يجب الحج عليه، على المفتي به
Book of Hajj. And among those around them, if they can walk on foot and have strength without difficulty, then they must; otherwise they need a mount absolutely. And that ability must be surplus to his expenses and the expenses of his family until his return, and beyond what is necessary like a home, its furnishings, tools of craftsmen, and repayment of debt. Knowledge of the obligation of Hajj is required for one who accepts Islam in dar al-harb or resides in dar al-Islam. The conditions for the obligation of performance are five according to the most correct opinion: soundness of body, removal of physical impediment to going for Hajj, safety of the road, not being in a waiting period, and the presence of a mahram - even from breastfeeding or in-law relationship - who is Muslim, trustworthy, sane, adult, or a husband for a woman in travel. The criterion is predominant safety by land and sea... [then commentary]
Source pages p. 728

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical commentary on the conditions (shurut) that make Hajj obligatory (wujub). The author begins by reiterating the general principle: ability (qudra) includes having provisions and a mount, but if one can walk without hardship, walking suffices. The ability must be surplus to necessities. The five conditions for obligation are then enumerated: (1) sound body including eyesight; (2) absence of physical barriers like imprisonment or fear of it; (3) a safe route, where safety is judged by predominant outcome, even if achieved by bribe or despite occasional fatalities; (4) not being in an 'iddah (waiting period) from divorce or death, based on Quran 65:6; (5) a mahram (unmarriageable kin) for women, who must be Muslim, trustworthy, sane, and adult (or a husband). The commentary clarifies that a mahram may be a slave or dhimmī but not a woman; a woman may travel without a mahram but it is makruh. A key debate is whether the mahram is a condition for obligation (shart al-wujub) or performance (shart al-ada). If it is a condition of obligation, then a woman is not required to acquire a mahram, whereas if it is a condition of performance, she must find one. The relied-upon position (al-mufta bihi) is that it is a condition of performance, so she must try to obtain a mahram. The commentary also discusses related issues like expenses of the mahram and the ruling on borrowing money for Hajj.

Key Terms
شرط الوجوب (shart al-wujub): A condition that triggers the obligation; if absent, one is not required to act.
شرط الأداء (shart al-ada): A condition that must be present at the time of performance; if absent, one is still obligated but the act is not valid without it.
محرم (mahram): A person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood, suckling, or marriage relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman is in her 'iddah from a revocable divorce. Is Hajj obligatory on her this year?
A) Yes, because 'iddah does not prevent obligation.
B) No, because being in 'iddah is a condition preventing obligation.
C) Yes, but she must perform it herself without mahram.
D) No, because she lacks a mahram.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is fard 'ayn only when five conditions are met; the mahram requirement is a condition of performance, not obligation, according to the mufta bihi.

Rukn and Wajib in Hajj: Conditions, Pillars, and Obligations
Lists the conditions, pillars, and wajibat of Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two conditions and two pillars that make Hajj valid from the list of wajibat that require a dam if omitted, and apply this distinction to a pilgrim's actions.

Core Idea
Two pillars, two conditions, and many wajibat – know which omission breaks your Hajj versus which costs a sheep.

Hajj has a precise structure. This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah on Maraqi al-Falah lays out that structure in a compact form: first the conditions (shurut) and pillars (arkan) that are essential for validity, then the long list of wajibat (obligatory acts) that must be performed but do not invalidate the Hajj if omitted – though a dam (blood sacrifice) is required. Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for every pilgrim and student of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions
The passage opens by saying Hajj is valid with four things: ihram and Islam are conditions. This means they must be present for the Hajj to be considered. Note that ihram here refers to the state of consecration, not just the intention.
Conditions precede the ritual; without them the act is not valid from the start.
2
Identify the two pillars
The two pillars are standing at Arafat (for any moment between noon on 9th Dhu al-Hijjah and dawn of 10th) and the majority of tawaf al-ifadah (four circuits) after dawn of the 10th. These are the essential acts; omitting either invalidates Hajj.
The remaining three circuits of tawaf al-ifadah are wajib, not rukn.
3
Parse the list of wajibat
The passage then enumerates many wajibat: starting ihram from the miqat, prolonging standing at Arafat until sunset, standing at Muzdalifah, stoning the jamarat, sacrifice for qarin/mutamatti', shaving, performing tawaf al-ziyarah in days of tashriq, sa'y after a valid tawaf, tawaf al-wada', beginning tawaf from the Black Stone, walking on the right, walking if able, purity, covering awrah, and avoiding prohibitions. Each wajib if omitted requires a dam but does not invalidate the Hajj.
The list integrates actions and prohibitions – all are wajib to perform or avoid.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a pilgrim omits a wajib (e.g., does not shave), his Hajj is valid but he must sacrifice a sheep. If he misses a rukn (e.g., does not stand at Arafat at all), his Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
This distinction is central to Hanafi fiqh.
5
Note intra-madhhab differences
The commentary mentions that the order of stoning before shaving is according to Imam Abu Hanifa; other Hanafi imams differed. Yet the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view.
These details matter for fatwa but do not change the overall structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصح أداء فرض الحج بأربعة أشياء للحر الإحرام والإسلام، وهما شرطان ثم الإتيان بركنيه وهما الوقوف محرماً بعرفات لحظة من زوال يوم التاسع إلى فجر يوم النحر بشرط عدم الجماع قبله محرماً والركن الثاني هو أكثر طواف الإفاضة في وقته، وهو بعد طلوع فجر النحر وواجبات الحج إنشاء الإحرام من الميقات ومد الوقوف بعرفات إلى الغروب، والوقوف بالمزدلفة فيما بعد فجر يوم النحر، وقبل طلوع الشمس، ورمي الجمار وذبح القارن والمتمتع والحلق وتخصيصه بالحرم ، وأيام النحر وتقديم الرمي على الحلق ونحر القارن والمتمتع بينهما، وإيقاع طواف الزيارة في أيام النحر والسعي بين الصفا والمروة في أشهر الحج ، وحصوله بعد طواف معتد به والمشي فيه لمن لا عذر له، وبداءة السعي من الصفا وطواف الوداع، وبداءة كل طواف بالبيت من الحجر الأسود، والتيامن فيه، والمشي فيه لمن لا عذر له والطهارة من الحدثين، وستر العورة، وأقل الأشواط بعد فعل الأكثر من طواف الزيارة، وترك المحظورات كلبس الرجل المخيط، وستر رأسه ووجهه وستر المرأة وجهها والرفث والفسوق والجدال، وقتل الصيد والإشارة إليه، ومن الصفا
And the performance of the obligation of Hajj is valid with four things for a free person: ihram and Islam, both are conditions; then performing its two pillars which are: standing in ihram at Arafat for a moment from noon of the ninth day to dawn of the day of sacrifice, with the condition of no intercourse before that while in ihram; and the second pillar is the majority of tawaf al-ifadah in its time, which is after dawn of the day of sacrifice. And the obligatory acts of Hajj are: commencing ihram from the miqat; prolonging the standing at Arafat until sunset; standing at Muzdalifah after dawn of the day of sacrifice and before sunrise; stoning the jamarat; slaughtering for the qarin and mutamatti'; shaving and confining it to the sanctuary; the days of sacrifice; giving precedence to stoning over shaving; sacrificing for qarin and mutamatti' between them; performing tawaf al-ziyarah in the days of sacrifice; the sa'y between Safa and Marwah in the months of Hajj; and its occurrence after a valid tawaf; walking in it for one without excuse; beginning sa'y from Safa; tawaf al-wada'; beginning every tawaf from the Black Stone; walking to the right; walking for one without excuse; purity from both hadaths; covering the awrah; the minimum number of circuits after performing the majority of tawaf al-ziyarah; and avoiding prohibitions such as a man wearing sewn garments, covering his head and face, a woman covering her face, obscenity, sin, argument, killing game, and pointing to it; and from Safa.
Source pages p. 729

Commentary
This passage is a concise listing of the essential components of Hajj. The author states that for a free person, Hajj is valid with four things: ihram and Islam are conditions, then the two pillars (arkan) are (1) standing at Arafat in ihram for any moment between noon of the 9th of Dhu al-Hijjah and dawn of the 10th, provided no intercourse preceded while in ihram; (2) performing most of tawaf al-ifadah (four circuits) after dawn of the 10th. The three remaining circuits are wajib. Then follows a list of wajibat (obligatory acts) that if omitted require a dam (blood sacrifice). These include: initiating ihram from the miqat, staying at Arafat until sunset (the sunnah is to stay until sunset), staying at Muzdalifah after dawn, stoning the jamarat, sacrifice for qarin and mutamatti', shaving or trimming hair in the Haram, performing tawaf al-ziyarah in the days of tashriq, sa'y after a valid tawaf, walking in sa'y if able, beginning sa'y from Safa, performing tawaf al-wada' (for non-Makkans), beginning tawaf from the Black Stone, walking on the right side, purity from both minor and major hadath, covering the awrah, and avoiding prohibitions like wearing sewn garments for men, covering the head/face for men, covering the face for women, obscene speech, sin, argument, and hunting. The commentary adds clarifications: e.g., shaving is an obligation on men, trimming suffices; the order between stoning and shaving is according to Imam Abu Hanifa; walking in tawaf is wajib for those without excuse; purity is on the relied-upon view wajib; covering awrah is also wajib; and the prohibitions are all wajib to avoid, as each requires dam if violated.

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): A pillar of Hajj that is essential; its omission invalidates Hajj.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act of Hajj that requires a dam if omitted, but Hajj remains valid.
طواف الإفاضة (tawaf al-ifadah): The tawaf performed after standing at Arafat and returning from Mina, considered the essential tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A pilgrim completed only three circuits of tawaf al-ifadah and then left Makkah. What is the ruling?
A) Hajj is invalid; must repeat everything.
B) Hajj is valid but a dam is required.
C) Hajj is valid without any compensation.
D) A dam is required for each missing circuit.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, Hajj has two pillars (standing at Arafat and most of tawaf al-ifadah) that are essential for validity, and many wajibat that require a dam if omitted but do not invalidate the Hajj.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Conditions, Pillars, and Obligations of Hajj (Hanafi)
Lists conditions, pillars, and wajibat of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions, two pillars, and list at least five wajibat of Hajj according to the Hanafi school, and apply the distinction between rukn and wajib by explaining the consequence of omitting each.

Core Idea
Hajj has two conditions and two pillars; the wajibat are many and omission of any wajib requires a dam (blood offering).

The performance of Hajj is a once-in-a-lifetime obligation for every free, sane, mature Muslim who has the means. But what makes Hajj valid? This lesson unpacks the foundational elements: the conditions that must be present, the two pillars that are the backbone of the pilgrimage, and the numerous wajibat that ensure its completeness. Understanding this taxonomy is essential for every Hanafi student, as the consequence of missing a condition vs. a pillar vs. a wajib differs dramatically.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish conditions from pillars from wajibat
Identify what is a precondition for validity (shart), what is an integral that invalidates if omitted (rukn), and what is obligatory but not invalidating (wajib). The source text lists them explicitly.
Conditions: ihram and Islam. Pillars: wuquf at Arafat and majority of tawaf al-ifadah.
2
Examine the first pillar: Wuquf at Arafat
Note the time frame (from zawal on 9th to dawn of 10th), the state (in ihram), and the prohibition of intercourse before it. Missing this pillar invalidates Hajj.
The minimum is a moment of presence.
3
Examine the second pillar: Tawaf al-Ifadah
Understand that the pillar is the majority of the seven circuits (four circuits). The remaining three are wajib, not rukn.
If one misses the majority, Hajj is invalid; if one misses a wajib circuit, a dam is required.
4
List the wajibat of Hajj
Scan the passage and extract all acts labeled as wajib: ihram from miqat, extending wuquf to sunset, standing at Muzdalifah, ramy, slaughter (for qarin/mutamatti'), halq/taqsir in the Haram, order of days, etc.
The hashya states: 'whatever requires blood for its omission is wajib' – a key principle.
5
Apply the rukn vs. wajib distinction
Given a scenario, determine whether the Hajj is valid and what compensation is needed. For example, missing a wajib circuit of tawaf requires dam; missing the majority requires repeating Hajj.
This distinction is uniquely Hanafi and critical for fatwa.
