وحصوله بعد طواف معتد به والمشي فيه لمن لا عذر له، وبداءة السعي من الصفا وطواف الوداع، وبداءة كل طواف بالبيت من الحجر الأسود، والتيامن فيه، والمشي فيه لمن لا عذر له والطهارة من الحدثين، وستر العورة، وأقل الأشواط بعد فعل الأكثر من طواف الزيارة، وترك المحظورات كلبس الرجل المخيط، وستر رأسه ووجهه وستر المرأة وجهها والرفث والفسوق والجدال، وقتل الصيد والإشارة إليه، من الصفا قال : أنه شرط الأداء، أوجب عليها جميع ذلك قوله : (وهما شرطان) أي للصحة. قوله: (بشرط عدم الجماع قبله محرماً) فإن فعل ذلك فسد حجه وعليه أن يمضي فيه كالصحيح، وأن يقضي من قابل قوله : (هو أكثر طواف الإفاضة) وهو أربعة أشواط والثلاثة الباقية واجبة يجبر تركها بالدم قوله : وهو ما بعد طلوع فجر النحر إلى آخر العمر، والواجب فعله أيام النحر . قوله : ( إلى الغروب الغاية داخلة في المغيالان الواجب إدراك لحظة من الليل إن وقف نهاراً. قوله : ( والحلق أي أو التقصير قوله : ( وتخصيصه) أي الحلق. قوله : (وتقديم الرمي) أي عند الإمام . قوله : ( بينهما) أي بين الرمي والحلق فهو على ترتيب حروف ردح. قوله: (وحصوله أي السعي قوله : ( وبداءة السعي من الصفا، فلو بدأ بالمروة لا يعتد بالشوط الأول في الأصح قوله : (وطواف الوداع) أي للآفاقي . قوله : (وبداءة كل طواف بالبيت من الحجر الأسود) قيل : فرض للمواظبة ، وقيل : سنة . قوله : ( والطهارة من الحدثين) على المذهب قيل : والخبثية من ثوب وبدن ومكان طواف والأكثر على إنها سنة مؤكد. قوله : وستر العورة) وبكشف ربع العضو فأكثر يجب الدم، ومن الواجب صلاة ركعتين لكل أسبوع من أي طواف كان فلو تركها هل عليه دم؟ قيل : نعم فيوصي به ومنه كون الطواف وراء الحطيم. قوله: (وترك المحظورات الخ) الضابط أن كل ما يجب بتركه دم فهو واجب. قوله: (كلبس الرجل المخيط) وجاز للمرأة. قوله : (وستر رأسه) هو وما بعده بالجر بالعطف على لبس قوله: (والرفث) ذكر الجماع بحضرة النساء قوله : ( والفسوق) أي الخروج عن طاعة الله فإنه من المحرم أشنع قوله : ( والجدال) أي المخاصمة مع المكارين والرفقة. قوله: والإشارة) أي في الحاضر.
Book of Hajj. According to the fatwa, the performance of the obligatory Hajj is valid with four things for a free person: ihram and Islam, and they are two conditions, then performing its two pillars: standing in ihram at Arafat for a moment from the decline of the sun on the ninth of Dhu al-Hijjah until the dawn of the day of sacrifice, with the condition of no intercourse before it in ihram. The second pillar is the majority of tawaf al-ifadah in its time, which is after the dawn of the day of sacrifice. And the obligations (wajibat) of Hajj: initiating ihram from the miqat, extending the standing at Arafat until sunset, standing at Muzdalifah after the dawn of the day of sacrifice and before sunrise, stoning the jamarat, slaughtering for the qarin and mutamatti', shaving or trimming the hair, and designating it (shaving) within the Haram and on the days of sacrifice, and preceding the stoning over shaving, and slaughtering the qarin and mutamatti' between them, and performing tawaf al-ziyarah on the days of sacrifice, and sa'i between Safa and Marwah in the months of Hajj, and its occurrence after a valid tawaf, and walking in it for one without an excuse, and beginning sa'i from Safa, and tawaf al-wada' (farewell tawaf), and beginning every tawaf around the House from the Black Stone, and making tawaf on the right side, and walking in it for one without an excuse, and ritual purity from both hadaths (minor and major impurities), and covering the private parts, and the minimum number of circuits after performing the majority of tawaf al-ziyarah, and avoiding prohibited things such as a man wearing sewn garments, covering his head and face, a woman covering her face, obscene speech, disobedience, argumentation, hunting game, and pointing to it (in the presence of game). From Safa, the commentator said: It is a condition of performance, and it is obligatory upon her all that. His saying: (They are two conditions) meaning for validity. His saying: (With the condition of no intercourse before it in ihram) if he does that, his Hajj is invalidated and he must continue in it like one valid, and make it up the next year. His saying: (It is the majority of tawaf al-ifadah) which is four circuits, and the remaining three are obligatory (wajib), and their omission is compensated by blood. His saying: And it is after the dawn of the day of sacrifice until the end of one's life, and the obligatory is to do it on the days of sacrifice. His saying: (Until sunset) the end is included because the obligation is to attain a moment of the night if one stood during the day. His saying: (And shaving) meaning or trimming. His saying: (And designating it) meaning shaving. His saying: (And preceding the stoning) meaning according to Imam Abu Hanifa. His saying: (Between them) meaning between stoning and shaving, so it is in the order of the letters of 'ردح'. His saying: (And its occurrence) meaning sa'i. His saying: (And beginning sa'i from Safa), so if he begins from Marwah, the first circuit is not counted in the soundest view. His saying: (And tawaf al-wada') meaning for the one from distant lands. His saying: (And beginning every tawaf around the House from the Black Stone) it is said it is fard due to constancy, and it is said it is sunnah. His saying: (And ritual purity from both hadaths) according to the madhhab, it is said (and impurity) from clothes, body, and place of tawaf, and the majority hold it is a confirmed sunnah. His saying: (And covering the private parts) and if a quarter of a limb or more is exposed, blood (dam) is obligatory. And among the obligations is praying two rak'ahs for each sebu' of any tawaf; if one omits it, is there blood? It is said yes, he should make a bequest for it. And among them is that the tawaf be behind al-Hatim. His saying: (And avoiding prohibited things etc.) the principle is that whatever requires blood for its omission is obligatory. His saying: (Such as a man wearing sewn garments) and it is permissible for a woman. His saying: (And covering his head) it and what follows are in the genitive case as an appendage to 'wearing'. His saying: (And obscene speech) mention of intercourse in the presence of women. His saying: (And disobedience) meaning exiting from obedience to Allah, for it is more heinous from a pilgrim. His saying: (And argumentation) meaning disputing with the camel drivers and companions. His saying: (And pointing to it) meaning to game in its presence.
Source pages p. 729

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling statement from the Hanafi school regarding the essential elements of Hajj. It begins by stating that the valid performance of obligatory Hajj for a free person requires four things: two conditions (ihram and Islam) and two pillars (arkan). The two pillars are: (1) standing at Arafat for at least a moment within the specified time from the afternoon of the 9th of Dhu al-Hijjah to before dawn of the day of sacrifice, while in the state of ihram and without having had intercourse before the standing; and (2) performing the majority (four circuits) of tawaf al-ifadah after the dawn of the day of sacrifice. The passage then lists many wajibat (obligatory acts) of Hajj, such as initiating ihram from the miqat, extending the standing at Arafat until sunset, standing at Muzdalifah after dawn, stoning the Jamarat, slaughter for qarin and mutamatti', shaving/trimming hair within the Haram and on the days of sacrifice, and ordering certain acts. The hashya (marginal commentary) explains each point: e.g., the two conditions are for validity; if intercourse occurs before standing, the Hajj is invalid but must be continued and repeated next year; the majority of tawaf al-ifadah is four circuits (the remaining three are wajib, requiring blood for omission); the time for the wajibat; and that omission of any wajib requires release of a blood offering (dam). The principle is stated: whatever requires blood for its omission is obligatory. The passage also details supererogatory sunnah acts in later portions.

Key Terms
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, initiated by intention and recitation of talbiyah, involving prohibitions on certain actions.
الوقوف بعرفات (al-wuquf bi-Arafat): The act of standing (or being present) at the plain of Arafat on the 9th of Dhu al-Hijjah; it is the first pillar of Hajj.
طواف الإفاضة (tawaf al-ifadah): The principal circumambulation of the Kaaba performed after standing at Arafat, on the day of sacrifice or thereafter. Its majority (four rounds) is a pillar; the remaining three are wajib.
الواجب (al-wajib): An obligatory element whose omission does not invalidate the act but requires compensatory blood (dam).
الركن (al-rukn): A pillar integral to the act; omission invalidates the act entirely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a pilgrim performs only three circuits of tawaf al-ifadah?
A) The Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The Hajj is valid but a dam is required.
C) The Hajj is valid and no compensation is needed.
D) The Hajj is valid but the three circuits must be made up later without dam.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school divides the elements of Hajj into conditions (shurut), pillars (arkan), and obligations (wajibat); conditions must be present, pillars are essential, and wajibat are obligatory but not invalidating, compensated by dam.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Sunnah Acts of Hajj and Their Details
Enumeration of recommended acts with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah acts of Hajj according to the Hanafi school and explain the specific conditions and details for each, such as ghusl, idtiba', ramal, and harwalah.

Core Idea
The sunnah acts of Hajj are many; knowing them brings completeness to the pilgrimage.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi enumerates the recommended (sunnah) acts of Hajj according to the Hanafi school. These acts, though not obligatory, carry great reward and reflect the Prophetic practice. The commentary explains the details and conditions for each, such as who performs which act and when. Understanding these sunnan helps a pilgrim maximize the spiritual benefit of the Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah acts listed
Read through the initial list of sunnan from ghusl to frequent tawaf. Note the range of acts covering purification, attire, prayer, talbiyah, entering Mecca, tawaf, and sa'i.
The list includes both preparatory and ritual acts.
2
Understand the conditions and exceptions
For each sunnah, note the specific conditions. For example, ghusl is recommended even for menstruating women, ramal is only for men and only in the first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum if sa'i follows, and idtiba' is performed before tawaf.
Conditions often relate to gender, timing, and sequence.
3
Note the intra-madhhab difference on perfume
The commentary states that applying perfume that leaves a trace after ihram is allowed according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees. Recognize this as a valid ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that of the majority.
4
Distinguish between acts for men only and acts for both genders
Some sunnan like idtiba', ramal, and harwalah are specified for men only. Women do not perform these. Other acts like ghusl, talbiyah, and supplication apply to both.
This distinction is important for correct practice.
5
Recognize the sunnah as non-obligatory but recommended
These are sunnan, not wajib. Omission does not invalidate the Hajj but loses reward. The commentary emphasizes that performing them with proper intention attains perfect reward.
The ruling level is sunnah; missing them is not sinful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسنن الحج منها الاغتسال ولو لحائض ونفساء، أو الوضوء إذا أراد الإحرام، ولبس إزار ورداء جديدين ،أبيضين والتطيب وصلاة ركعتين والإكثار من التلبية بعد الإحرام رافعاً بها صوته متى صلى، أو علا شرفاً أو هبط وادياً، أو لقي ركباً وبالأسحار وتكريرها كلما أخذ فيها، والصلاة على النبي ، وسؤال الجنة وصحبة الأبرار، والإستعاذة من النار والغسل لدخول مكة ودخولها من باب المعلاة نهاراً، والتكبير والتهليل تلقاء البيت الشريف والدعاء بما أحب عند رؤيته، وهو مستجاب، وطواف القدوم ولو في غير أشهر الحج والاضطباع فيه والرمل إن سعى بعده في أشهر الحج والهرولة فيما بين الميلين الأخضرين للرجال والمشي على هيئة في باقي السعي وقوله : أبيضين هو أفضل من لون آخر وهذا بيان للسنة وإلا فستر العورة كاف. قوله : ( والتطيب) أي لبدنه لا ثوبه وله أن يتطيب بما تبقى عينه بعد الإحرام خلافاً لمحمد قوله: (وصلاة ركعتين) ينوي فيهما سنة الأحرام ليحرز فضيلة السنة يقرأ فيهما بالكافرون، والإخلاص لحديث، ورد بذلك ولما فيهما من البراءة عن الشرك، وتحقيق التوحيد، ويقول بعد الصلاة: اللهم إني أريد الحج، أو العمرة، أو الحج والعمرة، فيسرهما لي وتقبلهما مني وفي الأفراد يفرد. قوله: (رافعاً بها صوته) أي رفعاً وسطاً قوله : (وتكريرها أي ثلاثاً، وقوله كلما أخذ فيها أي شرع فيها. قوله : (والصلاة) عطف على التلبية . قوله: (وصحبة الأبرار) أي في جنة النعيم. قوله: (ودخولها من باب المعلاة) أي من ثنية كداء بالفتح والمد الثنية العليا بأعلى مكة عند المقبرة، ولا ينصرف للعلمية، والتأنيث وتسمى تلك الجهة المعلى ا هـ مصباح ذكره السيد وفي نسخ المعلى، وهو الأولى، وترك الحاج ذلك في هذه الأيام. قوله والتكبير والتهليل) أي حين مشاهدة البيت المكرم، ومعناه الله أكبر من الكعبة والتوحيد لئلا يقع نوع شرك در قوله: (وطواف القدوم) أي للآفاقي قوله: (والاضطباع) هو أن يجعل قبل شروعه فيه رداءه تحت إبطه الأيمن ملقياً طرفه على كتفه الأيسر وهو سنة. قوله: (والرمل) هو المشي بسرعة مع تقارب الخطأ، وهز الكتفين في الثلاثة الأول استناناً، فلو تركه أو نسيه في الثلاثة الأول لم يرمل في الباقي، ولو زحمه الناس، وقف حتى يجد فرجة قوله : (إن سعى بعده) فظاهره أنه لا يطلب الرمل في طواف القدوم إلا لمن أراد السعي بعده، وسيأتي له ذلك في الفصل الآتي. قوله: (الميلين الأخضرين المتخذين في جدار البيت. قوله : (للرجال) راجع إلى الرمل والهرولة. قوله :
And the sunan (recommended acts) of Hajj include: taking a bath (ghusl) even for a menstruating woman or one with postnatal bleeding, or ablution (wudu) when one intends ihram; wearing a new white waist-wrapper and cloak; applying perfume; praying two rak'ahs; proclaiming the talbiyah frequently after ihram, raising one's voice with it when he has prayed, or when he ascends a hill, descends a valley, or meets a group of riders, and at dawn; repeating it three times whenever he starts it; sending blessings upon the Prophet; asking for Paradise and the company of the righteous; seeking refuge from the Fire; taking a bath for entering Mecca; entering it from Bab al-Ma'la during the day; pronouncing takbir and tahlil towards the noble House; supplicating as he wishes when seeing it, and it is answered; tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf) even outside the months of Hajj; performing idtiba' (exposing the right shoulder) in it; and ramal (quick walking with shoulder movements) if he intends to do sa'i afterwards during the months of Hajj; and brisk walking (harwalah) between the two green markers for men, and walking normally in the rest of sa'i; and frequently performing tawaf. His saying: (And pointing to it) meaning in the absence. His saying: (And the menstruating woman and the one with postnatal bleeding) it is for cleanliness, and tayammum is not legislated when unable. He should intend with it (ghusl) to attain perfect reward. The condition for attaining the sunnah is that he enters ihram while in a state of purity (tahara), which is better than wudu. His saying: (And wearing a waist-wrapper and cloak) the first covers the private parts, and the second covers the shoulders, for prayer with them uncovered or one uncovered is disliked (makruh) for example. His saying: (New) as a resemblance to the shroud of the deceased, and they are better than washed ones. His saying: White is better than any other color. This is a clarification of the sunnah; otherwise, covering the private parts is sufficient. His saying: (And applying perfume) meaning on his body, not his garment; he may apply perfume whose trace remains after ihram, contrary to Muhammad's view. His saying: (And praying two rak'ahs) he intends with them the sunnah of ihram to obtain the virtue of the sunnah; he recites in them al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas, according to a hadith related to that, and for the freeing from shirk and realization of tawhid. After prayer he says: O Allah, I intend Hajj or Umrah or Hajj and Umrah; facilitate them for me and accept them from me. In ifrad (Hajj alone), he singles out (the intention). His saying: (Raising his voice with it) meaning moderate raising. His saying: (And repeating it) that is, three times, and his saying: whenever he starts it means begins it. His saying: (And blessing) is an appendage to talbiyah. His saying: (and the company of the righteous) meaning in the Garden of Bliss. His saying: (And entering it from Bab al-Ma'la) meaning from the upper mountain pass of Kada' (with fatha and madd), the upper mountain pass at the top of Mecca near the cemetery; it is indeclinable due to being a proper noun and feminine. That area is called al-Ma'la. The copy has al-Mu'alla, which is more correct. Pilgrims have abandoned this nowadays. His saying: (And takbir and tahlil) meaning when viewing the noble House, its meaning is Allah is greater than the Kaaba and the oneness (tawhid) lest any form of shirk occur. His saying: (And tawaf al-qudum) meaning for the one from distant lands. His saying: (And idtiba') is to place, before beginning it, his cloak under his right armpit, throwing its end over his left shoulder; it is sunnah. His saying: (And ramal) is walking quickly with short steps and moving the shoulders in the first three circuits by way of sunnah. If he omits it or forgets it in the first three, he does not do ramal in the remaining. If people crowd him, he stops until he finds a gap. His saying: (If he intends to do sa'i after it) apparently ramal in the arrival tawaf is only requested for one who intends to do sa'i afterwards; this will come in the next chapter. His saying: (The two green markers) placed in the wall of the House. His saying: (For men) refers to ramal and harwalah.
Source pages p. 730

Commentary
This passage lists the sunnah (recommended) acts of Hajj as per the Hanafi school. These include both acts before and during Hajj such as ghusl or wudu before ihram even for women with menses or postpartum bleeding, wearing new white garments, applying perfume that remains after ihram, praying two rak'ahs with specific surahs, frequent talbiyah with moderate voice, repeating it thrice, and supplications at seeing the Kaaba. Details include entering Mecca from Bab al-Ma'la, performing tawaf al-qudum even outside Hajj months, and for men: idtiba' (uncovering the right shoulder), ramal (brisk walking) in the first three circuits of tawaf if sa'i follows, and harwalah (quick walking) between the two green markers during sa'i. The hashiya explains each point: e.g., ghusl is for cleanliness but tayammum is not allowed; the new white garments are likened to a shroud; perfume should be applied only to the body not clothes, contravening Muhammad's view; the two rak'ahs are intended as sunnat al-ihram with recitation of al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas; ramal is for men only; if forgotten in first three circuits, it is not made up later; tawaf al-qudum with idtiba' and ramal are only recommended if one will do sa'i afterwards. These are all considered sunnah, meaning meritorious but not obligatory; omission does not require compensation.

Key Terms
الاضطباع (al-idtiba'): To put the upper garment (rida') under the right armpit and throw its end over the left shoulder, exposing the right arm from behind.
الرمل (al-ramal): Brisk walking with short steps and moving the shoulders, performed in the first three circuits of tawaf by men if they intend to do sa'i afterwards.
الهرولة (al-harwalah): A fast walk (between running and normal walking) performed by men between the two green pillars in the sa'i between Safa and Marwah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is ramal (quick walking with shoulder movements) recommended in tawaf?
A) In every tawaf for both men and women.
B) Only in tawaf al-qudum for men if they intend to perform sa'i afterwards.
C) In all tawafs for men only.
D) Only in tawaf al-ifadah for men.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah acts of Hajj, though non-obligatory, are numerous and come with specific conditions; understanding them enhances the pilgrim's worship and brings the reward of following the Prophet's practice.

Sunan of Ihram: Ghusl, Clothing, Perfume, and Talbiyah
Lists the sunan acts for ihram with hashiya explanations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunan acts of ihram, explain their legal status (sunnah muakkadah), and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding applying perfume before ihram.

Core Idea
The sunan of ihram prepare the pilgrim; they are recommended, not obligatory.

The legislated acts of Hajj include recommended practices that elevate the worship. This lesson examines the sunan (recommended acts) related to entering the state of ihram, as detailed in the Hanafi tradition. We will see which acts are considered sunnah, their conditions, and a notable internal difference among the Hanafi imams about perfume.

Guided Path
1
Identify each sunnah act
Scan the passage and list all acts described as sunan: ghusl/wudu, wearing a new white waistcloth and cloak, applying perfume, praying two rak'ahs, reciting talbiyah loudly, repeating it, and the related supplications.
2
Understand the ruling level and consequence
All these acts are sunnah muakkadah. Omitting them does not invalidate the ihram or the Hajj, but one loses reward. Note that ghusl is even prescribed for those in ritual impurity (menstruating, postnatal) for cleanliness.
The sunnah status means it is recommended, not obligatory.
3
Analyse the detail on ghusl and purity
The commentary clarifies that ghusl is for purification, and if water is unavailable, tayammum is not prescribed for this sunnah. The condition for attaining the sunnah is to be in a state of purity when entering ihram.
Purity is a condition for the sunnah, not a pillar of ihram.
4
Examine the perfume dispute
The text mentions that applying perfume to the body (not garment) is sunnah. However, there is an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa allows applying perfume whose trace remains after ihram, while Muhammad prohibits it. The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's.
Refer to the Hanafi Position Box for details.
5
Recognize the overall fiqh framework
These sunan are preparatory and devotional. They show the importance of physical cleanliness, dignified attire, and spiritual readiness before entering the sacred state.
The sunan are based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ.

والدلالة عليه وسنن الحج منها الاغتسال ولو لحائض ونفساء، أو الوضوء إذا أراد الإحرام، ولبس إزار ورداء جديدين ،أبيضين والتطيب وصلاة ركعتين والإكثار من التلبية بعد الإحرام رافعاً بها صوته متى صلى، أو علا شرفاً أو هبط وادياً، أو لقي ركباً وبالأسحار وتكريرها كلما أخذ فيها، والصلاة على النبي ، وسؤال الجنة وصحبة الأبرار، والإستعاذة . النار قوله: (والدلالة عليه أي في الغائب . قوله : (والحائض ونفساء فهو للنظافة والتيمم ) عند العجز ليس بمشروع وينوي به الإحرام ليحصل الأجر التام، وشرط لنيل السنة أن يحرم ، وهو على طهارة، وهو أفضل الوضوء قوله : ( ولبس إزار ورداء) أولهما الستر العور، من وثانيهما الستر الكتفين، فإنّ الصلاة مع كشفهما، أو كشف أحدهما مكروهة مثلا علي قوله : (جديدين) تشبيهاً بكفن الميت وهما أفضل من الغسيلين وقوله : أبيضين هو أفضل من لون آخر وهذا بيان للسنة وإلا فستر العورة كاف. قوله : ( والتطيب) أي لبدنه لا ثوبه وله أن يتطيب بما تبقى عينه بعد الإحرام خلافاً لمحمد قوله: (وصلاة ركعتين) ينوي فيهما سنة الأحرام ليحرز فضيلة السنة يقرأ فيهما بالكافرون، والإخلاص لحديث، ورد بذلك ولما فيهما من البراءة عن الشرك، وتحقيق التوحيد، ويقول بعد الصلاة: اللهم إني أريد الحج، أو العمرة، أو الحج والعمرة، فيسرهما لي وتقبلهما مني وفي الأفراد يفرد. قوله: (رافعاً بها صوته) أي رفعاً وسطاً قوله : (وتكريرها أي ثلاثاً، وقوله كلما أخذ فيها أي شرع فيها. قوله : (والصلاة) عطف على التلبية . قوله: (وصحبة الأبرار) أي في جنة النعيم.
And the indication of it, and the sunan of Hajj include: ghusl even for a menstruating woman or one in postnatal bleeding, or wudu if one intends ihram, wearing a new white waistcloth and cloak, applying perfume, praying two rak'ahs, frequently reciting the talbiyah after ihram raising his voice with it when he prays, or ascends a high place, or descends a valley, or meets a rider, and at dawn, and repeating it whenever he begins it, and sending blessings upon the Prophet, and asking for Paradise and the company of the righteous, and seeking refuge from the Fire. He said: (and the indication of it) meaning for the absent. He said: (and the menstruating and postnatal) so it is for cleanliness, and tayammum is not prescribed when unable to use water. And he intends by it ihram to attain complete reward, and the condition for attaining the Sunnah is that he enters ihram while in a state of purity, and it is better than wudu. He said: (and wearing a waistcloth and cloak) the first covers the private parts, and the second covers the shoulders, for prayer with them uncovered or one of them uncovered is makruh, for example. He said: (new ones) resembling the shroud of the deceased, and they are better than washed ones. And he said: white is better than another color. This is an explanation of the Sunnah; otherwise covering the private parts is sufficient. He said: (and applying perfume) meaning to his body, not his garment. And he may apply perfume whose trace remains after ihram, contrary to Muhammad. He said: (and praying two rak'ahs) intending in them the sunnah of ihram to gain the virtue of the Sunnah. He recites in them al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas due to a hadith reported for that, and because they contain disavowal of shirk and realization of tawhid. And after the prayer he says: O Allah, I intend Hajj or Umrah or Hajj and Umrah, so make them easy for me and accept them from me. And in ifrad he specifies. He said: (raising his voice with it) meaning a moderate raising. He said: (and repeating it) meaning three times, and he said: every time he begins it meaning starts it. He said: (and sending blessings) is conjuncted to the talbiyah. He said: (and the company of the righteous) meaning in the Garden of Bliss.
Source pages p. 730

Commentary
This passage lists the sunan (recommended acts) of ihram as explained by the commentator. The text first mentions ghusl and wudu. The commentator clarifies that ghusl is for the menstruating and postnatal woman as well, for purification. If water is unavailable, tayammum is not prescribed for this sunnah. The key is to intend ihram while in a state of purity. Wearing a new white waistcloth (izar) and cloak (rida') is sunnah; the izar covers the lower body, the rida' covers the shoulders. New white garments are best, resembling the shroud. Perfume is applied to the body, not the garment, and its scent may remain after ihram according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to Muhammad. Two rak'ahs are prayed with the intention of sunnat al-ihram, reciting Surah al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas. After prayer, one says the specified supplication. The talbiyah is recited loudly in a moderate voice, repeated three times, and associated supplications include salawat, asking for Paradise and good company, and seeking refuge from the Fire.

Key Terms
الاغتسال (al-ightisāl): Full body washing with water, here prescribed as sunnah for ihram even for menstruating and postnatal women.
الإحرام (al-iḥrām): The sacred state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, marked by intention and specific prohibitions.
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited repeatedly after ihram.
الإستعاذة (al-istiʿādhah): Seeking refuge with Allah from the Fire, recited after the talbiyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on applying perfume before ihram if its trace remains after ihram?
A) Permissible according to Abu Hanifa, but Muhammad disagrees.
B) It is prohibited according to all Hanafi imams.
C) It is recommended according to Abu Yusuf.
D) It is disliked (makruh) according to Muhammad only.

Key Takeaway
The sunan of ihram are recommended acts that enhance the spiritual state; the most notable dispute is on residual perfume, with Abu Hanifa's view being operative.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
Sunan of Entering Mecca and Tawaf al-Qudum
Describes the sunan for entering Mecca and performing tawaf al-qudum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts for entering Mecca and performing tawaf al-qudum, and identify the conditions under which raml and idtiba' are performed.

Core Idea
The sunnan of entering Mecca and tawaf al-qudum are emphasized practices that enhance the Hajj experience, but their omission does not invalidate the pilgrimage.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi expands on the sunan (recommended acts) associated with entering the holy city of Mecca and performing the arrival circumambulation (tawaf al-qudum). While these acts are not obligatory, adhering to them follows the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and completes the spiritual journey. The commentary clarifies specific details, such as when raml (quick walking) is prescribed and for whom certain acts are recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Sunan of Entry
Go through the passage and list all the recommended acts for entering Mecca: ghusl, entering from Bab al-Ma'ala during daytime, saying takbir and tahlil upon seeing the Kaaba, making dua, and performing tawaf al-qudum.
These are all sunnah muakkadah for the afaqi (pilgrim coming from outside the Haram).
2
Examine the Specifics of Tawaf al-Qudum
Note the additional recommendations within tawaf al-qudum: idtiba' (uncovering right shoulder), raml (quick walking in first three circuits), and quick walking between the two green pillars during sa'y.
Raml is only prescribed if sa'y is performed after tawaf, and only in the months of Hajj.
3
Understand the Conditions and Exceptions
The passage states that raml is only for men, and if a man forgets or is unable to do raml in the first three circuits, he does not make it up later. Also, tawaf is better than supererogatory prayer for the afaqi, but the resident of the Haram has a different priority during the Hajj season.
These conditions highlight the contextual nature of the sunan.
4
Recognize the Commentary's Role
The commentary expands on the base text by explaining terms (e.g., Bab al-Ma'ala, Kada'), clarifying that tawaf al-qudum is for the afaqi, and noting that pilgrims have abandoned some sunan in recent times.
This shows how later scholars preserve and contextualize fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والغسل لدخول مكة ودخولها من باب المعلاة نهاراً، والتكبير من والتهليل تلقاء البيت الشريف والدعاء بما أحب عند رؤيته، وهو مستجاب، وطواف القدوم ولو في غير أشهر الحج والاضطباع فيه والرمل إن سعى بعده في أشهر الحج والهرولة فيما بين الميلين الأخضرين للرجال والمشي على هيئة في باقي السعي والإكثار من الطواف قوله: (ودخولها من باب المعلاة) أي من ثنية كداء بالفتح والمد الثنية العليا بأعلى مكة عند المقبرة، ولا ينصرف للعلمية، والتأنيث وتسمى تلك الجهة المعلى ا هـ مصباح ذكره السيد وفي نسخ المعلى، وهو الأولى، وترك الحاج ذلك في هذه الأيام. قوله والتكبير والتهليل) أي حين مشاهدة البيت المكرم، ومعناه الله أكبر من الكعبة والتوحيد لئلا يقع نوع شرك در قوله: (وطواف القدوم) أي للآفاقي قوله: (والاضطباع) هو أن يجعل قبل شروعه فيه رداءه تحت إبطه الأيمن ملقياً طرفه على كتفه الأيسر وهو سنة. قوله: (والرمل) هو المشي بسرعة مع تقارب الخطأ، وهز الكتفين في الثلاثة الأول استناناً، فلو تركه أو نسيه في الثلاثة الأول لم يرمل في الباقي، ولو زحمه الناس، وقف حتى يجد فرجة قوله : (إن سعى بعده) فظاهره أنه لا يطلب الرمل في طواف القدوم إلا لمن أراد السعي بعده، وسيأتي له ذلك في الفصل الآتي. قوله: (الميلين الأخضرين المتخذين في جدار البيت. قوله : (للرجال) راجع إلى الرمل والهر وله. قوله : وهو أفضل من صلاة النفل للآفاقي، قوله: (وهو أفضل الخ) وعكسه للمقيم بالحرم زمن الموسم، وفي غيره الأفضل له الطواف أيضاً ذكره صاحب البحر.
And ghusl for entering Mecca, and entering it from Bab al-Ma'ala during the day, and saying Allahu Akbar and la ilaha illallah facing the honored House, and supplicating as one wishes upon seeing it, which is answered, and tawaf al-qudum even in other than the months of Hajj, and idtiba' in it, and raml if one performs sa'y after it in the months of Hajj, and quick walking between the two green pillars for men, and walking at a normal pace in the rest of the sa'y, and performing much tawaf. He said: (and entering it from Bab al-Ma'ala) meaning from the mountain pass of Kada' with fatha and madd, the upper mountain pass at the top of Mecca near the cemetery, and it is indeclinable due to being a proper noun and feminine, and that area is called al-Ma'la, end from Misbah, mentioned by al-Sayyid, and in some copies al-Ma'li, which is preferable, and pilgrims have abandoned this in these days. He said: (and saying Allahu Akbar and la ilaha illallah) meaning upon sighting the honored House, its meaning is Allah is greater than the Ka'ba and tawhid, lest some kind of shirk occur. He said: (and tawaf al-qudum) meaning for the one coming from afar (afaqi). He said: (and idtiba') is that before commencing it he places his cloak under his right armpit, casting its end over his left shoulder, and it is sunnah. He said: (and raml) is walking quickly with short steps and shaking the shoulders in the first three circuits as a sunnah; if he abandons or forgets it in the first three, he does not perform raml in the remaining. If people crowd him, he stops until he finds a gap. He said: (if he performs sa'y after it) so its apparent meaning is that raml is not required in tawaf al-qudum except for one who intends to perform sa'y after it, and this will come in the following chapter. He said: (the two green pillars placed in the wall of the House. He said: (for men) refers to raml and quick walking. He said: and it is better than supererogatory prayer for the afaqi. He said: (and it is better etc.) and the opposite for the resident of the Haram during the season, and at other times tawaf is also better for him, as mentioned by the author of al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 730

Commentary
This passage covers the sunan related to entering Mecca and performing tawaf al-qudum. The ghusl for entering Mecca is sunnah. Entering from Bab al-Ma'ala (the upper pass) is sunnah. Upon seeing the Kaaba, one should say takbir and tahlil, and make dua, which is answered. Tawaf al-qudum is sunnah for the afaqi (one coming from outside the Haram), and idtiba' (uncovering the right shoulder) is sunnah during it. Raml (quick walking with short steps and shoulder movement) is sunnah in the first three circuits if one intends to perform sa'y after tawaf. The quick walking between the two green pillars is for men. Tawaf is better than supererogatory prayer for the afaqi, while for the resident of the Haram during the season, the opposite applies.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (ṭawāf al-qudūm): The circumambulation performed upon arrival in Mecca before going to Mina; sunnah for the afaqi.
الاضطباع (al-iḍṭibāʿ): Uncovering the right shoulder by placing the cloak under the right armpit and over the left shoulder during tawaf.
الرمل (al-raml): Walking briskly with short steps and slight shoulder movement during the first three circuits of tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) For the resident of Mecca.
B) For the pilgrim coming from afar (afaqi).
C) For women only.
D) For all pilgrims including residents.

Key Takeaway
The sunan of entering Mecca and tawaf al-qudum are recommended practices that enhance the pilgrimage; they are conditional on the pilgrim's status (afaqi) and the performance of sa'y.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

The Sunan of the Days of Hajj from 7th to 9th Dhul Hijjah
Lists the recommended acts from the 7th to the 9th

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of sunan from the 7th to the 9th of Dhul Hijjah and identify the time and manner for each sunnah.

Core Idea
The Hajj days have prescribed sunan from khutbah to Arafat—following them perfects the pilgrimage.

The passage outlines a series of recommended actions for the key days of Hajj: the 7th, 8th, and 9th of Dhul Hijjah. These include the imam's sermon, the departure to Mina, spending the night there, going to Arafat, and the combined prayer with two sermons. Understanding this sequence helps pilgrims perform the Hajj in accordance with the Hanafi school and gain maximum reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the day and the sunnah
For each day, note the recommended action: khutbah on 7th, departure to Mina on 8th, stay at Mina overnight, then departure to Arafat on 9th.
The khutbah on 7th is one sermon without sitting; at Arafat it is two sermons with a sitting.
2
Sequence the sunan in order
Place them in chronological order from 7th to 9th: Khutbah (7th after Zuhr) → Departure to Mina (8th after sunrise) → Spend night at Mina → Depart to Arafat (9th after sunrise) → Two sermons at Arafat after zawal → Combined Zuhr and Asr → Supplication.
The night of 8th is spent at Mina; the night of 9th is at Arafat (not mentioned but implied).
3
Note the details of each sunnah
For each sunnah, note the specific time and manner: e.g., departure after sunrise, combination of prayers, etc.

And the khutbah after Zuhr prayer on the seventh day of Dhul Hijjah in Mecca, and it is one sermon without sitting, teaching the rituals in it; and departing after sunrise on the day of Tarwiyah from Mecca to Mina, and spending the night there; then departing from it after sunrise on the day of Arafah to Arafat; then the imam delivers two sermons after zawal before Zuhr and Asr combined with advance joining with Zuhr, sitting between them; and striving in supplication, humility, weeping tears, supplicating for oneself, parents, and believing brothers with whatever one wishes of matters of this world and the Hereafter in the two gatherings; and departing with tranquility and dignity after sunset from Arafat; and descending at Muzdalifah, elevated above the valley floor, near Mount Quzah; and spending the night there on the night of Nahr; and spending the nights of Mina in Mina with all one's belongings; and it is disliked to send one's heavy luggage ahead to Mecca at that time; and he should place Mina to his right and Mecca to his left when standing for stoning the jamarat; and being mounted when stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on all days, and walking when stoning the first jamrah which is near the mosque, and the second, and standing in the valley hollow during stoning; and the time for stoning on the first day is between sunrise and zawal, and between zawal and sunset on the remaining days; and it is disliked to stone on the first and fourth days between dawn and sunrise; and it is disliked to stone during the three nights, and it is valid because all nights are attached to the following days, not the night following Arafah so that standing at Arafah on it is valid, and it is the night of Eid, and the three nights of stoning are attached to the preceding days; and the permissible time for stoning is after zawal until sunset on the first day, and by this all times of stoning are known in terms of permissibility, dislike, and recommendation. And from stoning... He said: (and the khutbah) the khutbah is specific to the imam or his deputy. He said: (after Zuhr prayer) and it is disliked before it. He said: (and departing) conjuncted to the sunan. He said: (the day of Tarwiyah) is the 8th of Dhul Hijjah. He said: (to Arafat) via the Dabb route. He said: (combined) is a circumstantial clause of 'Asr. He said: (two sermons) in which he teaches the rituals up to the third sermon, which is standing at Arafah and Muzdalifah, and moving from them, and stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, and slaughtering, and tawaf al-ziyarah, and shaving. He said: (in the two gatherings) relates to 'striving' etc. He said: (and descending at Muzdalifah) and all of it is a standing place except Batn Muhassir, which is known. He said: (near Mount Quzah) with damm and fatha, it is indeclinable due to being a proper noun and having changed the form from Qazih meaning high, and the correct opinion is that it is al-Mash'ar al-Haram. He said: (and it is disliked to send one's heavy luggage ahead) with two fathas, meaning his belongings and servants, and similarly it is disliked for the worshiper to place something like his heavy luggage behind him as it occupies his heart. This is if he is safe leaving it in Mina; otherwise there is no dislike. He said: (at that time) meaning the days of stoning and spending the nights there, and apparent from their words that the dislike is prohibition-level because Umar disciplined for it, and one is not disciplined for a tanzihi disliked act. He said: (which is near the mosque) meaning the mosque of al-Khayf. He said: (which is next to Arafah) meaning it comes after the Day of Arafah.

Commentary
This passage details the sunan of the later days of Hajj. On the 7th of Dhul Hijjah, the imam delivers a sermon after Zuhr. On the 8th (Yawm al-Tarwiyah), pilgrims depart for Mina and spend the night. On the 9th, they go to Arafat after sunrise. The imam delivers two sermons after zawal, combining Zuhr and Asr. Pilgrims should supplicate humbly, weep, and pray for themselves, parents, and believers. After sunset, they depart for Muzdalifah with dignity, spend the night there, then on the Day of Nahr go to Mina. They spend the days of Tashriq in Mina. It is disliked to send luggage ahead to Mecca during this time. For stoning, one should face the jamarat with Mina on the right and Mecca on the left. They should be mounted for Jamrat al-Aqabah but walk for the first and second jamrahs. The times for stoning are specified: the first day between sunrise and zawal, the next days between zawal and sunset. Stoning is disliked before sunrise on the first and fourth days, and disliked during the nights except that it is valid. The commentator explains that the dislike of sending luggage ahead is actually prohibition-level (tahrimi) based on Umar's discipline.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khuṭbah): A sermon delivered by the imam on specific days of Hajj, teaching the rituals.
الرمي (al-ramy): The act of stoning the jamarat (pillars) at Mina with pebbles.
الثقل (al-thiqal): Heavy luggage or belongings; it is disliked (makruh tahrimi) to send ahead to Mecca during the days of Mina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is wajib (obligatory).
B) It is sunnah muakkadah.
C) It is makruh.
D) It is mustahabb.

Key Takeaway
The sunan of the Hajj days from the 7th to the 9th are a recommended sequence that, when followed, complete the spiritual journey.

Times of Stoning and the Ruling on Sending Luggage Ahead
Specifies times for stoning and the dislike of sending luggage ahead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the preferred, disliked, and permissible times for stoning the jamarat and state the ruling on sending luggage ahead during the days of Mina.

Core Idea
Stoning has specific times: first day before zawal, later days after zawal; sending luggage ahead is makruh tahrimi.

The text specifies when it is best to stone the jamarat: on the first day (10th) between sunrise and zawal, and on the following days between zawal and sunset. Stoning at night is disliked but valid. Additionally, sending one's heavy belongings to Mecca during Mina days carries a strong dislike (makruh tahrimi) because Umar disciplined for it. Understanding these details helps pilgrims avoid actions that reduce the perfection of their Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the days of stoning
Stoning occurs on the Day of Nahr (10th) and the three Days of Tashriq (11th-13th). The passage also mentions a fourth day (the 13th) for stoning.
The first day is the 10th; remaining days are 11th, 12th, and 13th.
2
Note the preferred times for stoning
On the first day (10th), the preferred time is from sunrise to zawal (noon). On the remaining days, the preferred time is from zawal to sunset.
Stoning after sunset on the first day is permissible but not preferred.
3
Note the disliked times
Stoning between dawn and sunrise on the first and fourth days is disliked. Stoning during the nights (of the 11th, 12th, and 13th) is also disliked but valid.
The text explains that nights are attached to the following days, so stoning at night is valid though disliked.
4
Understand the ruling on luggage
Sending one's luggage (thiqal) to Mecca during the days of Mina is makruh tahrimi. This is because it implies leaving Mina prematurely. The commentator clarifies that the dislike is prohibition-level because Umar disciplined for it.
If there is a fear of theft, it is not disliked.

Khutbah and the Sequence of Hajj Days (7th–9th Dhul Hijjah)
Explains sunan of khutbah and sequence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunan related to the khutbah and the sequence of departure from Makkah to Arafat according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The khutbah on the 7th teaches rituals; departures and stays are sunnah.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya details the recommended (sunnah) practices of the khutbah and the movements during the Hajj days. Understanding this sequence ensures the pilgrim follows the prophetic model.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunan mentioned
List the sunan practices: khutbah on 7th, departure to Mina on 8th, stay overnight, departure to Arafat on 9th, and the khutbah at Arafat.
These are recommended, not obligatory.
2
Understand the timing of each sunnah
Note that the khutbah on 7th is after zuhr; departure to Mina after sunrise on 8th; departure to Arafat after sunrise on 9th; khutbah at Arafat after noon before combined prayers.
Timing ensures proper sequence.
3
Distinguish the two khutbahs
The khutbah on 7th in Makkah is one sermon without sitting. The khutbah on 9th at Arafat is two sermons with a sitting between them.
The Arafah khutbah is combined with zuhr and asr.
4
Recognize the sequence of locations
Makkah → Mina (8th) → Arafat (9th) → Muzdalifah (after sunset) → Mina (10th onwards).
Staying overnight in Mina on 8th is sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The book of Hajj: It is superior to supererogatory prayer for the one outside the Haram. The sermon after the zuhr prayer on the seventh day of Dhul Hijjah in Makkah, and it is one sermon without sitting, in which the rituals are taught. Departure after sunrise on the day of Tarwiyah from Makkah to Mina, staying overnight there, then departing from it after sunrise on the day of Arafah to Arafat. Then the imam delivers two sermons after noon before the zuhr and asr prayers combined with zuhr in advance, sitting between them. Striving in supplication, humility, weeping with tears, and praying for oneself, parents, and believing brothers for whatever one wishes of matters of this world and the Hereafter in both gatherings. Departure with tranquility and dignity after sunset from Arafat, and descending at Muzdalifah elevated above the valley floor near Mount Quzah. Staying overnight there on the night of sacrifice, and staying at Mina during the days of Mina with all one's belongings. It is disliked to send one's heavy luggage ahead to Makkah at that time. He places Mina to his right and Makkah to his left while standing for throwing the stones. He should be riding during the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah on all days, and walking for the first stoning near the mosque and the middle one, and standing in the valley floor while throwing. The throwing on the first day is between sunrise and noon, and between noon and sunset on the remaining days. Throwing on the first and fourth days between dawn and sunrise is disliked, and throwing during the three nights is disliked but valid because all nights follow the days after them, except the night after Arafah which is the night of Eid, and the three nights of throwing follow the days before them. The permissible time for throwing is from noon to sunset of the first day. Thus all times of throwing are known in terms of permissibility, dislikedness, and recommendation.

Commentary
This passage from Al-Tahtawi's Hashiya expands on the sunan (recommended acts) of Hajj as mentioned in Maraqi al-Falah. The commentator clarifies the details of the khutbah (sermon) on the seventh of Dhul Hijjah in Makkah, which is a single sermon without sitting, teaching the rituals. It also details the sequence of departure from Makkah to Mina on the day of Tarwiyah (8th), then to Arafat on the day of Arafah (9th), where the imam delivers two sermons after noon. The passage then covers the manner of stoning (ramy) the jamarat, specifying the times: on the first day (10th) from sunrise to noon, and on subsequent days from noon to sunset. Throwing before sunrise on the first and fourth days is makruh (disliked), but if done, it is valid. The nights are considered to follow the subsequent days, except the night of Arafah which is the night before Eid. The permissible time for ramy on the first day is after noon until sunset, clarifying the ruling.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The sermon delivered by the imam during Hajj, specifically on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah in Makkah and on the day of Arafah at Arafat.
التروية (at-tarwiyah): The 8th day of Dhul Hijjah, when pilgrims depart from Makkah to Mina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

beginner
6 min
Times of Ramy (Stoning) and Their Rulings
Explains sunan and disliked times for ramy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the recommended, disliked, and permissible times for ramy al-jimar according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ramy on the first day is from sunrise to noon; on subsequent days from noon to sunset; throwing before sunrise is makruh but valid.

This part of the passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya clarifies the sunnah and disliked times for stoning the jamarat. Knowing these timings helps the pilgrim perform the act in the best manner while avoiding disliked actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of time
Sunnah (recommended) time, makruh (disliked) time, and permissible time. The passage specifies each for the first day and subsequent days.
These rulings apply specifically to ramy al-jimar.
2
Understand the timing for the first day (10th Dhul Hijjah)
The sunnah time is from sunrise to noon. Throwing between dawn and sunrise is makruh but valid. Throwing after noon until sunset is permissible (since the text says permissible time for first day is from noon to sunset? Actually it says 'المباح من أوقات الرمي ما بعد الزوال إلى غروب الشمس من اليوم الأول' meaning the permissible time for the first day is from noon to sunset. Wait, that seems contradictory: earlier it said the sunnah time on first day is sunrise to noon, and then it says the permissible time is from noon to sunset. So there is a sunnah time (sunrise-noon) and a permissible time (noon-sunset). Throwing before sunrise is makruh.
The term 'المباح' here likely means 'jā'iz' (permissible), not necessarily equal to mubah (neutral).
3
Understand the timing for subsequent days (11th-12th/13th)
The sunnah time is from noon to sunset. Throwing before noon (i.e., from morning) is not mentioned as sunnah; the passage says 'وكون الرمي في اليوم الأول فيما بين طلوع الشمس وزوالها وفيما بين الزوال وغروب الشمس في باقي الأيام' meaning on first day between sunrise and noon, and on remaining days between noon and sunset. Throwing on the first or fourth days between dawn and sunrise is makruh. Throwing during the nights is also makruh but valid.
The fourth day is the 13th for those staying, or the 12th for those leaving early.
4
Understand the night rulings
The nights are considered to follow the subsequent days (i.e., the night after the day). The only exception is the night of Arafah (night before Eid) which is not considered part of the ramy timings. The three nights of stoning follow the days before them.
This detail clarifies why throwing at night is valid but disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج وهو أفضل من صلاة النفل للآفاقي، والخطبة بعد صلاة الظهر يوم سابع الحجة بمكة، وهي خطبة واحدة بلا جلوس يعلم المناسك فيها والخروج بعد طلوع الشمس يوم التروية مكة لمنى، والمبيت بها ثم الخروج منها بعد طلوع الشمس يوم عرفة إلى عرفات فيخطب الإمام بعد الزوال قبل صلاة الظهر والعصر مجموعة جمع تقديم مع الظهر خطبتين يجلس بينهما والاجتهاد في التضرع والخشوع والبكاء بالدموع والدعاء للنفس، والوالدين والإخوان المؤمنين بما شاء من أمر الدارين في الجمعين والدفع بالسكينة والوقار بعد الغروب من عرفات والنزول بمزدلفة مرتفعاً عن بطن الوادي بقرب جبل قزح، والمبيت بها ليلة النحر والمبيت بمنى أيام منى بجميع أمتعته وكره تقديم ثقله إلى مكة إذ ذاك، ويجعل منى عن يمينه، ومكة عن يساره حالة الوقوف لرمي الجمار، وكونه راكباً حالة جمرة العقبة في كل الأيام وماشياً في الجمرة الأولى التي تلي المسجد، والوسطى والقيام في بطن الوادي حالة الرمي، وكون الرمي في اليوم الأول فيما بين طلوع الشمس، وزوالها وفيما بين الزوال وغروب الشمس في باقي الأيام، وكره الرمي في اليوم الأول والرابع فيما بين طلوع الفجر والشمس، وكره في الليالي الثلاث وصح لأن الليالي كلها تابعة لما بعدها من الأيام لا الليلة التي تلي عرفة حتى صح فيها الوقوف بعرفات، وهي ليلة العيد، وليالي الرمي الثلاث فإنها تابعة لما قبلها، والمباح من أوقات الرمي ما بعد الزوال إلى غروب الشمس من اليوم الأول وبهذا علمت أوقات الرمي كلها جوازاً، وكراهة واستحباباً، ومن
The book of Hajj: It is superior to supererogatory prayer for the one outside the Haram. The sermon after the zuhr prayer on the seventh day of Dhul Hijjah in Makkah, and it is one sermon without sitting, in which the rituals are taught. Departure after sunrise on the day of Tarwiyah from Makkah to Mina, staying overnight there, then departing from it after sunrise on the day of Arafah to Arafat. Then the imam delivers two sermons after noon before the zuhr and asr prayers combined with zuhr in advance, sitting between them. Striving in supplication, humility, weeping with tears, and praying for oneself, parents, and believing brothers for whatever one wishes of matters of this world and the Hereafter in both gatherings. Departure with tranquility and dignity after sunset from Arafat, and descending at Muzdalifah elevated above the valley floor near Mount Quzah. Staying overnight there on the night of sacrifice, and staying at Mina during the days of Mina with all one's belongings. It is disliked to send one's heavy luggage ahead to Makkah at that time. He places Mina to his right and Makkah to his left while standing for throwing the stones. He should be riding during the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah on all days, and walking for the first stoning near the mosque and the middle one, and standing in the valley floor while throwing. The throwing on the first day is between sunrise and noon, and between noon and sunset on the remaining days. Throwing on the first and fourth days between dawn and sunrise is disliked, and throwing during the three nights is disliked but valid because all nights follow the days after them, except the night after Arafah which is the night of Eid, and the three nights of throwing follow the days before them. The permissible time for throwing is from noon to sunset of the first day. Thus all times of throwing are known in terms of permissibility, dislikedness, and recommendation.
Source pages p. 731

Commentary
This passage from Al-Tahtawi's Hashiya expands on the sunan (recommended acts) of Hajj as mentioned in Maraqi al-Falah. The commentator clarifies the details of the khutbah (sermon) on the seventh of Dhul Hijjah in Makkah, which is a single sermon without sitting, teaching the rituals. It also details the sequence of departure from Makkah to Mina on the day of Tarwiyah (8th), then to Arafat on the day of Arafah (9th), where the imam delivers two sermons after noon. The passage then covers the manner of stoning (ramy) the jamarat, specifying the times: on the first day (10th) from sunrise to noon, and on subsequent days from noon to sunset. Throwing before sunrise on the first and fourth days is makruh (disliked), but if done, it is valid. The nights are considered to follow the subsequent days, except the night of Arafah which is the night before Eid. The permissible time for ramy on the first day is after noon until sunset, clarifying the ruling.

Key Terms
الرمي (ar-ramy): The act of throwing pebbles at the three jamarat during the days of Tashriq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Sunnah
B) Makruh but valid
C) Haram and invalid
D) Permissible and recommended

Key Takeaway
Ramy on the first day sunnah time is sunrise-noon; remaining days sunnah time is noon-sunset; throwing before sunrise on first and fourth days is makruh but valid; nights follow subsequent days.

Sunnan of Hajj: Hady, Departure from Mina, and Sacred Rituals
Enumeration of sunan after day of Nahr and beginning of ihram sequence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings (sunnah, makruh, wajib) for Hady, departure timings from Mina, staying at al-Muhassab, drinking Zamzam, and clinging to al-Multazam, and identify the sunnah preparations for ihram.

Core Idea
Sunnan of Hajj: acts that are recommended but not obligatory; missing them reduces reward but does not invalidate Hajj.

This passage enumerates several sunan of Hajj that occur after the day of Nahr. These include the Hady (sacrificial animal), the timing of departure from Mina, the brief stay at al-Muhassab, drinking Zamzam with etiquettes, and clinging to al-Multazam. The passage also begins the chapter on the order of Hajj actions, starting with the sunnah of preparing for ihram. Understanding these helps the pilgrim maximize reward and avoid disliked actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
Go through the passage and note each act mentioned. For each, determine whether the author explicitly labels it as sunnah, or implies a ruling (e.g., staying until dawn of 13th makes stoning wajib).
The phrase 'من السنة' directly indicates sunnah.
2
Analyze the Hady rulings
The Hady is offered by the one doing Ifrad (sunnah to eat from it), and also for Tamattu' and Qiran on the day of Nahr. Eating from supererogatory Hady is also sunnah.
The text says 'ومن السنة هدي المفرد بالحج، والأكل منه' — eating from it is sunnah.
3
Examine the departure from Mina
There are three scenarios: leaving before sunset on 12th (sunnah), staying until sunset (makruh but no penalty), staying until dawn of 13th (stoning becomes wajib).
The phrase 'فلا شيء عليه وقد أساء' indicates makruh tanzihi.
4
Detail the post-Mina sunan
Staying at al-Muhassab for an hour, drinking Zamzam facing the Ka'bah, pouring it on oneself, and clinging to al-Multazam and the curtains are all sunnah.
These are listed after 'ومن السنة'.
5
Note the ihram preparations
The sunnah for ihram includes ghusl, trimming nails, removing hair, using perfume (even if perfumed), and having marital relations before assuming ihram.
The text ends with 'ويلبس' indicating the beginning of the ihram sequence.

It is from the Sunnah: the Hady (sacrificial animal) of the one performing Hajj Ifrad, and eating from it; and from the Hady of supererogation, Tamattu', and Qiran only on the day of Nahr (10th). Like the first, in it the remaining rituals are taught, and it is the third sermon of Hajj. Hastening the departure if he wishes from Mina before sunset on the 12th day; if he stays there until sunset on the 12th, there is nothing on him, but he has done wrong. If he stays at Mina until dawn of the 4th day, stoning becomes incumbent upon him. From the Sunnah: descending at al-Muhassab for an hour after departing from Mina, drinking Zamzam water and drinking one's fill of it, facing the Ka'bah and looking at it while standing, pouring it on one's head and all one's body for what one drinks for matters of this world and the Hereafter. From the Sunnah: clinging to al-Multazam, which is to place one's chest and face upon it, and clinging to the curtains for an hour supplicating as one wishes, and kissing the threshold of the House, and entering it with etiquette and veneration. Then nothing remains upon him except the greatest of acts of worship: visiting the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions; he intends it when leaving Makkah from Bab al-Sabika from the lower hill. We will mention a separate section for visitation if Allah wills. Chapter on the manner of arranging the actions of Hajj: If one wishes to enter Hajj, he assumes ihram from the miqat like Rabigh. He performs ghusl or wudu, and ghusl is more beloved for cleanliness. The menstruating and postpartum woman also bathes if it does not harm her. Complete cleanliness is recommended: cutting nails, mustache, plucking armpit hair, shaving pubic hair, intercourse with spouse, and oiling, even with perfume. He wears...
Source pages p. 732

Commentary
This passage continues the Hashiya's expansion of the sunan of Hajj. It first discusses the Hady (sacrificial animal) for the one performing Ifrad, Tamattu', or Qiran, noting that the one performing Ifrad eats from his own Hady. The third sermon of Hajj is on the day of Nahr. Then it covers the departure from Mina: it is sunnah to hasten departure on the 12th before sunset; if one stays until sunset, there is no penalty but it is disliked. If one stays until dawn of the 13th (4th day), stoning becomes obligatory. The sunnah also includes staying at al-Muhassab (al-Abtah) for an hour after leaving Mina, drinking Zamzam water to fullness while facing the Ka'bah, pouring it over the head and body. Clinging to al-Multazam (between the Black Stone and the door) and the curtains of the Ka'bah is sunnah. Finally, visiting the Prophet's ﷺ grave is the greatest act of worship. The text then begins a new chapter on the sequence of Hajj actions, starting with ihram from the miqat, with emphasis on ghusl and cleanliness.

Key Terms
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal offered during Hajj, required for those performing Tamattu' and Qiran, and recommended for Ifrad.
المحصب (al-muhassab): A place near Makkah, also known as al-Abtah, where it is sunnah to stay for a while after departing from Mina.
الملتزم (al-multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Ka'bah where it is sunnah to press one's chest and face.

Key Takeaway
The sunan of Hajj detailed in this passage—Hady, timely departure from Mina, al-Muhassab, Zamzam, and al-Multazam—are recommended acts that enhance the pilgrimage; neglecting them is not sinful but reduces perfection.

Sunna of Sacrifice (Hady) in Hajj
Lists recommended acts of Hajj including sacrifice and eating from it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunna rulings on offering a sacrificial animal (hady) in Hajj and identify when it is permissible to eat from it.

Core Idea
Offering hady is sunna; eating from it is sunna for voluntary and tamattu'/qiran but forbidden for penalty offerings.

The passage enumerates recommended acts (sunan) of Hajj. Among them is the sacrifice (hady) for the mufrid (individual Hajj), voluntary offerings, and the obligatory sacrifices for tamattu' and qiran. A key distinction is whether the pilgrim may eat from the sacrifice: the sunna allows it for most types, but not for penalty (jinnayat) sacrifices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of hady mentioned
The base text lists hady for mufrid (individual), tamattu', qiran, and voluntary offerings. The commentary adds that the ruling on eating applies only to the day of Nahr for tamattu' and qiran.
2
Distinguish between sunna and penalty sacrifices
The commentary explicitly states that from penalty sacrifices (jinnayat) one does not eat, whereas from voluntary and wajib sacrifices (like tamattu') eating is sunna.
3
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The distinction affects practice: a pilgrim who performs tamattu' or qiran may eat from his sacrifice, but one who owes a sacrifice for a violation may not.
This is a practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) even though no ikhtilaf is present in the text.

Source Text

ومن السنة هدي المفرد بالحج، والأكل منه، ومن هدي التطوع، والمتعة والقرآن فقط يوم النحر مثل الأولى يعلم فيها بقية المناسك، وهي ثالثة خطب الحج، وتعجيل النفر إذا أراده من منى قبل غروب الشمس من اليوم الثاني عشر وإن أقام بها حتى غربت الشمس من اليوم الثاني عشر، فلا شيء عليه وقد أساء وإن أقام بمنى إلى طلوع فجر اليوم الرابع لزمه رميه ومن السنة النزول بالمحصب ساعة بعد ارتحاله من منى، وشرب ماء زمزم والتضلع منه واستقبال البيت والنظر إليه قائماً والصب منه على رأسه، وسائر جسده لما شرب له من أمور الدنيا والآخرة ومن السنة التزام الملتزم وهو أن يضع صدره ووجهه عليه، والتشيث بالأستار ساعة داعياً بما أحب وتقبيل عتبة البيت ودخوله بالأدب والتعظيم ثم لم يبق عليه إلا أعظم القربات، وهي زيارة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه فينويه عند مكة خروجه من من باب سبيكة من الثنية السفلى، وسنذكر للزيارة فصلا على حدته إن شاء الله تعالى .

قوله: (والمتعة والقرآن أي إلا كل منهما قوله : (فقط) أما هدي الجنايات فلا يأكل قوله: (لزمه رميه) وإن قدم الرمي فيه على الزوال جاز فإنّ وقت الرمي فيه من الفجر إلى الغروب، وأما في الثاني والثالث فمن الزوال إلى طلوع الشمس در. قوله: (بالمحصب) بضم فتحتين الأبطح وليست المقبرة منه وهو موضع بقرب مكة يقال له الأبطح ذو حصى والتحصب النزول فيه، وذكر في المبسوط أنه سنة عندنا حتى لو تركه يصير مسيئاً مثلا مسكين . قوله: (والتضلع) أي الامتلاء منه فإنه علامة الإيمان قوله : واستقبال البيت، والنظر إليه) أي حال الشرب. قوله : (التزام) الملتزم) وهو ما بين الحجر وباب البيت. قوله : (والتشبث) أي التعلق بالأستار كالمستجير المتشفع بها والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
And from the sunna: the sacrificial animal for the one performing Hajj individually, and eating from it, and from the sacrificial animal of voluntary offering, and for tamattu‘ and qiran only on the day of sacrifice like the first, in which the rest of the rituals are taught, and it is the third sermon of Hajj. And hastening the departure from Mina before sunset on the twelfth day if he wishes, and if he stays until the sun sets on the twelfth day, there is nothing upon him, but he has done wrong. And if he stays in Mina until the dawn of the fourth day, he is obliged to stone. And from the sunna: descending at al-Muhassab for an hour after departing from Mina, and drinking Zamzam water and drinking one's fill of it, and facing the House and looking at it while standing, and pouring it on his head and all his body because of what he drinks for matters of this world and the Hereafter. And from the sunna: clinging to al-Multazam, which is placing his chest and face against it, and clinging to the curtains for an hour supplicating as he wishes, and kissing the threshold of the House, and entering it with etiquette and veneration. Then nothing remains upon him except the greatest acts of devotion, which is visiting the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions. So he intends it while leaving Mecca from Bab al-Saba’ik, from the lower mountain pass. We will mention for the Visit a chapter by itself, if Allah wills.

[Commentary:] His saying: 'and tamattu‘ and qiran' – meaning each of them. His saying: 'only' – as for the sacrificial animal for penalties, he does not eat. His saying: 'he is obliged to stone' – and if he performs the stoning before noon, it is permissible, for the time for stoning on that day is from dawn to sunset. As for the second and third days, it is from noon to sunrise. His saying: 'at al-Muhassab' – with dammah and two fathahs, it is al-Abtah, and the cemetery is not part of it. It is a place near Mecca called al-Abtah, which has pebbles; al-tahassub means staying there. It is mentioned in al-Mabsut that it is sunna according to us, so much so that if one abandons it, he becomes sinful. For example, a miskin. His saying: 'drinking one's fill' – meaning being satiated from it, for it is a sign of faith. His saying: 'and facing the House and looking at it' – meaning at the time of drinking. His saying: 'clinging to al-Multazam' – it is what is between the Black Stone and the door of the House. His saying: 'and clinging' – meaning clinging to the curtains like one seeking refuge and intercession by them. And Allah, exalted and high, knows best. I seek forgiveness of Allah the Mighty.
Source pages p. 732

Commentary
This passage enumerates recommended acts (sunan) of Hajj. The author lists: the sacrificial animal for a mufrid (one performing Hajj only) and eating from it; the same for the voluntary sacrifice; for tamattu‘ and qiran, the sacrifice is only on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). The three sermons of Hajj: the first on the 7th, second on the 8th, and third on the 9th at Arafah. Hastening from Mina before sunset on the 12th is permissible; delay without stoning is disliked, but after dawn of the 14th, stoning becomes wajib. Staying at Muhassab (al-Abtah) for a short while after departing Mina is sunna. Drinking Zamzam water, especially to one's fill, facing the Kaaba, and pouring it on oneself is recommended because it is a sign of faith. Clinging to al-Multazam (between Black Stone and door) and to the kiswah curtains, supplicating, kissing the threshold, and entering the Kaaba with veneration are all recommended. Finally, the most superior act is visiting the Prophet's ﷺ grave in Madinah, which will be discussed separately. The commentary clarifies details: the time for stoning on the 10th is from fajr to sunset, on the 11th and 12th from zawal to sunset; al-Muhassab is a specific location, and abandoning it is makruh; al-Multazam is defined; and 'clinging to the curtains' symbolizes seeking intercession.

Key Terms
الهدي (al-hady): A sacrificial animal offered in the Haram during Hajj or Umrah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Eating from the sacrifice is sunna except for penalty offerings; always verify the category of the hady before consuming.

Sunna of Departure from Mina (Nafr) and Stoning Times
Lists recommended acts of Hajj including departure from Mina and stoning times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for departing from Mina and the permitted times for stoning on each day.

Core Idea
Hastening departure from Mina before sunset on the 12th is permissible; stoning times vary by day.

The passage addresses the sunna of departing Mina (nafr) and the timings of ramy (stoning). The pilgrim may hasten departure on the 12th before sunset, but if he stays until sunset, he has done wrong (asa'a). However, if he remains until dawn of the 14th, stoning becomes obligatory. The commentary clarifies the stoning windows: on the 10th, from dawn to sunset; on the 11th and 12th, from noon to sunset.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling on nafr (departure)
The base text states that it is sunna to depart before sunset on the 12th. If one delays until after sunset, there is no sin but it is disliked (asa'a). If one stays until dawn of the 14th, stoning on that day becomes wajib.
The 13th is also a day of tashriq; staying beyond the 12th is only permissible if one delays stoning.
2
Identify stoning times for each day
The commentary gives the times: For the 10th (Nahr), stoning is from fajr to sunset; for the 11th and 12th, from zawal (noon) to sunset. Stoning before zawal on the 11th/12th is not valid.
3
Apply the rules to a scenario
A pilgrim who departs Mina after sunset on the 12th without stoning the 13th has done something disliked but no penalty. If he stays for the 13th, he must stone all three Jamarat on that day.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن السنة هدي المفرد بالحج، والأكل منه، ومن هدي التطوع، والمتعة والقرآن فقط يوم النحر مثل الأولى يعلم فيها بقية المناسك، وهي ثالثة خطب الحج، وتعجيل النفر إذا أراده من منى قبل غروب الشمس من اليوم الثاني عشر وإن أقام بها حتى غربت الشمس من اليوم الثاني عشر، فلا شيء عليه وقد أساء وإن أقام بمنى إلى طلوع فجر اليوم الرابع لزمه رميه ومن السنة النزول بالمحصب ساعة بعد ارتحاله من منى، وشرب ماء زمزم والتضلع منه واستقبال البيت والنظر إليه قائماً والصب منه على رأسه، وسائر جسده لما شرب له من أمور الدنيا والآخرة ومن السنة التزام الملتزم وهو أن يضع صدره ووجهه عليه، والتشيث بالأستار ساعة داعياً بما أحب وتقبيل عتبة البيت ودخوله بالأدب والتعظيم ثم لم يبق عليه إلا أعظم القربات، وهي زيارة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه فينويه عند مكة خروجه من من باب سبيكة من الثنية السفلى، وسنذكر للزيارة فصلا على حدته إن شاء الله تعالى .

قوله: (والمتعة والقرآن أي إلا كل منهما قوله : (فقط) أما هدي الجنايات فلا يأكل قوله: (لزمه رميه) وإن قدم الرمي فيه على الزوال جاز فإنّ وقت الرمي فيه من الفجر إلى الغروب، وأما في الثاني والثالث فمن الزوال إلى طلوع الشمس در. قوله: (بالمحصب) بضم فتحتين الأبطح وليست المقبرة منه وهو موضع بقرب مكة يقال له الأبطح ذو حصى والتحصب النزول فيه، وذكر في المبسوط أنه سنة عندنا حتى لو تركه يصير مسيئاً مثلا مسكين . قوله: (والتضلع) أي الامتلاء منه فإنه علامة الإيمان قوله : واستقبال البيت، والنظر إليه) أي حال الشرب. قوله : (التزام) الملتزم) وهو ما بين الحجر وباب البيت. قوله : (والتشبث) أي التعلق بالأستار كالمستجير المتشفع بها والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
And from the sunna: the sacrificial animal for the one performing Hajj individually, and eating from it, and from the sacrificial animal of voluntary offering, and for tamattu‘ and qiran only on the day of sacrifice like the first, in which the rest of the rituals are taught, and it is the third sermon of Hajj. And hastening the departure from Mina before sunset on the twelfth day if he wishes, and if he stays until the sun sets on the twelfth day, there is nothing upon him, but he has done wrong. And if he stays in Mina until the dawn of the fourth day, he is obliged to stone. And from the sunna: descending at al-Muhassab for an hour after departing from Mina, and drinking Zamzam water and drinking one's fill of it, and facing the House and looking at it while standing, and pouring it on his head and all his body because of what he drinks for matters of this world and the Hereafter. And from the sunna: clinging to al-Multazam, which is placing his chest and face against it, and clinging to the curtains for an hour supplicating as he wishes, and kissing the threshold of the House, and entering it with etiquette and veneration. Then nothing remains upon him except the greatest acts of devotion, which is visiting the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions. So he intends it while leaving Mecca from Bab al-Saba’ik, from the lower mountain pass. We will mention for the Visit a chapter by itself, if Allah wills.

[Commentary:] His saying: 'and tamattu‘ and qiran' – meaning each of them. His saying: 'only' – as for the sacrificial animal for penalties, he does not eat. His saying: 'he is obliged to stone' – and if he performs the stoning before noon, it is permissible, for the time for stoning on that day is from dawn to sunset. As for the second and third days, it is from noon to sunrise. His saying: 'at al-Muhassab' – with dammah and two fathahs, it is al-Abtah, and the cemetery is not part of it. It is a place near Mecca called al-Abtah, which has pebbles; al-tahassub means staying there. It is mentioned in al-Mabsut that it is sunna according to us, so much so that if one abandons it, he becomes sinful. For example, a miskin. His saying: 'drinking one's fill' – meaning being satiated from it, for it is a sign of faith. His saying: 'and facing the House and looking at it' – meaning at the time of drinking. His saying: 'clinging to al-Multazam' – it is what is between the Black Stone and the door of the House. His saying: 'and clinging' – meaning clinging to the curtains like one seeking refuge and intercession by them. And Allah, exalted and high, knows best. I seek forgiveness of Allah the Mighty.
Source pages p. 732

Commentary
This passage enumerates recommended acts (sunan) of Hajj. The author lists: the sacrificial animal for a mufrid (one performing Hajj only) and eating from it; the same for the voluntary sacrifice; for tamattu‘ and qiran, the sacrifice is only on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). The three sermons of Hajj: the first on the 7th, second on the 8th, and third on the 9th at Arafah. Hastening from Mina before sunset on the 12th is permissible; delay without stoning is disliked, but after dawn of the 14th, stoning becomes wajib. Staying at Muhassab (al-Abtah) for a short while after departing Mina is sunna. Drinking Zamzam water, especially to one's fill, facing the Kaaba, and pouring it on oneself is recommended because it is a sign of faith. Clinging to al-Multazam (between Black Stone and door) and to the kiswah curtains, supplicating, kissing the threshold, and entering the Kaaba with veneration are all recommended. Finally, the most superior act is visiting the Prophet's ﷺ grave in Madinah, which will be discussed separately. The commentary clarifies details: the time for stoning on the 10th is from fajr to sunset, on the 11th and 12th from zawal to sunset; al-Muhassab is a specific location, and abandoning it is makruh; al-Multazam is defined; and 'clinging to the curtains' symbolizes seeking intercession.

Key Terms
النفر (al-nafr): Departure from Mina after the stoning rites

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On which day(s) is stoning permissible only after zawal (noon) according to the commentary?
A) 10th only
B) 11th and 12th
C) 10th and 11th
D) 10th, 11th, and 12th

Key Takeaway
Hastening departure from Mina on the 12th before sunset is sunna; stoning on the 11th and 12th must be after zawal.

Sunan at Mecca: Muhassab, Zamzam, Multazam, and Kaaba Etiquette
Lists recommended acts of Hajj including staying at Muhassab and Zamzam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the Hanafi sunan related to staying at Muhassab, drinking Zamzam, clinging to Multazam, and Kaaba etiquette.

Core Idea
These acts are sunna muakkadah; abandoning them is disliked but does not invalidate Hajj.

After departing Mina, the passage recommends several sunan: stopping briefly at al-Muhassab (al-Abtah), drinking Zamzam water while facing the Kaaba, pouring it on the head and body, clinging to al-Multazam (between Black Stone and door) and the Kiswah curtains, and entering the Kaaba with reverence. The commentary emphasizes that Muhassab is a distinct location near Mecca and that abandoning it is sinful (i.e., makruh tahrimi). Zamzam drinking is a sign of faith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the location of Muhassab and its ruling
The base text says descending at Muhassab for an hour after leaving Mina is sunna. The commentary clarifies it is al-Abtah, a pebbly area near Mecca, and that abandoning it is sinful (i.e., makruh tahrimi) per al-Mabsut.
2
Understand the etiquette of drinking Zamzam
The sunna includes drinking to one's fill, facing the Kaaba, looking at it while standing, and pouring water on the head and body. The commentary notes that drinking one's fill is a sign of faith.
3
Learn the practice of clinging to Multazam and Kaaba etiquette
The sunna is to press the chest and face against al-Multazam (area between Black Stone and door), cling to the Kiswah curtains, supplicate, kiss the threshold, and enter the Kaaba with respect.

Key Takeaway
Stopping at Muhassab is a stressed sunna; other acts like Zamzam and Multazam are recommended but less emphasized.
