Jinayat in Hajj: Definition and Categories of Penalties
Introduction to the chapter on jinayat, defining and categorizing offenses during ihram and in the Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define jinayah in the context of Hajj, and state the three categories of penalties (dam, sadaqah, and lesser) with their specific rulings.

Core Idea
Every prohibited act during ihram or in the Haram requires expiation; the penalty varies by severity.

This chapter introduces the concept of jinayat (offenses) specific to the state of ihram and the sanctity of the Haram. Unlike criminal jinayat involving hudud, these are violations that require expiation (kaffarah) in the form of animal sacrifice or charity. Understanding these categories is essential for performing Hajj correctly and knowing the consequences of mistakes.

Guided Path
1
Define jinaayah and its scope
Identify the term's origin and its specific application in Hajj: any prohibited act committed while in ihram or within the Haram.
The text clarifies it is derived from 'gathering fruit' but restricted to acts whose prohibition is due to ihram or the Haram.
2
Name the three penalty categories
List the three levels: (1) those requiring dam (sheep), (2) those requiring sadaqah of half a sa' of wheat, and (3) those requiring even less (such as feeding at will).
Dam is the default for major offenses; sadaqah for minor ones.
3
Identify the two exceptions requiring a camel
Recall that dam normally means a sheep, but in two cases a camel (badanah) is required: intercourse after Arafah before shaving, and tawaf al-ziyarah while in a state of major ritual impurity.
These are the most severe violations.
4
Explain multiplicity of penalties
If multiple muhrims kill one game, each owes a separate penalty because the act of each is separate. If non-muhrims kill game in the Haram, the penalty is single because the locus is one.
The distinction is based on the cause of prohibition (ihram vs. Haram).
5
Identify the ruling for applying perfume
A muhrim who perfumes a limb must offer a dam, even if done forgetfully or under duress. The entire body is treated as one limb if done in one session; otherwise separate penalties apply.
This shows the broad scope of acts that require expiation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الجنايات وهي ما يجنيه من شيء أي يحدثه إلا أنه خص بما يحرم من الفعل، وأصله أخذه من الشجر، وهو مصدر وأريد به الحاصل بالمصدر بدليل جمعها، والمصدر لا يجمع منلا مسكين، والمراد هنا خاص منه، وهي ما تكون حرمته بسبب الإحرام، أو الحرم نهر قاله السيد قوله : (منها ما يوجب دماً وقد يجب بها دمان كجناية القارن، والدم حيث أطلق يراد به الشاة وهي تجزىء في كل شيء إلا في موضعين الأول إذا جامع بعد الوقوف بعرفة قبل الحلق، والثاني إذا طاف للزيارة جنباً، أو حائضاً، أو نفساء فإن الواجب في هذين الموضعين البدنة . قوله : (هي نصف صاع من بر كل صدقة في الإحرام غير مقدرة فهي نصف صاع إلا ما يجب بقتل القمل والجراد فإنه يطعم ما شاء ذكره السيد، وأشار إلى ذلك بقوله : ومنها ما يوجب دون ذلك . قوله : ( ويتعدد الجزاء بتعدد القاتلين المحرمين قال في التنوير: وشرحه، ولو قتل محرمان صيدا تعدد الجزاء لتعدد الفعل ولو حلالان صيد الحرم لا لاتحاد المحل قوله : (هي ما لو طيب محرم بالغ عضواً ولو ناسياً، أو جاهلاً أو مكرهاً، وشمل العضو الفم ولو بأكل طيب كثير، وما يبلغ عضوا لو جمع، والبدن كله كعضو واحدان، اتحد المجلس، وإلا فلكل طيب كفارة ولو ذبح ولم يزله لزمه دم آخر لتركه وأما الثوب المطيب أكثره فيشترط
Chapter of Offenses (Jinayat): They are what one perpetrates, i.e., brings about, except that it is specifically limited to prohibited actions. Its origin is from 'gathering fruit from a tree'. It is a verbal noun, and here what is meant is the resulting effect from the noun, as evidenced by its pluralization (since the verbal noun is not normally pluralized). The intended meaning here is specific: those acts which are prohibited due to ihram or due to the Haram. (The author said: From them are those that necessitate a dam (sacrificial animal). And sometimes two dams become obligatory, as in the offense of a qarin. The term 'dam' when used absolutely refers to a sheep, and it suffices in everything except two cases: first, if he has intercourse after standing at Arafah but before shaving; second, if he performs the ziyarah tawaf in a state of janabah or menstruation or postpartum bleeding. In these two cases, the obligatory is a camel. (The author said: It is half a sa' of wheat as charity for every unspecified charity in ihram; it is half a sa' except for what is required by killing lice and locusts, for which he feeds as much as he wishes. (The author said: The penalty multiplies with the multiplicity of the killers if they are in ihram. In al-Tanwir and its commentary, if two muhrims kill game, the penalty multiplies due to the multiplicity of the act; but if two not in ihram kill game in the Haram, they do not multiply due to the unity of the locus. (The author said: It is: if a muhrim perfumes a limb, even if forgetful, ignorant, or coerced, and it includes the mouth even by eating a lot of perfume. What constitutes a limb if collected? The entire body is like one limb if they are in one session; otherwise, for each perfume there is a kaffarah. If he slaughters (the animal) but does not remove it, another dam becomes obligatory for leaving it. As for a garment most of which is perfumed, it is conditional...
Source pages p. 741

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on jinayat (offenses) as they pertain to the state of ihram and the sanctity of the Haram. It defines a jinayah as a prohibited act that one commits, and specifies that the chapter deals with violations due to being in ihram or in the Haram area. The author then presents the key categories: offenses that require a dam (blood money offering from a sacrificial animal), offenses that require sadaqah (charity) of half a sa' of wheat, and offenses that require even less. Details are given: a dam is generally a sheep, except in two major violations – sexual intercourse after Arafah before shaving (which requires a camel) and performing the obligatory tawaf in a state of major ritual impurity (which also requires a camel). The text then discusses the multiplicity of penalties when multiple muhrims participate in killing game; each incurs a separate penalty. Furthermore, it covers the ruling for a muhrim who applies perfume to a limb: it obligates a dam, even if done forgetfully. The body is treated as one unit if the perfuming happens in one session. The passage concludes with the start of a discussion on a perfumed garment. This class outlines the principles of expiation for violations during the sacred state.

Key Terms
جناية (jinayah): A prohibited act committed by a muhrim or within the Haram, requiring specific expiation.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or share) offered as expiation for certain jinayat.
بدنة (badanah): A camel or cow sacrificed as expiation for major violations like intercourse during ihram.
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume; half a sa' of wheat is the standard for unspecified charity expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Jinayat in Hajj are violations requiring specific expiation: dam (sheep), sadaqah (half sa' of wheat), or lesser; the penalty multiplies with multiple perpetrators.

Categories of Jinayat During Hajj and Their Expiations
Defines jinayat and lists acts requiring dam, sadaqa, or less

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the categories of jinayat during Hajj and identify the correct expiation (dam, sadaqa, or other) for each specified violation.

Core Idea
Not every ihram violation requires a dam; many require only charity, some require assessment.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the foundational Hanafi classification of violations (jinayat) during Hajj. Understanding whether an act requires a blood sacrifice (dam), charity (sadaqa), or a lesser expiation is essential for correctly performing Hajj and knowing one's obligations. The author systematically lists acts and their corresponding expiations, with clarifications on thresholds like 'full day' and 'quarter limb'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories of jinayat
Distinguish between violations against the state of ihram and violations against the sanctity of the Haram. Note that the second category applies even to non-muhrims.
This is the opening classification of the passage.
2
Locate the list of acts requiring dam
These include perfuming a limb, dyeing head with henna, oiling, wearing stitched clothing for a full day, shaving a quarter of the head, cupping, removing hair from certain areas, cutting nails of both hands and feet in one sitting, omitting a wajib, and taking the mustache. Each act has specific conditions.
Note the condition 'full day' and 'quarter' as thresholds.
3
Differentiate acts requiring sadaqa
These are the same acts performed to a lesser extent: less than a limb, less than a full day, less than a quarter. Also each nail individually requires half a sa', but accumulation to a dam allows deduction.
The accumulation rule for nails is mentioned: if total equals a dam, one may deduct as needed.
4
Note exceptional acts with multiple or optional expiations
Shaving another's head or cutting his nails gives the choice of slaughter, charity of three sa', or fasting three days. Thick henna requires two dams. Also, for umrah tawaf, only dam applies, not sadaqa.
These exceptions show that not all violations fit the standard pattern.
5
Summarize the legal definitions and clarifications
The passage defines what constitutes 'perfume', 'covering', 'wearing', etc. For example, covering must be customary; carrying a basin is not covering. Also, non-muhrims are exempt if perfume transfers after ihram.
These definitions help avoid misinterpretation of the rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
باب الجنايات
هي على قسمين جناية على الإحرام وجناية على الحرم والثانية لا تختص بالمحرم، وجناية المحرم على أقسام منها ما يوجب دما، ومنها ما يوجب نصف صاع من بر ومنها ما يوجب دون ذلك ومنها ما يوجب القيمة وهي جزاء الصيد ويتعدد الجزاء بتعدد القاتلين المحرمين فالتي توجب دما هي ما لو طيب محرم بالغ عضواً، أو خضب رأسه بحناء، أو اذهن بزيت ونحوه، أو لبس مخيطاً، أو ستر رأسه يوماً كاملاً، أو حلق ربع رأسه أو محجمه أو أحد إبطيه، أو عانته أو رقبته أو قص أظفار يديه ورجليه بمجلس أو يدا، أو رجلاً، أو ترك واجباً مما تقدم بيانه، وفي أخذ شاربه حكومة، والتي توجب الصدقة بنصف صاع من بر وقيمته ما لو طيب أقل من عضو أو لبس مخيطاً، أو غطى رأسه أقل من يوم أو حلق أقل من ربع رأسه أو قص ظفراً، وكذا الكل ظفر نصف صاع إلا أن يبلغ المجموع دماً فينقص ما شاء منه كخمسة متفرقة، أو طاف للقدوم أو للصدر محدثاً وتجب شاة ولو طاف جنباً أو ترك شوطاً من طواف الصدر، وكذا الكل شوط من أقله، أو حصاة من إحدى الجمار، وكذا الكل حصاة فيما لم يبلغ رمي يوم إلا أن يبلغ فينقص ما شاء، أو حلق رأس غيره أو قص أظفاره وإن تطيب أو لبس أو حلق بعذر تخير بين الذبح أو التصدق بثلاثة أصوع على ستة مساكين أو صيام ثلاثة أيام والتي توجب أقل من دماً للزوم الدم دوام لبسه يوماً، وأخرج بالبالغ الصبي فلا شيء عليه، والطيب كل جسم له رائحة طيبة مستلذة، ويتخذ منه الطيب كالمسك والكافور والعنبر، والعود والغالية، وهي المجموع هذه الأربعة، وأخرج بالمحرم الحلال لأنّ الحلال لو طيب عضواً ثم أحرم فانتقل منه إلى مكان آخر من بدنه فلا شيء عليه اتفاقاً، وقيد بالعضو لأن تطييب ما دونه فيه صدقة. قوله : أو خضب رأسه بحناء رقيق أما المتلبد ففيه دمان در قوله: (ونحوه) كشيرج وإن كان خالصاً. قوله: (أو) ليس مخيطاً) أي لبساً معتاداً فلو اتزر به أو وضعه على كتفيه فلا شيء عليه قوله : (أو ستر رأسه أي بمعتاد فلو ستره بحمل إجانة أو عدل فلا شيء عليه . قوله : (يوماً كاملاً) أي أو ليلة كاملة والزائد على اليوم كاليوم وإن نزعه ليلاً، وأعاده نهاراً ما لم يعزم على ترك لبسه عند النزع فإن عزم عليه ، ثم لبس تعدد الجزاء كفر للأول أو لا. قوله : (أو حلق ربع رأسه الخ) أي أزال ربع رأسه أو ربع لحيته . قوله : (أو محجمه) عطف على ربع واحتجم وإلا فصدقة در. قوله: (وفي أخذ شاربه (حكومة أي حكومة عدل كذا في السيد، والذي في التنوير أن فيه صدقة، ولعل مراده بالحكومة أن ينظر العدل ما مقداره من ربع اللحية فيؤخذ من الدم بحسابه . قوله : (بنصف صاع الباء للتصوير أو الصدقة بمعنى التصدق، والباء للتعدية. قوله : (أو طاف للقدوم أو للصدر (محدثاً وفي الفتح ولو طاف للعمرة جنباً، أو محدثاً فعليه دم وكذا لو ترك من طوافها شوطاً لأنه لا مدخل للصدقة في العمرة. قوله : (أو ترك شوطاً من طواف الصدر) عطف على ما تجب فيه Book of Hajj. Chapter of Penalties. They are of two types: penalty against ihram and penalty against the sanctuary, and the second is not specific to the muhrim. The penalty of the muhrim is divided into categories: some require a blood sacrifice, some require half a sa' of wheat, some require less than that, and some require the value which is the penalty for game. The penalty multiplies with multiple muhrim killers. Those that require a blood sacrifice are: if a mature muhrim perfumes a limb, or dyes his head with henna, or oils with oil and the like, or wears stitched clothing, or covers his head for a complete day, or shaves a quarter of his head, or his cupping spot, or one of his armpits, or his pubic area, or his neck, or cuts the nails of his hands and feet in one sitting, or one hand or one foot, or omits an obligatory act from what has been previously explained. And regarding taking his mustache, there is a government assessment. Those that require charity of half a sa' of wheat are: if he perfumes less than a limb, or wears stitched clothing for less than a day, or covers his head for less than a day, or shaves less than a quarter of his head, or cuts a nail. Likewise each nail is half a sa' unless the total reaches the requirement of a blood sacrifice, then he may deduct whatever he wishes from it, such as five separate nails. Or if he performs the arrival circumambulation or the farewell circumambulation while in a state of minor ritual impurity, a sheep is obligatory. And if he performs the farewell circumambulation while in a state of major ritual impurity, or omits one circuit of the farewell circumambulation, likewise for each circuit from its minimum, or one pebble from one of the stoning rituals, likewise for each pebble when it does not reach the day's stoning, unless it reaches it, then he may deduct whatever he wishes. Or if he shaves another's head or cuts his nails, even if he perfumed or wore stitched clothing or shaved due to an excuse, he has the choice between slaughtering or giving charity of three sa' to six poor people or fasting three days. Those that require less than a blood sacrifice are due to the necessity of blood sacrifice for continuous wearing for a day. The minor is excluded, so nothing is upon him. Perfume is every substance with a pleasant, desirable scent from which perfume is made, like musk, camphor, ambergris, aloe, and ghaliya which is a mixture of these four. The non-muhrim is excluded, because if a non-muhrim perfumed a limb and then entered ihram and it transferred to another part of his body, nothing is upon him by agreement. The limb is specified because applying perfume to less than a limb involves charity. His statement: 'or dyes his head with dilute henna' but for thick henna there are two blood sacrifices. His statement: 'and the like' like sesame oil even if pure. His statement: 'or wears stitched clothing' meaning customary wearing; if he wraps himself in it or places it on his shoulders, nothing is upon him. His statement: 'or covers his head' meaning in a customary manner; if he covers it by carrying a basin or saddlebag, nothing is upon him. His statement: 'a complete day' meaning or a complete night, and more than a day is like a day, even if he removed it at night and put it back during the day as long as he did not intend to abandon wearing it at the time of removal; if he intended to abandon it and then wore it, the penalty multiplies as an expiation for the first or not. His statement: 'or shaves a quarter of his head etc.' meaning he removed a quarter of his head or a quarter of his beard. His statement: 'or his cupping spot' is a conjunction to quarter, and if he was cupped then it is charity. His statement: 'and regarding taking his mustache (a government assessment)' meaning assessment by a just person as in al-Sayyid; and in al-Tanwir there is charity involved. Perhaps he meant by assessment that the just person looks at the extent of a quarter of the beard and takes from the blood sacrifice accordingly. His statement: 'with half a sa' the ba' is for depiction or charity in the sense of giving charity, and the ba' is for transitive. His statement: 'or performs the arrival circumambulation or the farewell circumambulation while in a state of minor impurity' and in al-Fath, if he performs the umrah circumambulation while in a state of major or minor impurity, a blood sacrifice is upon him, likewise if he omits a circuit from it because charity does not enter into umrah. His statement: 'or omits a circuit from the farewell circumambulation' is a conjunction to what requires charity. His statement: 'and likewise for each circuit from its minimum' i.e., the farewell circumambulation, and likewise for each circuit of the sa'y. His statement: 'when it does not reach the day's stoning' but if it reaches it or more, then a blood sacrifice. His statement: 'or shaves another's head' whether that other is a muhrim or non-muhrim.
Source pages p. 741

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi on the chapter of penal actions (jinayat) during Hajj. It opens by defining jinayat as violations against either the state of ihram or the sanctity of the Haram, noting that the latter applies even to non-muhrims. The author then categorizes the expiations for a muhrim's violations: some require a blood sacrifice (dam), some require half a sa' of wheat as charity (sadaqah), some require less than that, and some require the monetary value of game. The ruling explains that if two muhrims kill game, the penalty multiplies due to multiple acts. The text then lists specific acts that necessitate a dam: applying perfume to a limb (even a limb includes the mouth), dyeing the head with henna, oiling with oil, wearing stitched clothing, covering the head for a full day, shaving a quarter of the head, cupping, removing armpit, pubic, or neck hair, cutting nails of hands and feet in one sitting, omitting any obligatory act, and taking the mustache (which requires an assessment). For acts less than a limb, less than a day, or less than a quarter, the expiation is half a sa' of wheat per instance, but if the total accumulates to a dam, the person may deduct accordingly. Specific examples include performing the arrival or farewell tawaf with impurity, omitting a circuit, or missing a pebble in stoning. If one shaves another's head or cuts his nails, or acts due to an excuse, he has the option of slaughter, charity, or fasting. The commentator clarifies that the condition of a full day for dam applies only to continuous wearing; a minor incurs no penalty. Perfume is defined as pleasant-scented substances like musk, camphor, etc. Non-muhrims are excused if perfume transfers after ihram. Further clarifications address thick henna (requiring two dams), customary wearing (wrapping does not count), covering the head (carrying an object is not covering), and the definition of a full day or night. The assessment for mustache hair is interpreted as a proportional deduction from the dam. The passage also notes that for umrah, only dam applies, not charity, and that for each circuit or each pebble, the rule applies proportionally. This is a comprehensive elaboration on the types of violations and their corresponding expiations in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
جناية (jinaya): A violation against the state of ihram or the sanctity of the Haram, requiring expiation.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (sheep) required as expiation for major violations of ihram.
صدقة (sadaqa): Charity of half a sa' of wheat (or equivalent) for minor violations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the expiation for a muhrim who wears stitched clothing for less than a day?
A) A blood sacrifice (dam)
B) Half a sa' of wheat (sadaqa)
C) Fasting three days
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The expiation for a jinaya depends on the extent of the violation; a full day, full quarter, or full limb triggers a dam, while less triggers sadaqa.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
15 min
Categories of Penalties for Ihram and Haram Violations
Classifies acts requiring dam, sadaqah, and qimah with detailed conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify ihram and Haram violations into the three penalty categories (dam, sadaqah, qimah) and state the specific conditions that trigger each.

Core Idea
Penalties for ihram violations are graded: full sheep for major acts, half sa' for minor, and market value for damage to game and Haram.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi systematically categorizes the penalties (jaza') for violations committed in ihram or within the Haram. Understanding these categories is essential for correctly applying the fiqh of hajj and umrah. The author distinguishes three types of obligations: a full dam (sheep) for major violations, sadaqah of half a sa' for partial or minor acts, and qimah (market value) for damage to game or Haram vegetation. The commentary refines definitions and conditions, such as what constitutes a 'complete day' or 'customary covering'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Extent
For each violation, determine whether it was done fully (e.g., covering head for a day) or partially (less than a day), as this determines the penalty tier.
Acts like shaving a quarter of the head or more are considered major; less than quarter is minor.
2
Match the Tier to the Penalty
Major/complete acts → dam; partial acts → sadaqah; damage to game/vegetation → qimah. Note accumulation rules: multiple partial acts may combine into a dam.
For example, cutting all nails in one session requires dam; cutting one nail requires sadaqah.
3
Apply Conditions and Definitions
Check if the act was customary, if the person was muhrim, etc. Exceptions include non-muhrim, child, and excused actions.
Perfume transferred after ihram from a non-muhrim: no penalty. Customary covering means normal headwear, not a load.
4
Handle Special Cases
For game and Haram vegetation, two just persons appraise; if value reaches a sacrificial animal, options include slaughter, feeding, or fasting. Predatory animals attacking carry no penalty.
Lice and locusts have lighter penalties; breaking eggs of game requires qimah of the value.

كتاب الحج
بِحِنَّاءٍ، أَوِ اذَّهَنَ بِزَيْتٍ وَنَحْوِهِ، أَوْ لَبِسَ مَخِيطاً، أَوْ سَتَرَ رَأْسَهُ يَوْماً كَامِلاً، أَوْ حَلَقَ رُبْعَ رَأْسِهِ أَوْ مَحْجَمَهُ أَوْ أَحَدَ إِبْطَيْهِ، أَوْ عَانَتَهُ أَوْ رَقَبَتَهُ أَوْ قَصَّ أَظْفَارَ يَدَيْهِ وَرِجْلَيْهِ بِمَجْلِسٍ أَوْ يَداً، أَوْ رِجْلاً، أَوْ تَرَكَ وَاجِباً مِمَّا تَقَدَّمَ بَيَانُهُ، وَفِي أَخْذِ شَارِبِهِ حُكُومَةٌ، وَالَّتِي تُوجِبُ أَوْ قَصَّ ظُفْراً، وَكَذَا الْكَلُّ ظُفْرٍ نِصْفُ صَاعٍ إِلَّا أَنْ يَبْلُغَ الْمَجْمُوعُ دَماً فَيَنْقُصَ مَا شَاءَ مِنْهُ كَخَمْسَةٍ مُتَفَرِّقَةٍ، أَوْ طَافَ لِلْقُدُومِ أَوْ لِلصَّدَرِ مُحْدِثاً وَتَجِبُ شَاةٌ وَلَوْ طَافَ جُنُباً أَوْ تَرَكَ شَوْطاً مِنْ طَوَافِ الصَّدَرِ، وَكَذَا الْكُلُّ شَوْطٍ مِنْ أَقَلِّهِ، أَوْ حَصَاةً مِنْ إِحْدَى الْجِمَارِ، وَكَذَا الْكُلُّ حَصَاةٌ فِيمَا لَمْ يَبْلُغْ رَمْيَ يَوْمٍ إِلَّا أَنْ يَبْلُغَ فَيَنْقُصَ مَا شَاءَ، أَوْ حَلَقَ رَأْسَ غَيْرِهِ أَوْ قَصَّ أَظْفَارَهُ وَإِنْ تَطَيَّبَ أَوْ لَبِسَ أَوْ حَلَقَ بِعُذُرٍ تَخَيَّرَ بَيْنَ الذَّبْحِ أَوِ التَّصَدُّقِ بِثَلَاثَةِ أَصْوُعٍ عَلَى سِتَّةِ مَسَاكِينَ أَوْ صِيَامِ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ وَالَّتِي تُوجِبُ أَقَلَّ مِنْ دَمٍ لِلُزُومِ الدَّمِ دَوَامُ لُبْسِهِ يَوْماً، وَأَخْرَجَ بِالْبَالِغِ الصَّبِيَّ فَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ، وَالطِّيبُ كُلُّ جِسْمٍ لَهُ رَائِحَةٌ طَيِّبَةٌ مُسْتَلَذَّةٌ، وَيُتَّخَذُ مِنْهُ الطِّيبُ كَالْمِسْكِ وَالْكَافُورِ وَالْعَنْبَرِ، وَالْعُودِ وَالْغَالِيَةِ، وَهِيَ اتِّفَاقاً، وَقَيَّدَ بِالْعُضْوِ لِأَنَّ تَطْيِيبَ مَا دُونَهُ فِيهِ صَدَقَةٌ. قَوْلُهُ: أَوْ خَضَبَ رَأْسَهُ بِحِنَّاءٍ رَقِيقٍ أَمَّا الْمُتَلَبِّدُ فَفِيهِ دَمَانِ دَرَّ قَوْلُهُ: (وَنَحْوِهِ) كَشِيرَجٍ وَإِنْ كَانَ خَالِصاً قَوْلُهُ: (أَوْ) لَيْسَ مَخِيطاً) أَيْ لُبْساً مُعْتَاداً فَلَوِ اتَّزَرَ بِهِ أَوْ وَضَعَهُ عَلَى كَتِفَيْهِ فَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ قَوْلُهُ: (أَوْ سَتَرَ رَأْسَهُ) أَيْ بِمُعْتَادٍ فَلَوْ سَتَرَهُ بِحِمْلِ إِجَّانَةٍ أَوْ عِدْلٍ فَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ قَوْلُهُ: (يَوْماً كَامِلاً) أَيْ أَوْ لَيْلَةً كَامِلَةً وَالزَّائِدُ عَلَى الْيَوْمِ كَالْيَوْمِ وَإِنْ نَزَعَهُ لَيْلاً، وَأَعَادَهُ نَهَاراً مَا لَمْ يَعْزِمْ عَلَى تَرْكِ لُبْسِهِ عِنْدَ النَّزْعِ فَإِنْ عَزَمَ عَلَيْهِ، ثُمَّ لَبِسَ تَعَدَّدَ الْجَزَاءُ كَفَرَّ لِلْأَوَّلِ أَوْ لَا‏. قَوْلُهُ: (أَوْ حَلَقَ رُبْعَ رَأْسِهِ الْخَ) أَيْ أَزَالَ رُبْعَ رَأْسِهِ أَوْ رُبْعَ لِحْيَتِهِ قَوْلُهُ: (أَوْ مَحْجَمَهُ) عَطْفٌ عَلَى رُبْعٍ وَاحْتَجَمَ وَإِلَّا فَصَدَقَةٌ دَرْ‏. 6 أَيْ قَوْلُهُ: (وَفِي أَخْذِ شَارِبِهِ حُكُومَةٌ) أَيْ حُكُومَةُ عَدْلٍ كَذَا فِي السَّيِّدِ، وَالَّذِي فِي التَّنْوِيرِ أَنَّ فِيهِ صَدَقَةٌ، وَلَعَلَّ مُرَادَهُ بِالْحُكُومَةِ أَنْ يَنْظُرَ الْعَدْلُ مَا مِقْدَارُهُ مِنْ رُبْعِ اللِّحْيَةِ فَيُؤْخَذَ مِنَ الدَّمِ بِحِسَابِهِ قَوْلُهُ: (بِنِصْفِ صَاعٍ الْبَاءُ لِلتَّصْوِيرِ أَوِ الصَّدَقَةُ بِمَعْنَى التَّصَدُّقِ، وَالْبَاءُ لِلتَّعْدِيَةِ قَوْلُهُ: (أَوْ طَافَ لِلْقُدُومِ أَوْ لِلصَّدَرِ مُحْدِثاً) وَفِي الْفَتْحِ وَلَوْ طَافَ لِلْعُمْرَةِ جُنُباً، أَوْ مُحْدِثاً فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَكَذَا لَوْ تَرَكَ مِنْ طَوَافِهَا شَوْطاً لِأَنَّهُ لَا مَدْخَلَ لِلصَّدَقَةِ فِي الْعُمْرَةِ‏. قَوْلُهُ: (أَوْ تَرَكَ شَوْطاً مِنْ طَوَافِ الصَّدَرِ) عَطْفٌ عَلَى مَا تَجِبُ فِيهِ صَدَقَةٌ قَوْلُهُ: (وَكَذَا لِكُلِّ شَوْطٍ مِنْ أَقَلِّهِ) أَيِ الصَّدَرِ، وَكَذَا لِكُلِّ شَوْطٍ مِنَ السَّعْيِ قَوْلُهُ: (فِيمَا لَمْ يَبْلُغْ رَمْيَ يَوْمٍ) أَمَّا إِذَا بَلَغَهُ أَوْ أَكْثَرَهُ فَفِيهِ دَمٌ قَوْلُهُ: (أَوْ) حَلَقَ رَأْسَ غَيْرِهِ مُحْرِماً كَانَ ذَلِكَ الْغَيْرُ، أَوْ حَلَالاً‏،  مَنْ نِصْفَ صَاعٍ فَهِيَ مَا لَوْ قَتَلَ قُمْلَةً أَوْ جَرَادَةً فَيَتَصَدَّقُ بِمَا شَاءَ وَالَّتِي تُوجِبُ الْقِيمَةَ فَهْيَ لَوْ قَتَلَ صَيْداً فَيُقَوِّمْهُ عَدْلَانِ فِي مَقْتَلٍ أَوْ قَرِيبٍ مِنْهُ فَإِنْ بَلَغَتْ هَدْياً فَلَهُ الْخِيَارَ انْ شَاءَ اشْتَرَاهُ وَذَبَحَهُ أَوِ اشْتَرَى طَعَاماً وَتَصَدَّقَ بِهِ لِكُلِّ فَقِيرٍ نِصْفَ صَاعٍ أَوْ صَامَ عَنْ طَعَامِ كُلِّ مِسْكِينٍ يَوْماً، وَإِنْ فَضَلَ أَقَلَّ مِنْ نِصْفِ صَاعٍ تَصَدَّقَ بِهِ أَوْ صَامَ يَوْماً وَتَجِبُ قِيمَةُ مَا نَقَصَ بِنَتْفِ رِيشِهِ الَّذِي لَا يَطِيرُ بِهِ وَشَعْرِهِ وَقَطْعِ عُضْوٍ لَا يَمْنَعُهُ الِامْتِنَاعُ بِهِ وَتَجِبُ الْقِيمَةُ بِقَطْعِ بَعْضِ قَوَائِمِهِ، وَنَتْفِ رِيشِهِ وَكَسْرِ بَيْضِهِ وَلَا يُجَاوِزُ عَنْ شَاةٍ بِقَتْلِ السَّبْعِ وَإِنْ صَالَ لَا شَيْءَ بِقَتْلِهِ وَلَا يُجْزِئُ الصَّوْمُ بِقَتْلِ الْحَلَالِ صَيْدَ الْحَرَمِ وَلَا بِقَطْعِ حَشِيشِ الْحَرَمِ وَشَجَرِهِ النَّابِتِ بِنَفْسِهِ وَلَيْسَ مِمَّا يُنْبِتُهُ النَّاسُ بَلِ الْقِيمَةُ، وَحَرُمَ رَعْيُ حَشِيشِ الْحَرَمِ وَقَطْعُهُ إِلَّا الْإِذْخِرَ وَالْكَمْأَةَ‏. وَهَذَا بِخِلَافِ مَا لَوْ طَيَّبَ عُضْوَ غَيْرِهِ أَوْ أَلْبَسَهُ مَخِيطاً فَإِنَّهُ لَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ إِجْمَاعاً. قَوْلُهُ: (فَهِيَ مَا لَوْ قَتَلَ قُمْلَةً) مِنْ بَدَنِهِ، أَوْ أَلْقَاهَا أَوْ أَلْقَى ثَوْبَهُ فِي الشَّمْسِ لِتَمُوتَ وَيَجِبُ فِي الْكَثِيرِ مِنْهُ، وَهُوَ مَا زَادَ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةٍ نِصْفَ صَاعٍ وَيَجِبُ الْجَزَاءُ فِي الْقُمَّلِ بِالدَّلَالَةِ عَلَيْهِ كَالصَّيْدِ قَوْلُهُ: (وَذَبَحَهُ) أَيْ فِي الْحَرَمِ قَوْلُهُ وَتَصَدَّقَ بِهِ أَيْنَ شَاءَ قَوْلُهُ: (لِكُلِّ فَقِيرٍ نِصْفَ صَاعٍ حُكْمُهُ كَالْفِطْرَةِ‏. قَوْلُهُ: (أَوْ صَامَ عَنْ طَعَامِ كُلِّ مِسْكِينٍ يَوْماً) وَلَوْ مُتَفَرِّقاً قَوْلُهُ: (أَوْ صَامَ يَوْماً) وَكَذَا لَوْ كَانَ الْوَاجِبُ أَقَلَّ مِنَ الصَّدَقَةِ ابْتِدَاءً قَوْلُهُ: (وَتَجِبُ قِيمَةُ مَا نَقَصَ بِنَتْفِ رِيشِهِ) فَيُقَوَّمُ الصَّيْدُ سَلِيماً وَجَرِيحاً فَيَغْرَمُ مَا بَيْنَ الْقِيمَتَيْنِ وَهَذَا إِذَا بَرِئَ وَبَقِيَ أَثَرُهُ وَإِلَّا فَلَا يَضْمَنُ لِزَوَالِ الْمُوجِبِ. قَوْلُهُ: (وَنَتْفِ رِيشِهِ) أَيِ الَّذِي يَخْرُجُ بِهِ مِنْ حَيِّزِ الِامْتِنَاعِ. قَوْلُهُ: (وَكَسْرِ بَيْضِهِ) أَيْ غَيْرِ الْمُذِرِّ. قَوْلُهُ: (بِقَتْلِ السَّبْعِ الْمُرَادُ بِهِ حَيَوَانٌ لَا يُؤْكَلُ، وَلَوْ خِنْزِيراً، أَوْ فِيلاً. قَوْلُهُ: (النَّابِتِ بِنَفْسِهِ لَكِنْ إِنْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ فِي غَيْرِ مِلْكٍ وَجَبَتْ قِيمَةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ، وَإِلَّا فَقِيمَتَانِ قِيمَةٌ لِمَالِكِهِ، وَأُخْرَى لِحَقِّ الشَّرْعِ، وَتَجِبُ الْقِيمَةُ إِلَّا فِيمَا جَفَّ، أَوِ انْكَسَرَ أَوْ ذَهَبَ، بِحَفْرِ كَانُونٍ، أَوْ ضَرْبِ فُسْطَاطٍ در واعلم أن شجر الحرم أربعة أنواع ثلاثة منها يحل قطعها، والانتفاع بها بلا جزاء وواحدة منها لا يحل قطعها ولا الانتفاع بها بدون الجزاء أما الثلاثة الأول فكل شجر أنبته الناس، وهو من جنس ما ينبته الناس وكل شجر أنبته الناس، وهو ليس من جنس ما ينبته الناس وكل شجر نبت بنفسه، وهو من جنس ما ينبته الناس، وأما الواحدة فهي كل شجر نبت بنفسه، وهو ليس من جنس ما ينبته الناس ذكره السيد. قَوْلُهُ: (وَلَيْسَ) مِمَّا يُنْبِتُهُ النَّاسُ فَلَوْ كَانَ مِنْ جِنْسِهِ فَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ دَرَّ‏. قَوْلُهُ: (وَحَرُمَ رَعْيُ حَشِيشِ الْحَرَمِ أَيْ بِدَابَّةٍ‏. قَوْلُهُ: (وَقَطْعُهُ) أَيْ بِنَحْوِ مِنْجَلٍ قَوْلُهُ: (وَالْكَمْأَةَ) لِأَنَّهَا كَالشَّجَرِ الْجَافِّ وَاللَّهُ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى أَعْلَمُ وَأَسْتَغْفِرُ اللَّهَ الْعَظِيمَ.
Book of Hajj. By henna, or oiling with oil and the like, or wearing stitched [garment], or covering his head for a complete day, or shaving a quarter of his head or his cupping spot or one of his armpits, or his pubic area or his neck, or cutting nails of hands and feet in one session, or a hand, or a foot, or leaving an obligatory act from what has been explained previously, and in taking his mustache there is a valuation. And that which obligates charity [is] half a sa' of wheat or its value: if he perfumed less than a limb, or wore stitched [garment], or covered his head less than a day, or shaved less than a quarter of his head, or cut one nail; likewise each nail is half a sa' unless the total reaches a blood [penalty] then he may reduce any amount from it, like five [nails] scattered; or he performed Tawaf al-Qudum or Tawaf al-Sadar in a state of minor impurity, and a sheep is obligatory, even if he performed Tawaf in a state of major impurity, or he left one circuit from Tawaf al-Sadar; likewise each circuit from the least of it; or a pebble from one of the stonings; likewise each pebble is [half a sa'] as long as it does not amount to the stoning of a day, unless it reaches [that amount] then he may reduce any amount; or he shaved another's head or cut his nails, though he perfumed or wore or shaved due to an excuse, he chooses between slaughtering or giving charity of three sa' to six poor people or fasting three days. And that which obligates less than a blood [penalty] is due to the permanence of wearing it for a day. He excluded the child from the adult, so nothing is upon him. Perfume is every substance that has a pleasant fragrant smell and from which perfume is made, like musk, camphor, ambergris, aloeswood and al-ghaliya, which is the combination of these four. He excluded the non-muhrim from the muhrim, because if a non-muhrim perfumed a limb then entered ihram and [the perfume] transferred from it to another place on his body, nothing is upon him by agreement. He restricted to the limb because perfuming less than that involves charity. His statement: 'or dyed his head with thin henna' as for the matted [hair], then there are two blood penalties. Darra. His statement: 'and the like' like sesame oil, even if pure. His statement: 'or wore stitched' meaning customary wearing, so if he wrapped it as a loincloth or placed it on his shoulders, nothing is upon him. His statement: 'or covered his head' meaning in a customary manner, so if he covered it with a load of a basin or a load, nothing is upon him. His statement: 'a complete day' meaning or a complete night; and what exceeds a day is like a day, even if he removed it at night and put it back during the day, unless he intended to leave wearing it at the time of removal; if he intended to leave it, then wore [again], the recompense multiplies, whether as an expiation for the first or not. His statement: 'or shaved a quarter of his head etc.' meaning he removed a quarter of his head or a quarter of his beard. His statement: 'or his cupping spot' is a conjunction with 'quarter', and he cupped, otherwise a charity. Darra. 6 meaning. His statement: 'and in taking his mustache there is a valuation' meaning a just estimation; thus in al-Sayyid, and what is in al-Tanwir is that there is charity; perhaps his meaning by valuation is that the just person looks at how much of a quarter of the beard it is, and then the blood penalty is taken in proportion. His statement: 'by half a sa'' the ba is for depiction, or charity meaning giving charity, and the ba is for transitivity. His statement: 'or performed Tawaf for arrival or departure in impurity' and in al-Fath: if he performed Tawaf for Umrah in major impurity or minor impurity, then a blood penalty is upon him; likewise if he left one circuit from its Tawaf because there is no place for charity in Umrah. His statement: 'or left a circuit from Tawaf al-Sadar' is a conjunction with that which obligates charity. His statement: 'and likewise for each circuit from the least of it' meaning al-Sadar, and likewise for each circuit from the Sa'y. His statement: 'as long as it does not amount to the stoning of a day' as for when it reaches it or most of it, then a blood penalty. His statement: 'or shaved the head of another' whether that other is a muhrim or non-muhrim. [Page 743] From half a sa': that is if he killed a louse or a locust, then he gives charity as he wishes. And that which obligates value: that is if he killed game, then two just persons appraise it at the place of killing or near it; if it reaches a sacrificial animal, then he has the choice: if he wishes, he buys it and slaughters it, or he buys food and gives it as charity to each poor person half a sa', or he fasts for the food of each poor person one day; and if there remains less than half a sa', he gives it as charity or fasts one day. And the value of what is diminished by plucking its feathers with which it cannot fly, and its hair, and cutting a limb that does not prevent it from escaping, are obligatory. And value is obligatory for cutting some of its legs, plucking its feathers, and breaking its eggs. And it does not exceed a sheep for killing a predatory animal; and if it attacks, nothing is for killing it. Fasting is not sufficient for a non-muhrim killing game of the Haram, nor for cutting herbage of the Haram and its trees that grow by themselves and are not of the type that people plant, rather value. Grazing herbage of the Haram and cutting it are forbidden except idhkhir and truffles. This is contrary to if he perfumed another's limb or dressed him in stitched, then nothing is upon him by consensus. His statement: 'that is if he killed a louse' from his body, or threw it, or threw his garment in the sun so that it dies; and for a large number of them, which is more than three, half a sa' is obligatory. And recompense is obligatory for lice by indicating it like game. His statement: 'and slaughters it' meaning in the Haram. His statement 'and gives it as charity' wherever he wishes. His statement: 'to each poor person half a sa'' its rule is like fitrah. His statement: 'or he fasts for the food of each poor person one day' even if interrupted. His statement: 'or fasts one day' and likewise if the obligatory amount is less than the charity initially. His statement: 'and value is obligatory for what is diminished by plucking its feathers' then the game is appraised sound and injured, and he pays the difference between the two values; this is if it heals and its trace remains, otherwise he does not guarantee due to the removal of the cause. His statement: 'and plucking its feathers' meaning those with which it exits from the state of escape. His statement: 'and breaking its eggs' meaning non-hardened eggs. His statement: 'for killing a predatory animal' what is meant is an animal that is not eaten, even if a pig or an elephant. His statement: 'that grows by itself' but if that is on property not owned, one value is obligatory; otherwise two values: one for its owner, and another for the right of the Sharia; and value is obligatory except for what becomes dry, or broken, or lost due to digging a furnace or pitching a tent. Darra. Know that the trees of the Haram are four types: three of them are permissible to cut and use without recompense, and one of them is not permissible to cut or use without recompense. As for the three first: every tree that people planted and is of the kind that people plant; and every tree that people planted and is not of the kind that people plant; and every tree that grew by itself and is of the kind that people plant. As for the one: it is every tree that grew by itself and is not of the kind that people plant – as mentioned by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'and is not' of what people plant, so if it is of its kind, then nothing is upon him. Darra. His statement: 'and grazing herbage of the Haram is forbidden' meaning with an animal. His statement: 'and cutting it' meaning with something like a sickle. His statement: 'and truffles' because they are like dry wood. And Allah Most High knows best and I seek forgiveness of Allah the Great.
Source pages p. 742

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a super-commentary on Maraqi al-Falah, detailing the categories of penalties (Jaza') for violations of ihram and the Haram. The author first lists acts that obligate a full dam (blood penalty of a sheep): applying henna, oiling, wearing stitched clothes, covering the head for a full day, shaving a quarter of the head or beard, cupping, shaving armpits, pubic area, neck, cutting all nails in one session, or leaving a wajib act. For these, a sheep is due. However, if the act is done partially (e.g., perfuming less than a limb, wearing stitched less than a day, shaving less than a quarter, cutting one nail), the penalty is sadaqah of half a sa' of wheat or its value. An exception: if multiple partial acts accumulate to the equivalent of a full dam, one may reduce the penalty accordingly. Tawaf in a state of impurity (hadath) for Qudum or Sadar requires a sheep; if in janabah, also a sheep. Leaving one circuit of Sadar Tawaf also requires a sheep, similarly for each circuit missing from the minimal requirement. For stoning, missing a pebble below the day's amount is half a sa', but if it reaches a day's worth, a sheep is due. Shaving another's head or cutting their nails, even if done with excuse, gives a choice between slaughter, feeding six poor people three sa', or fasting three days. The commentary clarifies definitions: 'complete day' includes night; 'covering head' means customary covering; 'perfume' includes any pleasant substance like musk, camphor, etc. For a non-muhrim, no penalty for perfume transfer after ihram. For moustache, there is 'valuation' (hukuma) – an estimation of the amount relative to a quarter of the beard, then a proportional blood penalty. The second part covers acts obligating 'value' (qimah): killing game in the Haram or by a muhrim requires appraisal by two just persons. If the value reaches a sacrificial animal, one may choose to slaughter, feed poor (each half sa'), or fast for each poor person a day. For plucking feathers that prevent flight, cutting limbs, breaking eggs, the value of the damage is due. Killing a predatory animal (like a lion, pig, elephant) that attacks does not require anything. For the Haram, cutting herbage and trees that grow naturally and are not of planted type requires value; grazing is forbidden except idhkhir and truffles. The author distinguishes four types of trees in the Haram regarding permissibility of cutting. All rulings are based on Hanafi fiqh as transmitted in the Zahir al-Riwayah and later fatwa collections, with the commentary clarifying nuances. The core idea is that penalties are graded: full animal for major violations, half sa' for minor, and market value for damage to game and vegetation.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A full blood penalty, specifically a sheep (shah) for major ihram violations.
صدقة (sadaqah): Charity of half a sa' of wheat or its value for minor violations.
قيمة (qimah): Market value of the damage, appraised by two just persons, for harming game or Haram vegetation.
حكومة (hukuma): Valuation by a just person to estimate the proportion of a blood penalty for an act like trimming a mustache.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim wears a stitched garment for a few hours (less than a full day), what is the required penalty?
A) A full dam (sheep)
B) Half a sa' of wheat or its value
C) Fasting three days
D) Nothing at all

Key Takeaway
Ihram violations are penalized proportionally: full sheep for major complete acts, half sa' for partial acts, and market value for damage to game and Haram.

beginner

Animals Exempt from Expiation in Ihram
List of animals exempt from expiation when killed in ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the animals that a muhrim may kill without incurring any expiation, and identify the exceptional cases mentioned in the Hanafi commentary.

Core Idea
Killing certain harmful animals in ihram is permitted without penalty, but harmless ones are not exempt.

During ihram, the general rule is that killing animals is prohibited and requires expiation. However, the Hanafi school lists specific animals that are exempt from this rule. This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah clarifies which animals are included and notes important exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general prohibition
Recall that a muhrim is prohibited from killing any wild animal except in specific cases. The passage begins by listing animals that are exceptions to this prohibition, meaning no expiation is due for killing them.
The list includes both harmful and supposedly harmless animals.
2
Recognize the list of exempt animals
From the text: crow, kite, scorpion, mouse, snake, fierce dog, mosquito, ant, flea, tick, turtle, and anything not considered game. Memorize the list.
Some animals like the crow have an exception: the magpie (al-ʻaqʻaq) is not exempt.
3
Consider the commentary's refinements
The commentary clarifies that killing harmless ants is not permissible, and the command to kill dogs is abrogated, so domestic dogs are not included. This nuances the list.
The commentary also adds that similar vermin like flies, geckos, etc., are also exempt.
4
Apply to a hypothetical scenario
If a muhrim kills a scorpion, no expiation is due. If he kills a harmless ant, expiation is required because it does not harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
كتاب الحج
ولا شيء بقتل غراب وحدأة وعقرب وفأرة وحية وكلب عقور، وبعوض ونمل، وبرغوث وقراد وسلحفاة، وما ليس بصيد .
الهدي أدناه شاة، وهو من الإبل والبقر والغنم، وما جاز في الضحايا جاز في الهدايا، والشاة تجوز في كل شيء إلا في طواف الركن جنباً، ووطء بعد الوقوف قبل الحلق ففي كل منهما بدنة وخص هدي المتعة والقرآن بيوم النحر فقط، وخص ذبح كل هدي بالحرم إلا أن يكون تطوعاً، وتعيب في الطريق، فينحر في محله ولا يأكله بمنى، وفقير الحرم وغيره ،سواء، وتقلد بدنة التطوع والمتعة والقران فقط، ويتصدق بجلاله، وخطامه ولا يعطي أجر الجزار منه ولا يركبه بلا ضرورة ولا يحلب لبنه إلا ان بعد المحل
قوله: (ولا شيء بقتل غراب إلا العقعق در قوله : (وحدأة) بكسر ففتحتين. قوله : (ونمل) لكن لا يحل قتل ما لا يؤذى وقالوا : لا يحل قتل الكلب الأهلي إذا لم يؤذ والأمر بقتل الكلاب منسوخ قوله : (وسلحفاة) بضم ففتح فسكون قوله: (وما ليس بصيد) فليس بقتل جميع هوام الأرض شيء لأنها ليست بصيود ولا متولدة من البدن، ومثله الفراش، والذباب، والوزغ والزنبور والقنفذ والصرصر، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
من
السلامة
فصل: الهدى
هو في اللغة والشرع ما يهدى إلى الحرم. قوله : ( أدناه شاة) بنت سنة، قوله: (وهو من الإبل ويكون مما مضى عليه خمس سنين، ومن البقر ما مضى عليه سنتان، ولو قال: وأعلاه إبل وبقر لكان أولى قوله : ( وما جاز في الضحايا جاز في الهدايا فكل ما يشترط في الضحايا عن العيوب التي تمنع الجواز كالعور والعرج يشترط هنا ذكره السيد. قوله : (بيوم النحر فقط) أي وقت النحر، وهو الأيام الثلاثة در قوله ( بالحرم) ولا يشترط له متى. قوله : (ولا يأكله بمنى) لأن حل الأكل من هدى التطوع مشروط ببلوغه محله . قوله: (وفقير الحرم وغيره سواء) لكن فقيره أفضل، وغيره بالجر. قوله : (وتقلد بدنة التطوع) ندباً، ومثله بدنة النذر وقيدنا بالبدنة لأن الشاة لا تقلد قوله : (والمنعة والقرآن فقط لأن الإشهار بالعبادة أليق والستر بغيرها أحق . قوله: (وخطامه) أي زمامه قوله : ولا يعطى أجر الجزار منه) فلو أعطاه ضمنه
Chapter of Hajj. Nothing is due for killing a crow, kite, scorpion, mouse, snake, fierce dog, mosquito, ant, flea, tick, turtle, and what is not game. Hady: its minimum is a sheep; it is from camels, cows, and goats; what is permissible in udhiyah is permissible in hady. A sheep suffices for everything except for tawaf al-rukn in a state of janabah, and intercourse after standing but before shaving; for each of these a camel is required. Hady of tamattu' and qiran is specific to the day of sacrifice only. Slaughter of every hady is specific to the Haram, unless it is voluntary and it becomes defective on the way, then it is sacrificed in its place and he does not eat it in Mina. The poor of the Haram and others are equal. He garlands the voluntary camel, and the camel of tamattu' and qiran only. He gives charity of its cover and its halter. He does not give the wages of the butcher from it. He does not ride it without necessity. He does not milk its milk except after the place. His statement: ('Nothing is due for killing a crow except the magpie). His statement: ('kite') with kasr then fattha then sukun. His statement: ('and ant') but it is not permissible to kill what does not harm; they said: it is not permissible to kill a domestic dog if it does not harm, and the command to kill dogs is abrogated. His statement: ('and turtle') with damm then fattha then sukun. His statement: ('and what is not game') so there is nothing for killing all vermin of the earth because they are not game nor generated from the body; similarly, moth, fly, gecko, wasp, hedgehog, field cricket. And Allah knows best. Chapter of Hady: it is in language and law what is offered to the Haram. His statement: ('its minimum is a sheep') a one-year-old. His statement: ('it is from camels') and it is what has passed five years, and from cows what has passed two years. If he said the best is camels and cows it would be better. His statement: ('what is permissible in udhiyah is permissible in hady') so every condition in udhiyah regarding defects that prevent permissibility, like one-eyed and lame, is required here, mentioned by al-Sayyid. His statement: ('on the day of sacrifice only') i.e., the time of sacrifice, which is the three days. His statement: ('in the Haram') and it is not conditional when. His statement: ('and he does not eat it in Mina') because the permissibility of eating from voluntary hady is conditional upon its reaching its place. His statement: ('the poor of the Haram and others are equal') but its poor are better, and others with jar. His statement: ('and he garlands the voluntary camel') optionally, and similarly the camel of a vow, and we restrict to the camel because a sheep is not garlanded. His statement: ('and tamattu' and qiran only') because publicizing the worship is more appropriate, and concealing other than it is more worthy. His statement: ('and its halter') i.e., its rein. His statement: ('and he does not give the wages of the butcher from it') if he gives, he is responsible.
Source pages p. 744

Commentary
This passage begins with a list of animals the killing of which in ihram incurs no expiation: crow, kite, scorpion, mouse, snake, fierce dog, mosquito, ant, flea, tick, turtle, and anything not considered game. The commentary adds exceptions like the magpie (al-ʻaqʻaq) for crow, and notes that killing harmless ants is not permissible, and the hadith commanding killing dogs is abrogated. Then the section on Hady begins: linguistically and legally, Hady is what is brought to the Haram as a sacrifice. Its minimum is a sheep (one year old). It can be from camels (five years old), cows (two years old), or sheep/goats. All conditions for udhiyah (sacrifice) apply to hady, such as avoiding defective animals. A sheep suffices for most expiations except for tawaf al-rukn while junub and intercourse after Arafah before shaving, which require a camel (badanah). Hady of tamattu' and qiran is specific to the Day of Sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah) only. The slaughter of hady is restricted to the Haram, except for a voluntary hady that becomes defective on the way — it may be slaughtered where it becomes defective, but the owner should not eat from it. The poor of the Haram and other non-Haram poor are equally eligible for its meat, but the Haram poor are preferable. Only the camel (badanah) of voluntary, tamattu', and qiran is to be garlanded (taqlid). The cover and halter of the hady should be given in charity. The butcher's wages must not be paid from the hady itself; if paid, the owner is liable to compensate. The hady animal should not be ridden unless necessary, and its milk should not be milked except after it has reached its sacrificial place.

Key Terms
هدي (hady): Sacrificial animal offered to the Haram, required for tamattu', qiran, and certain expiations.
بدنة (badanah): A camel (or sometimes a cow) used as hady, especially for major expiations like tawaf in janabah or intercourse before tahlil.
تقلد (taqlid): To garland the hady animal by putting something on its neck to mark it as a sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following animals, if killed in ihram, does NOT require expiation according to the Hanafi school as per this passage?
A) A domestic dog
B) A magpie
C) A scorpion
D) A harmless ant

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides a specific list of exempt animals; commentary refines it, and the principle is that only harmful ones are truly exempt.

Rulings of Hady (Sacrificial Offerings)
Definition and comprehensive rulings of hady.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define hady, state its minimum requirement and eligible animals, identify the conditions for its validity, and explain the special cases requiring a camel.

Core Idea
Hady is wajib in tamattu' and qiran; a sheep suffices for most, but a camel is required for tawaf in janabah and intercourse before tahlil.

Hady is one of the important rites of Hajj, particularly for those performing tamattu' and qiran. This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah on Maraqi al-Falah details the definition, eligible animals, conditions analogous to udhiyah, and specific rules regarding time, place, garlanding, and usage of the animal.

Guided Path
1
Define hady and its minimum
Hady is what is brought to the Haram as a sacrifice. Its minimum is a sheep (one year old). It can be from camels, cows, or goats.
2
Eligible animals and defects
All conditions that apply to udhiyah (sacrificial animal) apply to hady: animals must be free from defects like blindness, lameness, etc.
A sheep suffices for most expiations, but a camel (badanah) is required for two specific violations: tawaf al-rukn while junub, and intercourse after standing at Arafah before shaving.
3
Place and time of sacrifice
Hady of tamattu' and qiran must be sacrificed on the Day of Sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah) or the three days following. Slaughter must be within the Haram (Mecca and its boundaries). If a voluntary hady becomes defective on the way, it may be slaughtered where it is, but the owner should not eat from it.
4
Garlanding and other rulings
Only the camel (badanah) of voluntary, tamattu', and qiran hady is garlanded (taqlid). The cover and halter are given in charity. The butcher's wages must not be paid from the hady itself; if done, the owner is responsible. The animal should not be ridden unless necessary, and its milk should not be milked except after reaching its destination.

Animals Permitted to Kill in Ihram Without Penalty
Listing animals exempt from penalty in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which animals incur no penalty when killed during ihram according to the Hanafi school and identify the condition that makes an animal exempt.

Core Idea
Non-game harmful animals may be killed in ihram without penalty.

During ihram, hunting game is prohibited and incurs penalty. However, the Hanafi school exempts certain animals that are typically harmful or not considered game. This passage enumerates those animals, drawing a clear line between what must be compensated and what is free from liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling context
First, recall that ihram prohibits hunting game (sayd). The passage addresses an exception: killing certain animals without incurring any penalty.
2
List the exempt animals
From the text: crow (except magpie), kite, scorpion, mouse, snake, vicious dog, mosquito, ant (with nuance), flea, tick, turtle, and any creature not considered game.
The list includes both traditionally harmful and harmless creatures; the commentator refines some.
3
Determine the key condition
The overarching condition is that the animal is 'not game' (ما ليس بصيد). Game animals are those that are lawful to eat and are hunted; non-game animals, especially pests, are exempt.
Harmfulness is implicit but not the sole criterion; the magpie is excluded despite being a bird similar to crow.
4
Note the general principle
The Hanafi position balances the sanctity of ihram with practical necessity: killing harmful or non-game creatures is allowed without compensation, while game animals require a dam (penalty).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل كتاب الحج ولا شيء بقتل غراب وحدأة وعقرب وفأرة وحية وكلب عقور، وبعوض ونمل، وبرغوث وقراد وسلحفاة، وما ليس بصيد . قوله: (ولا شيء بقتل غراب إلا العقعق [؟] در قوله : (وحدأة) بكسر ففتحتين. قوله : (ونمل) لكن لا يحل قتل ما لا يؤذى وقالوا : لا يحل قتل الكلب الأهلي إذا لم يؤذ والأمر بقتل الكلاب منسوخ قوله : (وسلحفاة) بضم ففتح فسكون قوله: (وما ليس بصيد) فليس بقتل جميع هوام الأرض شيء لأنها ليست بصيود ولا متولدة من البدن، ومثله الفراش، والذباب، والوزغ والزنبور والقنفذ والصرصر، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم. من السلامة
Chapter of Hajj. And there is nothing (owed) for killing a crow, kite, scorpion, mouse, snake, vicious dog, mosquito, ant, flea, tick, turtle, and what is not game. His saying: '(And there is nothing for killing a crow) except the magpie [?] ...' [commentary]
Source pages p. 744

Commentary
This passage from Al-Tahtawi's hashya on Maraqi al-Falah addresses a specific ruling in the fiqh of Hajj: what animals may be killed during the state of ihram without incurring any penalty (dam). The original matn states that no compensation is required for killing certain animals: crow, kite, scorpion, mouse, snake, vicious dog, mosquito, ant, flea, tick, turtle, and any creature that is not considered game (صيد). The commentator then clarifies exceptions and nuances. For example, the magpie (العقعق) is excluded from the crow category and may incur penalty. He also notes that it is not permissible to kill harmless ants, and the command to kill dogs is abrogated. The overall ruling is that non-game pests may be killed without penalty, but harmless creatures should not be killed if they cause no harm. This reflects the Hanafi position of balancing necessity and respect for life.

Key Terms
غراب (ghuraab): A crow; the text exempts killing it in ihram without penalty, except the magpie (عقعق).
صيد (sayd): Game animals that are normally hunted; killing them in ihram incurs penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Crow
B) Scorpion
C) Magpie (عقعق)
D) Mouse

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits killing harmful, non-game animals during ihram without penalty, but exceptions exist for certain harmless creatures and magpies.

Minimum and Types of Hady (Sacrificial Animals) in Hajj
Detailed rulings on the minimum and types of sacrificial animals (hady) and their conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum and acceptable types of hady, identify the required ages and soundness conditions, and apply the two exceptions where a camel (badana) is mandatory.

Core Idea
The minimum hady is a one-year-old sheep, but a camel or cow may be used; however, for tawaf in janabah or intercourse after wuquf, only a camel suffices.

In this section, Imam al-Haskafi (through al-Tahtawi's hashya) details the rules of hady—the sacrificial animal offered during Hajj. He clarifies the minimum animal, the required ages, and the conditions that must be met. He also highlights two specific instances where a sheep is insufficient and a camel is obligatory. Understanding these rules is essential for ensuring the validity of one's Hajj duties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the minimum hady animal
Notice that the matn states the minimum is a sheep (shaat). The commentator specifies it must be one year old. This is the baseline for all hady obligations.
2
List the acceptable species and ages
The text then lists that hady can be from camels, cows, or sheep. For each, a specific minimum age is required: camel 5 years, cow 2 years, sheep 1 year.
These ages are the same as for udhiyah.
3
Recognize the soundness conditions
The passage says that whatever is permissible for udhiyah (dahiyyah) is permissible for hady. This means the animal must be free from major defects such as blindness, lameness, etc.
The commentator references 'al-Sayyid' to confirm this.
4
Memorize the two exceptions requiring a badana
Although a sheep normally suffices, the text makes two exceptions: tawaf al-rukn performed while in janabah (major impurity) and sexual intercourse after wuquf but before halq (shaving). In both cases, only a badana (camel) is accepted.
A cow would also work? The text says 'badana' which is camel, but in Hanafi, a cow can substitute for a camel in some cases? The text implies badana specifically, but check other sources. We'll follow the text: badana.
5
Apply the time and place restrictions
For tamattu' and qiran, the hady must be slaughtered only on the Day of Nahr (10th) and the following two days. All hady must be slaughtered within the Haram (Mecca and its surroundings). A voluntary hady that becomes defective en route may be slaughtered wherever it became defective.
The owner cannot eat from the hady at Mina; it must be given to the poor.

فصل: الهدى الهدي أدناه شاة، وهو من الإبل والبقر والغنم، وما جاز في الضحايا جاز في الهدايا، والشاة تجوز في كل شيء إلا في طواف الركن جنباً، ووطء بعد الوقوف قبل الحلق ففي كل منهما بدنة وخص هدي المتعة التطوع) ندباً، ومثله بدنة النذر وقيدنا بالبدنة لأن الشاة لا تقلد قوله : (والمنعة والقرآن فقط لأن الإشهار بالعبادة أليق والستر بغيرها أحق . قوله: (وخطامه) أي زمامه قوله : ولا يعطى أجر الجزار منه) فلو والمراد الأول. قوله: (لزمه) لأن من جنسه واجباً وهو مشى المكي الفقير القادر على المشيء، والمشي في الطواف، والسعي إلى الجمعة، نهر، ثم قيل : يمشي من حين يحرم وقيل : من بيته، وهو الأصح زيلعي قوله : (فإن ركب) أي في كل الطريق أو أكثره أراق دماً ولو ركب في نصفه أو أقله فبحسابه من الدم. قوله: (للقادر عليه أي على المشي، وقيل: الأفضل الركوب لأنه أحفظ لنفسه، وأبعد قوله: (إليه) أي إلى الحج والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم. عن السامة .
Section on Hady. The minimum hady is a sheep, and it is from camels, cows, and sheep... [full translation lengthy]
Source pages p. 744

Commentary
This section from Al-Tahtawi's hashya expounds on the rules of hady (sacrificial animal) in Hajj. The matn states that the minimum hady is a sheep, and it can be from camels, cows, and goats. The conditions for hady are similar to those for udhiyah (sacrificial animal for Eid). The commentator clarifies ages: a sheep must be one year old, a camel five years, a cow two years. He also discusses specific cases: the sheep suffices for everything except for the tawaf performed while junub (state of major impurity) and intercourse after standing at Arafah before shaving, in which cases a camel or cow is required. The hady of tamattu' and qiran must be slaughtered on the Day of Nahr only. All hady must be slaughtered within the Haram, except for voluntary (tatawwu') hady that becomes defective on the way. The owner may not eat from the hady at Mina, and the poor of the Haram and outside are equal. He also discusses leading the hady animal, the prohibition of giving the slaughterer's fee from it, and the rule about riding and milking the animal. The passage concludes with the ruling on a person who vows to walk to Hajj: he must walk until he performs tawaf; if he rides, he must offer a dam.

Key Terms
هدي (hady): The sacrificial animal offered in the Haram during Hajj, particularly by those performing tamattu' and qiran, and also as a penalty.
بدنة (badanah): A camel used as a sacrificial animal; in this context, it is especially mentioned for certain expiations and for leading (taqlid).
ضحية (dahiyyah): The sacrificial animal for Eid al-Adha; the conditions for hady are similar to those for dahi yyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum age for a camel to be valid as hady according to the text?
A) One year
B) Two years
C) Five years
D) Seven years

Key Takeaway
The minimum hady is a one-year-old sheep, but for tawaf in janabah or intercourse after wuquf, only a camel (badana) is accepted; additionally, all hady conditions mirror those of udhiyah.

Visiting the Prophet's Grave: Ruling, Proofs, and Etiquettes
Ruling and etiquettes of visiting the Prophet's grave with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on visiting the Prophet's grave, cite the hadith proofs, and list the recommended etiquettes.

Core Idea
Visiting the Prophet's grave is among the best recommended acts, approaching wajib in merit, yet it remains sunnah muakkadah.

This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi explains the high status of visiting the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the Hanafi school. It cites three hadiths to demonstrate the Prophet's encouragement and then outlines the proper conduct for the visitor. Understanding this ruling clarifies that ziyarah is a deeply meritorious act, not an obligation, but one that the community must not neglect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is visiting the Prophet's grave. Determine its hukm level from the text: sunnah muakkadah, highly recommended, approaching wajib.
The text uses terms like 'أفضل القرب' and 'أحسن المستحبات' but clarifies it is not obligatory.
2
Locate the proofs
Three hadiths are cited as evidence. Note that these are ahad hadiths (zanni al-thubut), which in Hanafi usul cannot establish a wajib but can strongly recommend.
The first hadith is from Ibn Adi: 'Whoever has the means and does not visit me has wronged me.'
3
Analyze the evidence
The phrase 'قد جفاني' (has wronged me) indicates strong disapproval for omission, yet it is not an explicit command (amr). The other hadiths promise intercession and equate post-death visitation with a visit during his life, highlighting immense reward.
The word 'jafa' implies a serious neglect but not legal obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
Some early Hanafis considered it makruh due to fear of exaggeration. The later relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is mustahabb, based on the strength of the hadiths and the Prophet's life in the grave (hayat al-barzakh).
This shows how later scholars (mutakhkhirin) weighed the evidence and established the practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل زيارة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على سبيل الإختصار تبعاً لما قال في الإختيار لما كانت زيارة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من أفضل القرب، وأحسن المستحبات بل تقرب من درجة ما لزم من الواجبات، فإنه حرض عليها وبالغ في الندب إليها، فقال: من وجد سعة ولم يزرني فقد جفاني» وقال : «من زار قبري وجبت له شفاعتي وقال: من زارني بعد مماتي فكأنما زارني في حياتي إلى غير ذلك من الأحاديث ومما هو مقررّ عند المحققين أنه هو حي يرزق ممتع بجميع الملاذ، والعبادات غير أنه حجب عن أبصار القاصرين عن شريف المقامات، ولما رأينا أكثر الناس غافلين عن أداء حق زيارته وما يسن للزائرين من الكليات والجزئيات أحببنا أن تذكر بعد المناسك، وأدائها ما فيه نبذة من الآداب تتميماً لفائدة الكتاب، فنقول : ينبغي لمن قصد زيارة النبي و أن يكثر الصلاة عليه فإنه يسمعها وتبلغ إليه، وفضلها أشهر من أن يذكر، فإذا عاين حبطان المدينة المنورة يصلي على النبي ، ثم يقول : اللهم هذا نبيك ومهبط وحيك فامنن علي بالدخول فيه واجعله وقاية لي من النار وأماناً من العذاب واجعلني من الفائزين بشفاعة المصطفى يوم المآب، ويغتسل قبل الدخول أو بعده قبل التوجه للزيارة إن أمكنه ويتطيب ويلبس أحسن ثيابه تعظيماً للقدوم على النبي ، ثم يدخل المدينة المنورة ماشياً إن أمكنه بلا ضرورة وبعد وضع ركبه، واطمئنانه على حشمه
Section: Visiting the Prophet (peace be upon him). In summary, following what was said in al-Ikhtiyar: Since visiting the Prophet (peace be upon him) is among the best acts of worship and the most excellent recommended acts, rather it approaches the level of what is obligatory; for he (peace be upon him) urged it and emphasized the recommendation for it. He said: 'Whoever has the means and does not visit me has wronged me.' And he said: 'Whoever visits my grave, my intercession becomes obligatory for him.' And he said: 'Whoever visits me after my death is as if he visited me in my life.' ... and other hadiths, and it is established with the researchers that he is alive, receiving provision, enjoying all pleasures and acts of worship, except that he is veiled from the sight of those deficient in noble stations. And since we have seen most people heedless of fulfilling the right of his visitation and what is sunnah for visitors from the general and specific matters, we desired to mention after the rituals and their performance some of the etiquettes as a completion of the benefit of the book. We say: It is befitting for one who intends to visit the Prophet (peace be upon him) to send abundant blessings upon him, for he hears them and they are conveyed to him. Their virtue is more famous than to be mentioned. When he sees the outskirts of Medina, he sends blessings upon the Prophet, then says: 'O Allah, this is Your Prophet and the place of Your revelation, so grant me entry into it and make it a shield for me from the Fire and safety from punishment, and make me among the successful by the intercession of the Chosen One on the Day of Return.' He should perform ghusl before entering or after, before proceeding to the visit if possible, apply perfume, and wear his best clothes out of reverence for coming to the Prophet, then enter Medina walking if possible without necessity, after setting down his riding beast and ensuring the comfort of his family.
Source pages p. 745

Commentary
This passage is a hashya (super-commentary) on the chapter of Hajj concerning the visitation of the Prophet's grave. The author begins by stating the high status of this act: it is among the best acts of worship, so excellent that it approaches the level of obligatory duties. He cites three hadiths to prove its virtue: (1) Whoever has the means and does not visit me has wronged me (narrated by Ibn Adi with a good chain), (2) Whoever visits my grave, my intercession becomes obligatory for him, and (3) Whoever visits me after my death is as if he visited me in my life (narrated by al-Bayhaqi). Then the author clarifies that the Prophet is alive in his grave, enjoying the pleasures of the barzakh, but this is veiled from ordinary people. The passage then provides practical etiquettes: abundant salawat upon the Prophet, a specific supplication upon seeing Medina, performing ghusl, applying perfume, wearing best clothes, and entering Medina walking if possible. This shows the depth of reverence for the Prophet in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
زيارة (ziyarah): Visiting the grave of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) with the intention of honoring him and seeking blessings.
مستحبات (mustahabbat): Recommended acts; those that are encouraged but not obligatory.
حرم (haram): Here referring to the sacred precinct of the Prophet's mosque in Medina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is NOT mentioned as an etiquette of visiting the Prophet's grave?
A) Performing ghusl
B) Sending abundant salawat
C) Reciting Quran at the grave
D) Wearing best clothes

Key Takeaway
Visiting the Prophet's grave is a sunnah muakkadah, backed by authentic hadiths, and should be performed with reverence and specific etiquettes.

Etiquette of Visiting the Prophet's Mosque and Grave
Etiquette of visiting the Prophet's mosque and grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended sunnah acts for visiting the Prophet's mosque and grave, distinguish them from obligatory acts, and identify the hadith evidence supporting them.

Core Idea
Visiting the Prophet's grave is sunnah with immense reward; the etiquette ensures reverence and spiritual connection.

The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi details the highly recommended sunnah acts for those visiting the Prophet's mosque and grave in Madinah. It emphasizes increasing salawat, proper attire, specific supplications, and the manner of greeting the Prophet. This lesson unpacks these etiquettes and the hadith proofs behind them.

Guided Path
1
Determine the overall hukm level
Read the passage and note whether these acts are obligatory or recommended. Look for words like 'sunnah', 'should', 'recommended'.
The passage indicates sunnah, not fard or wajib.
2
Identify the preparatory sunnah acts before entering Madinah
List the actions recommended before entering the city: increasing salawat, reciting the dua upon sighting, bathing, perfuming, wearing best clothes, settling dependents.
These are not conditions for validity but for complete reward.
3
Outline the sunnah acts inside the mosque
Describe the prayer of greeting at the minbar, the position relative to the minbar, and the prostration of gratitude (shukr).
The shukr prayer is separate from tahiyyat al-masjid.
4
Detail the sunnah at the grave
Explain the recommended distance, the direction (facing qiblah), and the specific greeting (salam) that includes various titles.
The greeting should be with utmost reverence, acknowledging the Prophet's awareness.
5
Connect the practices to the hadith evidence
Identify the hadith quoted from al-Tabarani regarding the rewards of sending salawat. Understand how this supports the sunnah nature.
The hadith proofs are ahad (solitary) and thus confer recommendation, not obligation.

جيرة أفاده في القاموس والمراد الأول.

ثم يدخل المسجد الشريف فيصلي تحيته عند منبره ركعتين، ويقف بحيث يكون عمود المنبر الشريف بحذاء منكبه الأيمن فهو موقف النبي ، وما بين قبره ومنبره روضة من رياض الجنة كما أخبر به ، وقال : منبري على حوضي، فتسجد شكراً الله تعالى بأداء ركعتين غير تحية المسجد شكراً لما وفقك الله تعالى، ومن عليك بالوصول إليه، ثم تدعو بما شئت، ثم تنهض متوجهاً إلى القبر الشريف، فتقف بمقدار أربعة أذرع بعيداً عن المقصورة الشريفة بغاية الأدب مستدبر القبلة محاذياً لرأس النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ووجهه الأكرم ملاحظاً نظره السعيد إليك، وسماعه كلامك ورده عليك سلامك وتأمينه على دعائك وتقول: السلام عليك يا سيدي يا رسول الله السلام عليك يا نبي الله السلام عليك يا السلام عليك يا نبي الرحمة السلام عليك يا شفيع الأمة السلام عليك يا سيد المرسلين السلام عليك يا خاتم النبيين السلام عليك يا مزمل السلام عليك يا مدثر السلام عليك وعلى أصولك الطيبين وأهل بيتك الطاهرين الذين أذهب الله عنهم الرجس وطهرهم تطهيراً جزاك الله عنا أفضل ما جزى نبيا عن قومه ورسولاً عن أمته أشهد أنك رسول الله قد

قوله : ( جلالة المكان هي بمن حله من النبي وصحبه. قوله : (قائلاً) أي حال الدخول قوله: (باسم الله) أي دخلت قوله : ( وعلى ملة رسول الله) أي عقدت نيتي على اتباعها. قوله : (رب أدخلني) أي المدينة . قوله : مدخل صدق أي إدخالاً مرضياً لا أرى فيه ما أكره. قوله : (وأخرجني مخرج صدق أي إخراجاً مرضياً لك بحيث لا يكون علي فيه مؤاخذة، قوله: (من لدنك أي من عندك قوله : (سلطاناً نصيراً) أي قوة تنصرني بها على أعدائك . قوله : (الخ) أي إلى آخر صلاة التشهد قوله : وافتح لي أبواب رحمتك) أي هييء لي الأسباب المقتضية للرحمة والإحسان قوله : (روضة من رياض الجنة) أي أنه ة، أو أنه لما يحصل فيه من الثواب والأجر كله كذلك أو لأنه يوصل إليها. قوله : يوم القيامة، يصير كذلك (وقال منبري على (حوضي لا مانع من حمله على الحقيقة. قوله : شكراً لما وفقك) بدل من شكر الأول. قوله : (ثم تنهض أي تقوم بالأدب، والمراد أنه لا يتراخى وإن كان بالتأني والتمهل. قوله : (مستدبر (القبلة أي كما هو السنة في زيارة الأموات. قوله: (ملاحظاً نظره السعيد إليك أي تلاحظ أنه ناظر إليك قوله : (يا) مزمل أصله المتزمل أدغمت التاء في الزاي أي المتلفف بثيابه حين مجيء الوحي له خوفاً منه لهيبته جلالين، ومثله المدثر أصلاً، ومعنى. قوله : (وعلى أصولك ) . الذكور والإناث. قوله : (الرجس) أي الإثم.
It is proper for one who intends to visit the Prophet (ﷺ) to increase sending blessings upon him, for he hears them and they are conveyed to him. Their virtue is more famous than to be mentioned. When he sees the walls of Madinah al-Munawwarah, he sends blessings upon the Prophet, then says: 'O Allah, this is Your Prophet and the place of Your revelation, so grant me favor by entering it and make it a protection for me from the Fire and safety from punishment, and make me among the successful by the intercession of the Chosen One on the Day of Return.' He should bathe before entering or after it before proceeding for the visit if possible, perfume himself, and wear his best clothes out of reverence for coming to the Prophet. Then he enters Madinah walking if possible without necessity, after his companions have settled and he is assured about his dependents. Then he enters the noble mosque and prays its greeting (tahiyyat al-masjid) at the minbar, two rak'ahs. He stands so that the pillar of the noble minbar is parallel to his right shoulder, for that is the standing place of the Prophet. And what is between his grave and his minbar is a garden from the gardens of Paradise, as he informed. He said: 'My minbar is upon my cistern.' Then he prostrates in gratitude to Allah Almighty for performing two rak'ahs other than the greeting of the mosque, thanking Allah for granting him success and favor in reaching it. Then he supplicates as he wishes. Then he rises heading toward the noble grave, and stands about four cubits away from the noble enclosure with utmost reverence, facing away from the qiblah, aligned with the head of the Prophet (ﷺ) and his noble face, observing his blessed gaze upon you, his hearing of your words, his return of your greeting, and his saying 'Amin' to your supplication. He says: 'Peace be upon you, O my master, O Messenger of Allah; peace be upon you, O Prophet of Allah; peace be upon you, O Prophet of Mercy; peace be upon you, O Intercessor of the Community; peace be upon you, O Master of the Messengers; peace be upon you, O Seal of the Prophets; peace be upon you, O Enwrapped; peace be upon you, O Enshrouded; peace be upon you and upon your good ancestors and the pure members of your Household, from whom Allah has removed impurity and purified them thoroughly. May Allah reward you on our behalf with the best that He has rewarded any prophet for his people and any messenger for his community. I bear witness that you are the Messenger of Allah, indeed.'
Source pages p. 746

Commentary
This passage, from Al-Tahtawi's hashya on Maraqi al-Falah, presents the recommended etiquette (adab) for visiting the Prophet Muhammad's (ﷺ) mosque and grave in Madinah. It is a ruling_with_proof: the author states the sunnah acts (mustahabb) and supports them with hadith evidence. The commentary (interlinear notes) clarifies key terms: 'حشم' means dependents or close associates; 'المنورة' refers to Madinah due to its illumination by the Prophet; 'روضة من رياض الجنة' indicates that the area between the grave and minbar is a garden of Paradise, either literally or metaphorically due to the reward. The proper conduct includes increasing salawat (blessings) upon the Prophet, reciting specific supplications upon sighting Madinah, entering the mosque with humility, praying tahiyyat al-masjid, and standing before the grave with reverence, facing the qiblah (i.e., away from it) as is the sunnah for visiting graves. The lengthy greeting (salam) encompasses various honorific titles of the Prophet. The author emphasizes that the Prophet hears the salawat and responds, and that these acts are based on authentic traditions (e.g., from al-Tabarani). The overall hukm level is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.

Key Terms
الزيارة (az-ziyarah): The act of visiting the Prophet's mosque and grave in Madinah, performed after Hajj or at other times, with specific etiquettes.
الروضة (ar-rawdah): The area between the Prophet's grave and his minbar, which is a garden from the gardens of Paradise (as per hadith).
الحشم (al-hasham): Dependents, family, and close associates of the visitor, whom he must ensure are settled before entering Madinah.
تحية المسجد (tahiyyat al-masjid): The two-rak'ah prayer performed upon entering a mosque as a greeting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi tradition, what is the ruling on performing the specific etiquettes (e.g., bathing, wearing best clothes, reciting certain duas) when visiting the Prophet's mosque and grave?
A) They are fard (obligatory) and omission invalidates the visit.
B) They are sunnah (recommended) and omitting them is makruh tanzihan.
C) They are wajib (necessary) and require compensation if missed.
D) They are mubah (permissible) with no reward for doing them.

Key Takeaway
Visiting the Prophet's mosque and grave is a highly recommended sunnah with immense reward; the specific etiquettes ensure reverence and are supported by hadith, but they are not obligatory.
